Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Intention in Wudu: Sunnah or Fard? The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Comprehensive explanation of intention's ruling and details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in wudu, explain the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the author's response.

Core Idea
Intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard—water purifies without it, but reward depends on it.

This lesson delves into one of the most famous ikhtilafat between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the ruling of intention (niyyah) in wudu. The author of Nur al-Idah states clearly that intention is sunnah, not fard, and provides a systematic case covering definition, time, modality, and place. The central debate turns on two proofs: the absolute Quranic command to wash and the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions.' We will walk through the Hanafi argument that water is inherently purifying, and then see how the Shafi'i proof is reinterpreted to apply to reward, not validity.

Guided Path
1
Define intention and its aspects
Identify the five aspects covered: reality (linguistic and technical), time, quality (ruling), modality (how to intend), and place (heart vs. tongue). Understand that the author builds his argument around these five dimensions.
The technical definition: 'the direction of the heart towards performing the action with certainty.'
2
Locate the Hanafi ruling and its primary evidence
The author states intention is sunnah (quality). Two proofs: first, the Prophet ﷺ did not teach intention to the Bedouin despite his ignorance; second, the Quranic command (5:6) is unconditional—washing is commanded without any mention of intention, so imposing it would restrict the unrestricted.
The Quranic verse: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ...
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith 'إِنَّمَا الأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ' to argue that intention is necessary for validity. The Hanafi response: this hadith governs reward and perfection of the commanded act, not the validity of the purification itself. The author supports this by drawing an analogy: water is created as purifying, just as fire burns and food satiates, regardless of intent.
The passage specifically distinguishes between wudu with water and tayammum with earth—tayammum requires intention because earth is not inherently purifying.
4
Apply the ruling: what changes in practice?
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): a person who performs wudu without any intention is considered pure (valid wudu) in the Hanafi school, but does not earn the reward of a worshipful act. In the Shafi'i school, such wudu would be invalid and must be repeated.
This is why the Hanafi position is called a 'mercy'—ease for those who may forget or be unaware.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يسن ( النّيّةُ). والكلام عليها من وجوه، حقيقتها، ووقتها، وصفتها، وكيفيتها، ومحلها. أما حقيقتها لغة فعزم القلب على الشيء. واصطلاحاً: توجـه القـلـب نحو إيجاد الفعل جزماً. ودخل فيه كف النفس عن المنهي عنه، لأن كفها إيجاد فعل، لأنه لا تكليف إلا بفعل على الراجح، وبه يندفع قول بعضهم: إن المكلف به في النهي ليس هو الكف الذي هو الانتهاء. وبما قلناه علم أن النية معنى وراء العلم، فهي نوع إرادة، كالقصد والعزيمة، والهـم والـحـب والــود، فالكل اسم للإرادة الحادثة، لكن العزم: اسم للمتقدم على الفعل، والقصد : اسم للمقترن بالفعل
والنية: اسم للمقترن بالفعل مع دخوله تحت العلم، كالمنوي، وهذا لأن الفعل لا يوجـد بـدون الإرادة. وأما وقت النية: فعند ابتداء الوضوء حتى قبل الاستنجاء، ليكون جميع فعله قربة يثاب عليها، فبهذا يحمل قول المشايخ: إن وقتها عند غسل الوجـه علـى مـا إذا اقتصر في الوضوء على المفروض، وإلا فيفوت فضلها، خصوصاً على ما قدمناه أنه إذا ذكرها في أثناء الوضوء، فأتى بها لا يكون مقيماً لسنتها. وأما صفتها: فإنها سنة ، لأنه ، لم يعلم الأعرابي النية حين . علمه الوضوء)، مع جهله، ولو كانت فرضاً لعلمه ولقوله تعالى: ﴿يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ اللة : ٦] أمر بالغسل والمسح مطلقاً عن شرط النية، فلا يجوز تقييد المطلـق إلا بدليل. وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّمَا الأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ، وَلِكُلِّ امْرِئٍ مَا نَوَى» (۳). قلنا بموجبه لكمال المأمور به، أي: ثواب العمل بحسب النية، فالمنتفي ترتب الثواب على الفعل المجـرد عــن النية؛ لعدم كون الوضوء ونحوه قربة إذا لم ينو، وأما حصول الطهارة فلا يتوقف علـى وجـود النية، لأن الوضوء طهارة بالماء، فكان كغسل النجاسة؛ لأنه خُلِقَ مُطَهَّرَاً، فإذا أصاب الأعضاء طهرها، وإن لم يقصد كهو في الإرواء والطعام في الإشباع، والنار في الإحراق والحدث الحكمي دون النجاسة. وأما التراب فإنه غير مزيل للحدث بأصله، ولهذا لو أبصر المتيمم الماء كان محدثاً بالحدث السابق، فلم يبق في التيمم إلا معنى القصد. وذلك لا يحصل بدون النية)، فافترقا. وأما كيفيتها: فهي، أن ينوي رفع الحدث، أو ما لا . يصح إلا بالطهارة من العبادة، كإقامة الصلاة، أو استباحة الصلاة، أو ينوي الوضوء أو امتثال الأمر. وقال بعض الشراح استفيد من هذا أن نية الطهارة لا تكفي في تحصيل السنة كافة. والله أعلم؛ لأنها متنوعة إلى إزالة الحدث والخبث، فلـــم يـنــو خـصـوص الطهارة الصغرى. وأما محلها فهو القلب، لأنها من الأمور التي تتعلق به، فلا يشترط النطق بها، ولكـن المشايخ استحبوا النطق بها، ليجمع بين فعل القلب واللسان.
(And) intention is sunnah. Discussion of it is in aspects: its reality, its time, its quality, its modality, and its place. As for its reality linguistically, it is the resolve of the heart upon something. Technically: the direction of the heart towards performing the action with certainty. And it includes restraining the self from what is prohibited, because restraining is performing an action, since there is no obligation except by an action according to the preponderant view. By this, the saying of some is refuted that what is obligated in prohibitions is not the restraint that is the desisting. By what we said, it is known that intention is a meaning beyond knowledge; it is a type of will, like purpose, determination, concern, love, and affection; all are names for temporal will. But determination is the name for what precedes the action, and purpose is the name for what is concurrent with the action. And intention is the name for what is concurrent with the action while falling under knowledge, like the intended. This is because the action does not exist without will. As for the time of intention: it is at the beginning of wudu, even before istinja', so that all his action becomes an act of worship rewarded. By this is interpreted the saying of the mashayikh that its time is at washing the face, on the condition that one confines wudu to the obligatory parts, otherwise its virtue is lost, especially according to what we previously stated that if one remembers it during wudu and performs it, he does not fulfill its sunnah. As for its quality: it is sunnah, because the Prophet did not teach the Bedouin intention when he taught him wudu, despite his ignorance; if it were obligatory, he would have taught him. And due to His saying: 'O you who believe, when you rise for prayer, wash your faces and your hands...' He commanded washing and wiping absolutely without the condition of intention, so it is not permissible to restrict the unrestricted except with evidence. And his saying, peace be upon him: 'Actions are but by intentions, and for each person is what he intended.' We respond to its purport for the perfection of the commanded, i.e., the reward of an action is according to intention. So what is negated is the reward attached to the action devoid of intention, because wudu and the like are not acts of worship if one does not intend. As for the attainment of purity, it does not depend on the existence of intention, because wudu is purification by water, so it is like washing impurity; because water is created as purifying, so when it reaches the limbs, it purifies them, even if one does not intend, just like water irrigates and food satiates and fire burns. This applies to ritual impurity (hadath hukmi), not to physical impurity. As for earth (tayammum), it does not remove hadath in its essence; hence if the mutayammim sees water, he remains in the previous hadath. So nothing remains in tayammum except the meaning of intention, and that is not attained without intention. So they differ. As for its modality: it is that he intends removal of hadath, or something that is not valid except with purity from worship, like performing prayer, or making prayer permissible, or he intends wudu or compliance with the command. And some commentators said that this indicates that the intention of purity is not sufficient for fulfilling all the sunnah. And Allah knows best, because it is diverse into removal of hadath and impurity, so he did not intend specifically the minor purity. As for its place: it is the heart, because it is among matters related to it; so verbal utterance is not required, but the mashayikh recommended uttering it to combine the action of the heart and tongue.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the ruling of intention (niyyah) in wudu. The author states that intention is sunnah, not fard, and then covers five aspects: reality, time, quality, modality, and place. The reality is defined as the heart's resolution to perform an action. The time is at the start of wudu; if one only intends at washing the face, the sunnah is not fully observed. The quality is that it is sunnah, proven by the fact that the Prophet did not teach the Bedouin intention when he taught him wudu. The author also refutes the view that intention is fard by citing the Quranic verse which commands washing unconditionally, and by interpreting the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions' as applying to reward, not validity. A key argument is that water is inherently purifying, so wudu is valid without intention, unlike tayammum which requires intention. The modality involves intending either removal of hadath or permission for prayer. The place is the heart; verbalization is recommended but not required. The passage also addresses a subtle point about the sufficiency of general intention for all sunnah acts.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The heart's resolution to perform an action; in wudu, it is the intention to remove ritual impurity or to make prayer permissible.
الحدث الحكمي (al-hadath al-hukmi): Ritual impurity that is legally considered impure, as opposed to physical impurity (najasa).
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry purification with earth when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a person performs wudu without intention?
A) The wudu is invalid.
B) The wudu is valid but no reward is earned.
C) The person must repeat the wudu.
D) The wudu is still rewarded.

Key Takeaway
Intention in wudu is sunnah, not fard—water purifies without it, but reward depends on intention.

Order (Tartib) in Wudu: Sunnah Mu'akkadah, Not Fard
Evidence that order in wudu is a confirmed sunnah, not obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers order in wudu as sunnah mu'akkadah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The particle 'waw' indicates conjunction, not sequence; thus order in wudu is sunnah, not fard.

This passage addresses a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: is it obligatory to wash the limbs in order during wudu? The Hanafi school holds that order is a confirmed sunnah, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it fard. The dispute hinges on the linguistic analysis of the Quranic verse (Al-Ma'idah 5:6). The author explains that the word 'waw' (and) in the verse denotes mere conjunction, not sequential order, and that the Prophet's practice confirms it as sunnah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: order in wudu is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard. The one who leaves it is blameworthy (musi') but the wudu remains valid.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that order is fard; wudu without order is invalid.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof: linguistic analysis of 'waw'
The Quranic verse uses 'waw' (and) which, in Hanafi usul, indicates absolute conjunction (majmu') without implying sequence. Therefore, the verse does not mandate order.
The particle 'fa' (then) in the verse is interpreted as succession of the limbs, not mandatory order.
4
Follow the opposing proof
Shafi'is rely on the use of 'fa' (then) and the Prophet's consistent practice of performing wudu in order, which they consider as evidence of obligation.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response and determine the practical difference
The Hanafi response clarifies that 'fa' refers to the sequence of mentioning limbs, not a required order. The Prophet's practice shows it is a sunnah, not fard. The practical consequence: Hanafis consider wudu without order valid but blameworthy; Shafi'is consider it invalid.
Tamarah al-khilaf: validity of wudu when order is omitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن مؤكداً في الصحيح (الترتيب) في الوضوء، كما نَصَّ اللهُ تَعَالى في كِتَابِهِ) (*)، فيكون مسيئاً بتركه، ولم يكن الترتيب فرضاً، لأن الواو في الآية لمطلق الجمع، فلا يفيد الترتيب، والفاء لتعقيب جملة الأعضاء؛ لأن : (1) (۱) لقوله : « إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ وَإِنَّمَا لِكُلِّ امْرِئٍ مَا نَوَى، أخرجه البخاري في بدء الوحي (۱). (۲) تقدم تخريجه ص (۷۱). (۳) تقدم تخريجه بالتعليق رقم (۱). (٤) لأن التراب ملوث فلا يصير مطهراً إلا بالنية. أفاده المؤلف في المراقي. (۵) تنبيه : الآية خالية عن الدلالة على ذلك الترتيب، وإنما جاء التنصيص من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام. ط. (٦) في قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاغْسِلُوا [ المائدة: ٦ ].
(And) it is a confirmed sunnah in the correct view (order) in wudu, as Allah the Exalted stated in His Book, so one is blameworthy for leaving it, and order is not obligatory, because the waw in the verse is for absolute conjunction, so it does not indicate order, and fa is for the succession of the limbs; because: (1) (1) for his saying: 'Actions are but by intentions...' ..., (2) its takhrij preceded on p.71, (3) its takhrij preceded in comment no.1, (4) because earth is impure so it does not become purifying except with intention. The author stated in al-Maraqi. (5) Note: The verse does not indicate that order; rather the specification came from his action, peace be upon him. (6) In the verse: 'So wash your faces and your hands...'
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of order (tartib) in wudu. The author states that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not fard. The reason is that the Quranic verse uses the particle 'waw' (and) which indicates mere conjunction, not sequence. The particle 'fa' (then) in the verse refers to the succession of the limbs but does not impose a mandatory order. The author notes that a person who leaves order is blameworthy (musi') but the wudu remains valid. The footnotes provide additional references and clarifications, including that the specification of order comes from the Prophet's action, not the Quran.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): The sequential order of washing the limbs in wudu: face, then hands, then wiping head, then feet.
الواو (al-waw): The Arabic letter 'waw' meaning 'and', which in Hanafi usul indicates mere conjunction, not sequence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider order (tartib) in wudu as sunnah mu'akkadah and not fard?
A) Because the Prophet never did it in order.
B) Because the particle 'waw' in the Quran does not imply sequence.
C) Because it is mentioned in the Quran as optional.
D) Because the Sahaba disagreed.

Key Takeaway
Order in wudu is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) because the Quranic particle 'waw' does not indicate sequence; leaving it is blameworthy but the wudu remains valid.

The Ruling of Intention (Niyyah) in Wudu: Sunnah, Not Fard
Explains the ruling of niyyah as sunnah in wudu, with proof and details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on niyyah in wudu as sunnah, explain the proof from the Prophet's teaching and the Quran, and identify the time and modality of intention.

Core Idea
Intention in wudu is sunnah — the Prophet didn't teach it to the Bedouin, so it cannot be fard.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies a fundamental Hanafi position: intention (niyyah) is sunnah mu'akkadah in wudu, not fard. The author defines niyyah, discusses its time, ruling, and proof, and distinguishes it from the Shafi'i view. The lesson will walk through the legal reasoning, including the dalil from the Prophet's teaching of wudu to a Bedouin and the absolute command in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Define Niyyah and Its Time
Identify the legal definition of niyyah and when it should be made — at the start of wudu, even before istinja, to include all actions as worship.
The mashayikh's statement about washing the face refers to a limited case.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard. This is based on the Prophet not teaching it to the Bedouin and the absolute Quranic command.
3
Analyze the Dalil
The hadith 'Actions are by intentions' is interpreted to affect reward, not validity. Similarly, Quran 5:6 commands washing without mentioning intention, so it cannot be added without evidence.
This is the wajh al-dalalah.
4
Understand the Modality
One must intend either removal of hadath, permission of prayer, or similar. The intention is in the heart, but utterance is recommended.
5
Differentiate from Tayammum
Tayammum requires intention because earth does not remove hadath inherently, unlike water.
This reinforces that water purifies regardless of intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنية: اسم للمقترن بالفعل مع دخوله تحت العلم، كالمنوي، وهذا لأن الفعل لا يوجـد بـدون الإرادة. وأما وقت النية: فعند ابتداء الوضوء حتى قبل الاستنجاء، ليكون جميع فعله قربة يثاب عليها، فبهذا يحمل قول المشايخ: إن وقتها عند غسل الوجـه علـى مـا إذا اقتصر في الوضوء على المفروض، وإلا فيفوت فضلها، خصوصاً على ما قدمناه أنه إذا ذكرها في أثناء الوضوء، فأتى بها لا يكون مقيماً لسنتها. وأما صفتها: فإنها سنة ، لأنه ، لم يعلم الأعرابي النية حين . علمه الوضوء)، مع جهله، ولو كانت فرضاً لعلمه ولقوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ وَأَيْدِيَكُمْ﴾ [المائدة: ٦] أمر بالغسل والمسح مطلقاً عن شرط النية، فلا يجوز تقييد المطلـق إلا بدليل. وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : « إِنَّمَا الأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ، وَلِكُلِّ امْرِئٍ مَا نَوَى ». قلنا بموجبه لكمال المأمور به، أي: ثواب العمل بحسب النية، فالمنتفي ترتب الثواب على الفعل المجـرد عــن النية؛ لعدم كون الوضوء ونحوه قربة إذا لم ينو، وأما حصول الطهارة فلا يتوقف علـى وجـود النية، لأن الوضوء طهارة بالماء، فكان كغسل النجاسة؛ لأنه خُلِقَ مُطَهَّرَاً، فإذا أصاب الأعضاء طهرها، وإن لم يقصد كهو في الإرواء والطعام في الإشباع، والنار في الإحراق والحدث الحكمي دون النجاسة. وأما التراب فإنه غير مزيل للحدث بأصله، ولهذا لو أبصر المتيمم الماء كان محدثاً بالحدث السابق، فلم يبق في التيمم إلا معنى القصد. وذلك لا يحصل بدون النية)، فافترقا. وأما كيفيتها: فهي، أن ينوي رفع الحدث، أو ما لا . يصح إلا بالطهارة من العبادة، كإقامة الصلاة، أو استباحة الصلاة، أو ينوي الوضوء أو امتثال الأمر. وقال بعض الشراح استفيد من هذا أن نية الطهارة لا تكفي في تحصيل السنة كافة. والله أعلم؛ لأنها متنوعة إلى إزالة الحدث والخبث، فلـــم يـنــو خـصـوص الطهارة الصغرى. وأما محلها فهو القلب، لأنها من الأمور التي تتعلق به، فلا يشترط النطق بها، ولكـن المشايخ استحبوا النطق بها، ليجمع بين فعل القلب واللسان.
And intention: it is a term for that which is connected to the action while it enters under knowledge, like the intended thing. This is because the action does not exist without will. As for the time of intention: it is at the beginning of wudu even before istinja, so that all of his action becomes an act of worship for which he is rewarded. Thus is understood the saying of the mashayikh: its time is at washing the face, based on when one limits wudu to the obligatory parts; otherwise its virtue is lost, especially according to what we have presented: that if he remembers it during wudu and performs it, he is not fulfilling its sunnah. As for its ruling: it is sunnah, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not teach the Bedouin intention when he taught him wudu, despite his ignorance, and if it were obligatory he would have taught him, and due to His saying: 'O you who believe, when you rise to prayer, wash your faces and your hands' – He commanded washing and wiping absolutely without the condition of intention, so it is not permissible to restrict the absolute except with evidence. And his saying (peace be upon him): 'Actions are but by intentions, and every man has what he intended.' We accept it as meaning the perfection of the commanded act, i.e., the reward of an action is according to intention; hence, what is negated is the reward resulting from the mere action without intention, due to the failure of wudu and the like to be an act of worship if one does not intend. As for attaining purification, it does not depend on the existence of intention, because wudu is purification with water, so it is like washing off impurity; because water was created as a purifier, so when it hits the limbs it purifies them even if not intended, just like water in quenching thirst, food in satiation, fire in burning, and the ruling state of impurity (hadath) – not impurity (najasa). As for earth (tayammum), it does not remove hadath by its essence, and hence if the one performing tayammum sees water, he remains in the previous hadath, so only the meaning of intent remains in tayammum. And that is not obtained without intention, so the two differ. As for its modality: it is that he intends removal of hadath, or something that is only valid with purification from worship, like performing prayer, or making prayer permissible, or intends wudu or obeying the command. Some commentators said: it is understood from this that intending purification (general) is not sufficient to achieve the complete sunnah. And Allah knows best; because purification is of various types – removing hadath and removing najasa – and he did not intend the specific minor purification. As for its locus, it is the heart, because it is among matters that pertain to it. Hence verbal utterance is not required, but the mashayikh recommended uttering it to combine the action of the heart and tongue.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the intention (niyyah) in wudu. The author begins by defining niyyah as the connection of the action with the knowledge of the intended act, since action is impossible without will. He then discusses the time: it should be at the start of wudu, even before istinja, so that all actions are acts of worship rewarded. The mashayikh's statement that its time is at washing the face is interpreted as applying when one only perfoms the obligatory parts; otherwise the virtue of early niyyah is lost. Next, he states the ruling: niyyah is sunnah, not fard. The proof is that the Prophet taught wudu to a Bedouin without mentioning intention – if it were obligatory, he would have taught it. Additionally, the Quranic verse commanding washing and wiping is absolute, without the condition of intention, and an absolute cannot be restricted without evidence. The hadith 'Actions are by intentions' is interpreted to mean that reward depends on intention, not that the act itself is invalid without it; purification is achieved by water regardless of intent, like water removes impurity even if not intended. Tayammum differs because it requires intent as it does not remove hadath by itself. The modality: one must intend either removal of hadath, permission of prayer, performance of wudu, or obedience. Niyyah in the heart is sufficient, but utterance is recommended.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The intention connected to the action, occurring at the start, that distinguishes acts of worship from habits.
الوضوء (al-wudu): Ritual washing of the limbs with water to remove minor impurity (hadath).
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that prevents prayer, removed by wudu or ghusl.
الاستنجاء (al-istinja): Washing the private parts after relieving oneself, part of wudu preparation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling of niyyah (intention) in wudu?
A) Fard (obligatory)
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mustahabb (recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention in wudu is sunnah for reward, not fard for validity; the primary proof is that the Prophet did not teach it to the Bedouin.

The Sunnah of Tartib (Order) in Wudu
Ruling with proof: legal derivation of tartib's status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tartib, explain the linguistic proof from the Quranic verse, and distinguish it from fard.

Core Idea
Tartib is sunnah mu'akkadah in Wudu, not fard, because the waw in the verse indicates mere conjunction.

The Hanafi school holds that performing the acts of wudu in order (face, hands, head, feet) is a highly recommended sunnah, not an obligation. This lesson unpacks the linguistic reasoning that distinguishes the Hanafi position from other schools, focusing on the interpretation of the conjunction 'waw' in the Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Tartib
State that tartib is sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard, and that leaving it is makruh but wudu remains valid.
The text says 'يسن مؤكداً في الصحيح' – confirmed sunnah.
2
Locate the Quranic Proof and the Linguistic Point
The author cites the verse of wudu and argues that the waw (and) indicates pure conjunction, not order. The fa (then) connects the group of limbs but does not impose sequence.
Compare with the Shafi'i view that waw sometimes indicates order.
3
Analyze the 'Bread and Meat' Analogy
The example 'enter the market and buy bread and meat' shows that the command is to do both actions in succession after entering, not in a fixed order.
This analogy clarifies that the fa does not require sequencing among the items.
4
Conclude the Hanafi Position
Tartib is a recommended sunnah because the dalil (Quran) does not impose obligation, and the Prophet's constant practice confirms it as sunnah.
This aligns with the general principle that a command (amr) indicates obligation unless diverted by evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يسن مؤكداً في الصحيح (الترتيب) في الوضوء، كما نَصَّ اللهُ تَعَالى في كِتَابِهِ، فيكون مسيئاً بتركه، ولم يكن الترتيب فرضاً، لأن الواو في الآية لمطلق الجمع، فلا يفيد الترتيب، والفاء لتعقيب جملة الأعضاء؛ لأن المعقب طلب الفعل، وله متعلقات وصل إلى أولها ذكراً بنفسه، والباقي بواسطة الحرف المشترك، فاشتركت كلها فيه من غير إفادة طلب تقديم تعليق بعضها على بعض في الوجود، فصار مؤدى الترتيب طلب إعقاب غسل جملة الأعضاء، وهو نظير قولك: ادخل السوق فاشتر لنا خبزاً ولحماً، حيث كان المفاد إعقاب الدخول لشراء ما ذكر كيف ما وقع (و) يسن (البداءة بالميامن)، جمع ميمنة، خلاف الميسرة، وذكر في «المغرب» أن البداية، بالياء، عامية، والصواب بدأة. أي: البداءة باليمين في غسل اليدين والرجلين سنة، لا في باقي الأعضاء لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « إِذَا تَوَضَّأْتُمْ فَابْدَؤُوا بِمَيَامِنِكُمْ ). ولأنه : ( كَانَ يُحِبُّ التَّيَامُنَ في كلِّ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى فِي طُهُورِهِ وَتَنَعْلِهِ وَتَرَجُلِهِ وَشَأْنِهِ كلَّه). والتنعل : لبس النعلين، والترجل: تسريحا الشعر. ولأن من حكى وضوءه ، صرحوا بتقديم اليمني على اليسرى من اليدين والرجلين، وذلك يفيد المواظبة، لأنهم إنما يحكون وضوءه، الذي هو دأبه وعادته، فيكون سنة، وبمثله ثبتت سنية استيعاب الرأس، لأنهم كذلك حكوا المسح، ولم يكن الأمر مقتضياً وجوب تقديم اليمين، لأنه مصروف عن مقتضاه بالإجماع على استحباب ذلك. قال « ابن قدامة» في « المغني : التيامن مستحب، ولا نعلم قائلاً بخلاف ذلك، ولأنه لا يعقل فيه الأشرف اليمين، وذلك لا يقتضي عدمه العقاب، (وَ) البداءة بالغسل من (رؤوس الأصابع) في اليدين والرجلين؛ لأن الله تعالى جعل المرافق والكعبين غاية الغسل، فتكون منتهى الفعل. لأنه كان يفعل هكذا. (و) البداءة في المسح من مُقدَّمِ الرّأسِ) لأنه « بَدَا مِنْ مُقَدَّمِ رَأْسِهِ ثُمَّ ذَهَبَ إِلَى قفَاهُ . (و) يسن (مسحُ الرَّقَبَةِ)؛ لأنه ( توضأ وأوْمَا بِيَدَيهِ من مقدّم رأسه حتى بلَغَ بِهما أسفل عنقهِ مِنْ قِبَلِ قَفَاهُ ). ( لا ) يسن مسح (الحلقوم) وهو بدعة. (وقيل: إنَّ الأربعة الأخيرة) التي أولها البداءة بالميامن (مُستحبَّةٌ). وكان وجهه عدم ثبوت المواظبة، وليس مسلماً.
And (it is sunnah, confirmed in the correct view) order (tartib) in wudu, as Allah the Exalted has stated in His Book. So one becomes blameworthy by leaving it, and order is not obligatory because the waw in the verse indicates mere conjunction, not sequence, and the fa is for connecting the group of limbs; because the connector requests the action, and it has attachments that reach the first by itself and the rest by means of the shared letter, so they all share in it without indicating a request for precedence of some over others in existence. Thus the meaning of tartib is the request for successive washing of the group of limbs, similar to saying: enter the market and buy for us bread and meat, where the meaning is the succession of entry to buy what is mentioned, however it occurs. And (it is sunnah) beginning with the right side (al-mayamin), plural of maymana, as opposed to the left. It is mentioned in al-Mughrib that al-bidayah with ya is colloquial; the correct is bad'ah i.e., beginning with the right in washing the hands and feet is sunnah, not in the remaining limbs, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides.' And because he (peace be upon him) loved the right side in everything, even in his purification, wearing sandals, combing hair, and all his affairs. And because those who narrated his wudu explicitly stated the precedence of the right over the left in hands and feet, and that implies consistent practice because they only narrate his wudu which was his habit and custom, so it becomes sunnah. Similarly, the sunnah of encompassing the head is established because they narrated wiping (in such a way). And the command did not necessitate obligation of giving precedence to the right because it is diverted from its literal meaning by consensus that it is recommended. Ibn Qudamah said in al-Mughni: 'Tayammun (using the right) is recommended, and we do not know anyone holding otherwise, because it is not rationally understood that the right is more honorable, and that does not necessitate punishment for leaving it.' And (it is sunnah) beginning washing from the tips of the fingers in the hands and feet because Allah made the elbows and ankles the limit of washing, so it becomes the end of the action. Because he (peace be upon him) used to do so. And (it is sunnah) beginning wiping from the front of the head because he (peace be upon him) began from the front of his head then went to his nape. And (it is sunnah) wiping the neck because he performed wudu and pointed with his hands from the front of his head until he reached the bottom of his neck from the back of his nape. Not wiping the throat (al-halqum) is sunnah, and it is innovation. And it is said that the last four (which begin with starting with the right) are recommended (mustahabbah). Its reasoning is the lack of proven constancy, but it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the sunnah acts of wudu. The first ruling is on tartib (order): it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and one is blameworthy for leaving it, but not sinful in the sense of invalidity. The author explains why the Quranic verse does not impose order—the waw (and) indicates mere conjunction, not sequence. The example of 'enter the market and buy bread and meat' shows that order is not intended, only succession of actions. Then he discusses beginning with the right side (al-mayamin): sunnah for hands and feet, supported by hadith and the Prophet's practice. The command is not obligatory; consensus makes it recommended. Next, beginning from the fingertips in washing: because the limit is the elbows/ankles, so starting from the opposite end is logical and based on the Prophet's practice. Wiping from the front of the head is sunnah, following the hadith that he began from the front and went to the nape. Wiping the neck is also sunnah, based on a specific hadith, but not the throat (halqum), which is innovation. Finally, there is a difference of opinion: some say the last four (right side, fingertips, front of head, neck) are merely mustahabb (recommended) rather than sunnah mu'akkadah, due to lack of proven constancy, but the author rejects this view.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Performing the acts of wudu in the order mentioned in the Quran: face, hands, head, feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person washes his hands before his face in wudu?
A) Wudu is invalid because order is fard.
B) Wudu is valid but makruh, and the person is blameworthy.
C) Wudu is valid and no blame because order is only mustahabb.
D) Wudu is invalid unless he repeats the entire wudu.

Key Takeaway
Tartib is a confirmed sunnah, not a fard, due to the linguistic structure of the Quranic verse and the Prophet's practice.

Beginning with the Right Side and Remaining Sunnah Acts of Wudu
Ruling with proof for multiple sunnah acts and a note on ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of wudu beyond tartib, state their proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on the last four.

Core Idea
Beginning with the right side, from fingertips, front of head, and wiping the neck are sunnah acts; wiping the throat is bid'ah.

Beyond order, the Hanafi school specifies several other sunnah acts in wudu: starting with the right hand and foot, washing from the fingertips, wiping from the front of the head, and wiping the neck. Each is supported by authentic hadith. This lesson also addresses a difference of opinion among Hanafis whether the last four are sunnah mu'akkadah or merely mustahabb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Beginning with the Right
State that it is sunnah mu'akkadah to begin washing the right hand and right foot before the left, based on the hadith and the Prophet's practice.
The text specifies this applies only to hands and feet, not to face or head.
2
Analyze the Proofs for Right Side
The author cites the hadith 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides' and the general love of the Prophet for using the right. The command is diverted to recommendation by consensus.
Consensus among scholars that starting with right is sunnah, not fard.
3
Examine the Remaining Sunnah Acts
List: beginning washing from fingertips (due to the limit being elbows/ankles), beginning wiping from front of head (based on hadith), wiping the neck (based on hadith), and not wiping the throat (bid'ah).
Each has specific evidence from the Prophet's practice.
4
Address the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Some later Hanafis consider the last four acts (right side, fingertips, front of head, neck) as merely mustahabb, not sunnah mu'akkadah, due to lack of proven constant practice. The author rejects this, affirming sunnah mu'akkadah.
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that they are sunnah mu'akkadah.

And (it is sunnah, confirmed in the correct view) order (tartib) in wudu, as Allah the Exalted has stated in His Book. So one becomes blameworthy by leaving it, and order is not obligatory because the waw in the verse indicates mere conjunction, not sequence, and the fa is for connecting the group of limbs; because the connector requests the action, and it has attachments that reach the first by itself and the rest by means of the shared letter, so they all share in it without indicating a request for precedence of some over others in existence. Thus the meaning of tartib is the request for successive washing of the group of limbs, similar to saying: enter the market and buy for us bread and meat, where the meaning is the succession of entry to buy what is mentioned, however it occurs. And (it is sunnah) beginning with the right side (al-mayamin), plural of maymana, as opposed to the left. It is mentioned in al-Mughrib that al-bidayah with ya is colloquial; the correct is bad'ah i.e., beginning with the right in washing the hands and feet is sunnah, not in the remaining limbs, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When you perform wudu, begin with your right sides.' And because he (peace be upon him) loved the right side in everything, even in his purification, wearing sandals, combing hair, and all his affairs. And because those who narrated his wudu explicitly stated the precedence of the right over the left in hands and feet, and that implies consistent practice because they only narrate his wudu which was his habit and custom, so it becomes sunnah. Similarly, the sunnah of encompassing the head is established because they narrated wiping (in such a way). And the command did not necessitate obligation of giving precedence to the right because it is diverted from its literal meaning by consensus that it is recommended. Ibn Qudamah said in al-Mughni: 'Tayammun (using the right) is recommended, and we do not know anyone holding otherwise, because it is not rationally understood that the right is more honorable, and that does not necessitate punishment for leaving it.' Because he (peace be upon him) used to do so. And (it is sunnah) beginning wiping from the front of the head because he (peace be upon him) began from the front of his head then went to his nape. And (it is sunnah) wiping the neck because he performed wudu and pointed with his hands from the front of his head until he reached the bottom of his neck from the back of his nape. Not wiping the throat (al-halqum) is sunnah, and it is innovation. And it is said that the last four (which begin with starting with the right) are recommended (mustahabbah). Its reasoning is the lack of proven constancy, but it is not accepted.

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the sunnah acts of wudu. The first ruling is on tartib (order): it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and one is blameworthy for leaving it, but not sinful in the sense of invalidity. The author explains why the Quranic verse does not impose order—the waw (and) indicates mere conjunction, not sequence. The example of 'enter the market and buy bread and meat' shows that order is not intended, only succession of actions. Then he discusses beginning with the right side (al-mayamin): sunnah for hands and feet, supported by hadith and the Prophet's practice. The command is not obligatory; consensus makes it recommended. Next, beginning from the fingertips in washing: because the limit is the elbows/ankles, so starting from the opposite end is logical and based on the Prophet's practice. Wiping from the front of the head is sunnah, following the hadith that he began from the front and went to the nape. Wiping the neck is also sunnah, based on a specific hadith, but not the throat (halqum), which is innovation. Finally, there is a difference of opinion: some say the last four (right side, fingertips, front of head, neck) are merely mustahabb (recommended) rather than sunnah mu'akkadah, due to lack of proven constancy, but the author rejects this view.

Key Terms
الميامن (al-mayamin): The right side, specifically beginning with the right hand and right foot in washing during wudu.
الحلقوم (al-halqum): The throat (specifically the windpipe area), which is not to be wiped during wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is considered an innovation (bid'ah) in wudu according to this passage?
A) Wiping the neck
B) Wiping the throat
C) Starting with the right
D) Washing from the fingertips

Key Takeaway
Beginning with the right side, washing from fingertips, wiping from the front of the head, and wiping the neck are all sunnah mu'akkadah; wiping the throat is bid'ah.

Taharah — Purification

Sunan of Wudu: Right Side, Fingertips, Front of Head, and Wiping the Neck
Detailed ruling and proof for sunan acts in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan acts of wudu mentioned in the text and explain why they are considered sunnah and not wajib.

Core Idea
Starting with the right and other sunan in wudu are established by the Prophet's practice, but consensus makes them recommended, not obligatory.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah lists four specific acts that are recommended during wudu: starting with the right side, washing from the fingertips, wiping from the front of the head, and wiping the neck. He provides hadith evidence and explains why these are sunnah (recommended) rather than wajib (obligatory), addressing a potential misunderstanding. By the end, you will be able to identify these sunan and understand the legal reasoning behind their classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunan acts
Read the passage and list the four acts described as sunnah. Note that the larynx (Adam's apple) is explicitly excluded as an innovation.
The acts are: starting with right side (in hands and feet), starting from fingertips, starting from front of head, and wiping the neck.
2
Locate the primary proof for each
For each sunnah, find the hadith or practice (fi'l) cited in the text. For starting with right: hadith 'When you perform wudu, start with your right sides'. For starting from front of head: 'He started from the front of his head then went back'. For neck wiping: 'He gestured from front to bottom of neck'.
The text also cites the Prophet's general love for using the right side.
3
Analyze why they are sunnah not wajib
The author argues that the command 'start with your right sides' is an imperative, but its apparent meaning (obligation) is overridden by consensus (ijma’) that it is recommended. Also, the Prophet's consistent practice (muwazabah) makes it sunnah, not wajib.
This is a key usul al-fiqh point: commands can be diverted from obligation by evidence.
4
Note the exception: larynx is bid'ah
The text explicitly says wiping the larynx (the throat area) is not sunnah but an innovation (bid'ah). Recognize that not every related act is recommended.
This shows the precision of the Hanafi school in avoiding innovations in worship.
5
Consider the alternative view (mustahabb)
The text mentions that some say these last four sunan are merely mustahabb (recommended) rather than sunnah. The author rejects this, asserting that the constancy of the Prophet's practice (muwazabah) elevates them to sunnah.
This is an intra-Hanafi discussion; the relied-upon view is sunnah.

(و) البداءة في المسح من مُقدَّمِ الرّأسِ) لأنه « بَدَا مِنْ مُقَدَّمِ رَأْسِهِ ثُمَّ ذَهَبَ إِلَى قفَاهُ . (وقيل: إنَّ الأربعة الأخيرة) التي أولها البداءة بالميامن (مُستحبَّةٌ). وكان وجهه عدم ثبوت المواظبة، وليس مسلماً.
And starting with the right sides, and the tips of the fingers, and the front of the head, and wiping the neck, not the larynx. And it is said that the last four are recommended. The sequential order demands the action, and it has connections. It is sunnah to start with the right sides, i.e., the right in washing hands and feet, not in other limbs, due to his saying: 'When you perform wudu, start with your right sides.' And because he loved using the right side in everything, even in his purification, wearing sandals, combing hair, and all his affairs. And because those who narrated his wudu stated that he gave precedence to the right over the left in hands and feet, and this indicates constancy, so it is sunnah. Similarly, the sunnah of covering the head is established. The command does not necessitate obligation because it is diverted from its apparent meaning by consensus on its recommendation. Ibn Qudamah said in al-Mughni: 'Using the right side is recommended, and we do not know anyone who says otherwise.' And because the right side is not inherently superior in a way that would entail punishment for omission. And starting washing from the tips of the fingers in hands and feet because Allah made the elbows and heels the limit, so they are the end of the action. And starting wiping from the front of the head because he started from the front of his head then went to his nape. And it is sunnah to wipe the neck because he performed wudu and gestured with his hands from the front of his head until he reached the bottom of his neck from the side of his nape. It is not sunnah to wipe the larynx; that is an innovation. And it is said that the last four, starting with the right sides, are recommended. The reason is lack of constancy, but it is not accepted.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu, specifically four actions: starting with the right side when washing hands and feet, starting from the fingertips when washing, starting from the front of the head when wiping, and wiping the neck. The author uses textual evidence from the Prophet's hadiths and his practice (fi'l) to establish these as sunnah. Importantly, the author addresses a potential misconception: some might think the command to start with the right implies obligation, but the author clarifies that it is diverted to recommendation by consensus (ijma'). The Hanafi position is that these are sunnah, not wajib. There is a discussion that some scholars consider these 'mustahabb' (recommended) rather than sunnah, but the author leans towards sunnah. The larynx (Adam's apple) is specifically excluded; wiping it is considered an innovation (bid'ah).

Key Terms
ميامن (mayamin): Right sides of the body; plural of maimana.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed; omission is not sinful but disliked.
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act; doing it brings reward, leaving it is not blameworthy.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religion; here, wiping the larynx is considered a bid'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is starting with the right side in wudu considered sunnah and not wajib?
A) Because the hadith is weak
B) Because the command is diverted from obligation by consensus on its recommendation
C) Because it is only for hands and feet
D) Because the left side is also acceptable

Key Takeaway
The four sunan (starting with right, fingertips, front of head, wiping neck) are recommended but not obligatory, established by the Prophet's practice and hadith, with the exception of wiping the larynx, which is an innovation.

The Fourteen Etiquettes (Adab) of Wudu
Enumerates and explains the recommended etiquettes of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between adab and sunnah in Hanafi fiqh and list the recommended etiquettes of wudu.

Core Idea
Adab are recommended acts that the Prophet did occasionally; they are rewarded but not blameworthy if omitted.

This lesson unpacks the definition and list of adab (etiquettes) of wudu as explained in the Hanafi tradition. The text first clarifies the technical meaning of adab versus sunnah, then enumerates fourteen recommended practices. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly classifying acts in worship and knowing their reward and blame.

Guided Path
1
Define adab according to Sharh al-Hidayah
Identify the definition given in the text: an act the Prophet performed once or twice without continuous practice. Contrast with acts he consistently performed (sunnah).
The text provides multiple definitions but adopts the one from Sharh al-Hidayah.
2
Distinguish the ruling of adab from sunnah
Note that adab carries reward for doing and no blame for leaving, while sunnah carries reward and is blameworthy (but not punishable) to leave.
3
List the etiquettes mentioned in the text
Identify each etiquette from the list: sitting elevated, facing qibla, vessel placement, not seeking help, avoiding speech, combining intention and utterance, prescribed supplications, and saying basmalah at each limb.
The text says 'fourteen' but explicitly names eight; the rest are implied or in footnotes.
4
Explain the wisdom behind each etiquette
For each listed adab, state the reason given in the text (e.g., sitting high to avoid used water, facing qibla to enhance acceptance of supplication).

Section on the etiquettes of wudu: The etiquettes of wudu are fourteen things, and we have added to them what is easy by the grace of Allah. 'Adab' is plural of 'adab', defined as placing things in their proper places, or a praiseworthy trait, or piety, or that which doing is better than leaving, or that for which the responsible person is praised and not blamed, or that which is required by the law without blame for leaving. In Sharh al-Hidayah, adab is what the Prophet did once or twice but did not consistently practice. It is called nafl, mustahab, and tatawwu'. Its ruling is reward for doing and no blame for leaving. As for what the Prophet consistently practiced, or left once or twice without excuse, it is sunnah, and its ruling is reward, and leaving it is blameworthy but not punishable. (Sitting in a high place) to avoid the used water; (facing the qiblah) except during istinja, to perform the act of worship and because the qiblah makes supplication more likely to be accepted; (placing the small vessel on the left and the large one on the right); (not seeking help from others) to perform the worship by oneself, unless there is an excuse; (not speaking worldly talk) without necessity, as it distracts from the prescribed supplications; (combining the intention of the heart with the utterance of the tongue) to achieve determination; (supplicating with transmitted prayers) i.e., those from the Prophet, the Companions, and the Followers; (saying the basmalah at each limb) when washing or wiping, and after the basmalah he says at rinsing: 'O Allah, help me to recite the Quran, remember You, thank You, and worship You well'; at sniffling: 'O Allah, let me smell the fragrance of Paradise and not the fire'; at washing the face: 'O Allah, whiten my face on the day when faces are whitened and blackened'; at washing the right hand: 'O Allah, give me my book in my right hand and call me to an easy account'; at washing the left: 'O Allah, do not give me...'
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This section lists the etiquettes (adab) of wudu. The author first defines 'adab' by citing various definitions and clarifies the distinction between adab (mustahab) and sunnah in Hanafi fiqh: adab is an act the Prophet performed occasionally (once or twice) without continuous practice, while sunnah is what he did consistently. The ruling of adab is reward for doing and no blame for leaving. The list includes fourteen items: sitting in a high place to avoid splashed water, facing the qiblah except when relieving oneself, placing the small vessel on the left and large on right, not seeking help from others, not speaking worldly talk, combining intention with utterance, reciting transmitted supplications, and saying 'Bismillah' at each limb with specific du'as for each step. The author also mentions adding more adab, but the text focuses on these. The commentary emphasizes that these adab are recommended, not obligatory, and that they perfect the worship.

Key Terms
أدب (adab): An act done by the Prophet once or twice without constant practice; a recommended act that is rewarded but not blameworthy if left.
مستحب (mustahab): Synonymous with adab; a recommended act.
سنة (sunnah): An act the Prophet consistently practiced; leaving it is blameworthy (makruh tanzihan) but not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Acts that are fard
B) Acts the Prophet did once or twice and did not consistently practice
C) Acts that must be done in wudu
D) Acts that are makruh

Key Takeaway
Adab are recommended acts in wudu that the Prophet did occasionally; they bring reward but no blame for leaving, distinct from sunnah which is consistently practiced and blameworthy to omit.

The Fourteen Etiquettes of Wudu
Commentary on the etiquettes of wudu with definitions and sub-rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourteen etiquettes of wudu and explain the difference between adab (mustahabb) and sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Etiquettes (adab) are recommended; omitting them brings no blame, but omitting a sunnah brings reproach.

This passage from the Hanafi commentary on Nur al-Idah enumerates the fourteen recommended etiquettes of wudu. Understanding these nuances helps you perfect your worship beyond the obligatory. The commentary also defines key terms like adab and sunnah, clarifying their distinct legal weight.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions of adab and sunnah
Find where the text defines adab (actions done once or twice by the Prophet without persistence) and sunnah (actions persisted in with occasional leaving). Note the ruling: reward for adab, no blame; reward for sunnah, reproach for leaving.
The definition is in the first portion of the commentary.
2
List the fourteen etiquettes
From the phrase 'من آداب الوضوء أربعة عشر شيئاً' (from the etiquettes of wudu are fourteen things), enumerate each one as stated in the text.
Some etiquettes have sub-points; focus on the major ones.
3
Understand the evidence for each
The text provides proofs (e.g., hadith for the two testimonies, qiyas for using right hand for mouth and nose). Identify the main proofs cited.
Not every etiquette has a explicit proof; some are derived from general principles.
4
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Read the section on 'التوضؤ قبل دخول الوقت' (wudu before the time). Note the disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say wudu is nullified by exit of time, Zufr says entrance, Abu Yusuf says both.
This sub-ruling is a khilaf among Hanafis.
5
Recognize reward and blame levels
From the definitions, understand that adab yields reward and no blame, sunnah yields reward and reproach, while wajib yields reward and punishment for leaving.
This hierarchy is key to Hanafi fiqh.

مسح.
عنقه بسم
وإدخال خِنْصَرِه في صِمَاحَ أُذُنَيْهِ، وتحريك خاتَمِهِ الواسع، والمَضْمَضَةُ والاسْتِنْشَاقُ باليد اليمنى، والامتخاط باليسرى، والتَّوَضُو قبل دخول الوقتِ لغير المعذور، والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده، وأنْ يشرب من فضلِ الوُضُوءِ قائماً، كتابي بشمالي، ولا من وراء ظهري وعند مسح رأسه بسم الله اللهم أظلني تحت ظل عرشك، يوم لا ظل إلا ظل عرشك. وعند مسح أذنيه: بسم الله اللهم اجعلني من الذين يستمعون القول فيتبعون أحسنه. وعـنـد الله، اللهم أعتق رقبتي من النار، وعند غسل رجله اليمنى: بسم الله اللهم ثبت قدمي على الصراط يوم تزل الأقدام. وعند غسل اليسرى: اللهم اجعل ذنبي مغفوراً وسـعـيـي مشكوراً وتجـارتـي لـن تبور. ويصلي على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد غسل كل عضو ، وشرح هذه الأدعية في « التوضيح » شـرح مقدمـة الفـقـيـه أبي الليث. (وإدخالُ خِنْصَره في صِمَا أُذُنَيْهِ)، مبالغة في المسح. (وتحريك خاتمه الواسع)، مبالغة في الغسل (والمَضْمَضَةُ، والاسْتِنْشَاقُ باليد اليمنى الشرفهما. والامتخاط باليُسْرَى)، لامتهانـــه وقــال بعضهم: الاستنشاق باليسار لأن اليمين مطهرة، والأنف مقذرة، واليمين للأطهار، واليسار للأقذار. ولـنـا مـا روي عن الحسن بن علي ، أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: « اليمين للوجه، واليسار للمقعدة». (والتَّوَضُو قبل دخول الوقتِ) مبادرة للطاعة (لغير المَعْدُورِ)، لأن وضوءه ينتقض بخروج الوقت عندنا، وبدخـولـه عـنـد زفر وعند أبي يوسف بهما (والإتيان بالشهادتين بعده قائماً مستقبلاً لقوله : « مَا مِنْكُمْ مِنْ أَحَدٍ يَتَوَضَا فَيُسْبِعُ الْوُضُوءَ ثُمَّ يَقُولُ: أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهَ وَأَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُولُهُ»، وفي رواية « أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللهُ وَحْدَهُ لا شَرِيكَ لَهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أنَّ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُولُهُ إِلا فُتِحَتْ لَهُ أَبْوَابُ الْجَنَّةِ الثَّمَانِيَةُ يَدْخُلُ مِنْ أَيِّ بَابٍ شاءَ » . وقال الشيخ أبو الحسن البكري: أخرج البيهقي في «الشعب»، قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « مَنْ قالَ إِذَا تَوَضَّأَ سُبْحَانَكَ اللَّهُمَّ وَبِحَمْدِكَ، أَشْهَدُ أن لا إله إلا أنت، أسْتَغْفِرُكَ وأتُوبُ إليك، طبعَ بِطَابع ثم جعل تحت العرش، حتَّى يُؤْتَى بِصَاحِبِهَا يومَ القِيَامَةِ » . ( وأنْ يشربَ منْ فضلِ الوُضُوءِ قائماً) (۳) مستقبل القبلة،
وو
(۱) أخرجه مسلم في الطهارة، باب الذكر المستحب عقب الوضوء (٢٣٤)، وأبو داود في الطهارة، باب: مـا يقـول الرجل إذا توضأ (١٦٩). (٢) أخرجه البيهقي في شعب الإيمان (۲۱/۳). (۳) فائدة: ذكر العلامة عبد الرحمن بن محمد العمادي رحمه الله في شرح هدية ابن العماد (١٥٣)، إن من فوائد الشرب من فضل الوضوء فيه شفاء من أمراض شتى. وعن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( أن في شرب فضلة الوضوء شفاء من سبعين داء». وقال العمادي - رحمه الله -: ومما جربتـه أنــي كنت إذا أصابني مرض، أقصد الاستشفاء بشرب فضلة ماء الوضوء من الإناء أو غيره فيحصل لي الشفاء بإذن الله وذلك اعتماداً على قول الصادق المصدوق في هذا الطب النبوي وفي هذا المعنى قيل:
تَوَضَّأُ يا فتى إِن كُنتَ تَرجو لقاء الله في دار البقاء
واشرب بعـــد إسباغ وضـــــوءاً لماء كانَ يَبْقى في الإنـ
فإنَّ الشـرب مـــن بـاقـي وَضوع إلى سبعين داء
- ٧٦ -
Chapter on the etiquettes of wudu. Among the etiquettes of wudu are fourteen things: sitting in an elevated place, facing the qibla, not seeking help from others, not speaking the speech of people, combining intention of the heart with action of the tongue, supplicating with transmitted supplications, saying bismillah at each limb. [Commentary]: ... (sitting in an elevated place) to avoid the splashing water, (facing the qibla) except during istinja, to perform the worship and because it is the qibla and supplication towards it is more hopeful for acceptance. ... (not seeking help from others) to perform the worship by himself, so he should not seek help from others except with an excuse. (not speaking the speech of people) without necessity because it distracts him from the commanded supplications. (combining intention of the heart and action of the tongue) to acquire resolution. (supplicating with transmitted supplications) i.e. transmitted from the Prophet and the companions and the followers, and saying bismillah when washing each limb or wiping. ... (inserting his little finger into the ear holes) to exaggerate in wiping, (moving his loose ring) to exaggerate in washing, (rinsing the mouth and snuffing water with the right hand) to honor them, and blowing the nose with the left because of its lowliness. Some said: snuffing with the left because the right is for purification and the nose is impure, and the right is for pure things and the left for impure things. Our evidence is what is narrated from Hasan ibn Ali that the Prophet said: 'The right is for the face and the left for the posterior.' (performing wudu before the entrance of the time) hastening to obedience (for the one who is not excused) because his wudu is nullified by the exit of the time according to us, and by its entrance according to Zufr and according to Abu Yusuf by both. (and coming with the two testimonies after it) standing facing the qibla, because of his statement: 'There is none of you who performs wudu and perfects the wudu, then says: I testify that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His slave and Messenger...' In a narration: 'I testify that there is no god but Allah alone, no partner for Him, and I testify that Muhammad is His slave and Messenger, except that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for him, he enters from whichever he wishes.' (And that he drinks from the leftover water of wudu) standing, facing the qibla. [Then a long footnote about the benefits of drinking leftover wudu water, including a hadith and a poem.]
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the fourteen etiquettes (adab) of wudu. It begins by defining 'adab' linguistically and technically, noting that according to al-Hidayah it refers to actions done by the Prophet once or twice without persistence. Such actions are called nafil, mustahabb, or tatawwu', and their ruling is reward for doing and no blame for leaving. Actions the Prophet persisted in with leaving once or twice are sunnah, with reward and reproach for leaving. The commentary then explains each etiquette: sitting on a raised place to avoid splash water; facing qibla except during istinja; not seeking help from others (allowed with excuse); not speaking unnecessary words; combining heart intention with tongue; making transmitted supplications, including specific du'as for each limb—these du'as are quoted in full, asking for various benefits related to the Day of Judgment and good deeds. Then the commentary adds more etiquettes: inserting the little finger into the ear holes for thorough wiping; moving a loose ring for thorough washing; using the right hand for rinsing mouth and nose, and left for blowing nose—with an interesting debate: some argue the left for snuffing because it handles impurities, but the Hanafi position relies on a hadith that 'the right is for the face, the left for the posterior.' Next is performing wudu before the time for a person not excused—note the intra-madhhab difference: according to the Hanafi school, wudu is nullified by the exit of the time (i.e., if one prays the obligatory prayer with that wudu, after the time it breaks), while Zufr says by entrance of the time, and Abu Yusuf says by both. Then reciting the two testimonies after wudu, standing and facing qibla, supported by a hadith that the eight gates of Paradise are opened for one who says that. Finally, drinking leftover wudu water standing and facing qibla, with a benefit that it heals seventy diseases. The passage is rich in practical detail and shows the Hanafi emphasis on perfecting acts of worship with recommended supplements.

Key Terms
أدب (adab): A recommended action that the Prophet did once or twice without persisting; its performance yields reward and its omission is not blameworthy.
سنة (sunnah): An action the Prophet consistently performed with occasional (once or twice) abandonment; its omission brings reproach but not punishment.
مستحب (mustahabb): Synonymous with adab in this text: a recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on performing wudu before the time of prayer for a person who is not excused (ghayr ma'dhur)?
A) It is wajib
B) It is mustahabb (recommended)
C) It is makruh
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
The fourteen etiquettes of wudu are recommended (mustahabb) acts; knowing their legal weight helps one distinguish between the obligatory, sunnah, and adab.

Taharah — Purification

Sunan of Wudu: Comprehensive List and Proofs
Lists sunan of wudu with proofs and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the sunan muakkadah of wudu, explain the Hanafi proof for using the right hand for istinshaq, and state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar on wudu before the prayer time.

Core Idea
The sunan of wudu elevate purification from mere ritual to an act of worship with multiplied reward.

Wudu is not only about fulfilling the obligatory and necessary acts; the sunan transform it into a comprehensive spiritual practice. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah enumerates several recommended actions, each supported by Prophetic practice or explicit hadith. We will walk through each sunnah, understand its rationale, and examine a minor intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of wudu performed before the prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the physical sunan
List the recommended acts related to body parts: inserting little finger into ears, moving a loose ring, madmadah, istinshaq, and imtikhat.
These are all sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the right-left distinction
Understand the proof for using right hand for madmadah/istinshaq and left for imtikhat. The hadith 'The right is for the face, the left for the private parts' establishes a general principle.
Refutes an opinion that istinshaq should be with left hand.
3
Examine the sunnah of wudu before time
Note that performing wudu before the prayer time is recommended for a non-excused person, but there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on when it becomes nullified.
Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: nullified by exit of time; Zufar: by entry; Abu Yusuf: by both.
4
Review the post-wudu dhikr
Reciting the shahadah and the additional dua after wudu is a sunnah, with explicit promises of Paradise and acceptance.
Facing qibla and standing are recommended but not required.

Source Text

وإدخال خِنصَرِه في صِمَاخ أُذُنَيْهِ، وتحريك خاتَمِهِ الواسع، والمَضمَضَةُ والاستِنشَاقُ باليد اليُمنى، والامتِخاطُ باليُسرى، والتَوَضُّؤُ قبل دخول الوقتِ لغير المَعذورِ، والإتيانُ بالشهادتين بعده، ثم قال: (وإدخالُ خِنصَرِه في صِمَاخ أُذُنَيْهِ) مبالغةً في المسح. (وتحريك خاتَمِهِ الواسع) مبالغةً في الغَسل. (والمَضمَضَةُ والاستِنشَاقُ باليد اليُمنى) شرفهما. (والامتِخاطُ باليُسرى) لامتهانِهِ. وقال بعضهم: الاستنشاق باليسار لأن اليمين مُطهَّرة، والأنف مُقذرة، واليمين للأطهار، واليسار للأقذار. ولنا ما رُوي عن الحسن بن علي رضي الله عنهما أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «اليَمينُ للوَجهِ، واليَسارُ للمَقعدةِ». (والتَوَضُّؤُ قبل دخول الوقتِ) مُبادرةً للطاعة (لغير المَعذورِ)، لأن وضوءَهُ ينتقضُ بخروج الوقتِ عندنا، وبدخوله عند زُفَر، وعند أبي يوسف بهما. (والإتيانُ بالشهادتين بعده قائماً مُستَقبِلاً) لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «ما مِنكُم مِن أحَدٍ يَتَوَضَّأُ فَيُسبِغُ الوُضوءَ ثُمَّ يَقولُ: أَشهَدُ أن لا إلهَ إلاَّ اللهُ وأنَّ مُحمَّداً عبدُهُ ورَسولُهُ، إلاَّ فُتِحَتْ له أبوابُ الجَنَّةِ الثَّمانِيةُ يَدخُلُ مِن أيِّ بابٍ شاء». وقال الشيخ أبو الحسن البكري: أخرج البيهقي في «الشعب» قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَن قالَ إذا تَوَضَّأَ: سُبحانَكَ اللَّهُمَّ وبِحَمدِكَ، أَشهَدُ أن لا إلهَ إلا أنت، أستَغفِرُكَ وأتوبُ إليك، طُبِعَ بطابِعٍ ثم جُعِلَ تحتَ العَرشِ حتى يُؤتى بِصاحِبِها يومَ القيامةِ».
And inserting his little finger into the ear canals, and moving his loose ring, and rinsing the mouth and sniffing water with the right hand, and blowing the nose with the left, and performing wudu before the entry of the time for the non-excused, and reciting the two testimonies after it. Then he said: (And inserting his little finger into the ear canals) as an exaggeration in wiping. (And moving his loose ring) as an exaggeration in washing. (And rinsing the mouth and sniffing water with the right hand) due to their honor. (And blowing the nose with the left) due to its indignity. Some said: sniffing water with the left because the right is pure and the nose is impure, and the right is for pure things, the left for impure. Our proof is what is narrated from al-Hasan ibn Ali that the Prophet said: 'The right is for the face, and the left is for the private parts.' (And performing wudu before the entry of the time) as haste to obedience (for the non-excused), because his wudu is nullified by the exit of the time according to us, and by its entry according to Zufar, and according to Abu Yusuf by both. (And reciting the two testimonies after it standing facing the qibla) due to his saying: 'There is none of you who performs wudu and completes it, then says: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, except that the eight doors of Paradise are opened for him, and he enters from whichever he wishes.' And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Bakri said: al-Bayhaqi narrated in 'al-Shu'ab' that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever says when he performs wudu: Glory be to You, O Allah, and with Your praise, I bear witness that there is no god but You, I seek Your forgiveness and repent to You, it is stamped with a seal and placed under the Throne until its owner is brought on the Day of Resurrection.'
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah elaborates on the sunan (recommended acts) of wudu as stated in the matn of Nur al-Idah. It begins by listing several physical sunan: inserting the little finger into the ear canals to ensure thorough wiping, moving a loose ring to allow water to reach the skin, performing madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water) with the right hand due to its honor, and istintar (blowing the nose) with the left hand because it is an act of cleaning impurities. The author refutes an opinion that istinshaq should be with the left, citing the hadith 'The right is for the face, and the left is for the private parts,' which establishes a general principle. Next, the text discusses the sunnah of performing wudu before the prayer time for someone who is not excused (i.e., not having a chronic excuse like continuous bleeding). It mentions an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the wudu of such a person is nullified by the exit of the time, while Zufar holds it is nullified by the entry, and Abu Yusuf says by both. This disagreement affects whether the wudu must be repeated if the time passes. Finally, the passage covers the sunnah of reciting the shahadah after wudu, standing and facing the qibla, supported by a hadith promising Paradise. An additional dua is recommended from the narration of al-Bayhaqi. The overall lesson highlights that wudu is not merely a physical purification but is accompanied by spiritual practices that multiply its reward.

Key Terms
خِنصَر (khinsar): The little finger; recommended to insert into the ear canals while wiping the ears.
صِمَاخ (simakh): The ear canal; the opening of the ear into which the little finger is inserted during ear wiping.
المَضمَضَة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water; a sunnah act of wudu.
الاستِنشَاق (al-istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nostrils; a sunnah act of wudu.
الامتِخاط (al-imtikhat): Blowing the nose to expel water after istinshaq; done with left hand.
التَوَضُّؤُ قبل دخول الوقت (al-tawaddū' qabla dukhūl al-waqt): Performing wudu before the prayer time begins; recommended for a non-excused person.
الشهادتان (al-shahādatān): The two testimonies: 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh', recited after wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which hand should be used for istinshaq (sniffing water) during wudu?
A) Right hand
B) Left hand
C) Either hand
D) Both hands together

Key Takeaway
The sunan of wudu, including physical acts, timing, and supplications, are recommended but not obligatory; they enhance the act of purification and bring reward, but their omission does not invalidate wudu.

Post-Wudu Sunan: Drinking Leftover Water and Wudu Etiquette
Describes the sunnah of drinking leftover wudu water and adab of wudu.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah rulings related to drinking leftover wudu water and list at least three adab of wudu, explaining their legal basis.

Core Idea
Drinking leftover wudu water is a sunnah muakkadah; standing while drinking is makruh tanzih except for wudu water and Zamzam.

This lesson covers two related areas: the specific sunnah of drinking leftover wudu water (including its ruling, proof, and exception) and the broader adab of wudu. You will see how the Hanafi school derives these rulings from hadith and scholarly consensus, and learn practical etiquettes that elevate wudu from a mere ritual to a holistic act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts
Recognize that drinking leftover wudu water while standing facing qibla with a specific dua is a sunnah muakkadah. Note that standing while drinking in general is disliked except for wudu leftover and Zamzam.
The dua is 'Allahumma aj'alni min al-tawwabin...'.
2
Understand the dalil
Learn the hadith prohibiting standing drinking: 'La yashrabanna ahadukum qa'iman...' and the scholarly consensus (ijma') that the karahah is tanzihiyyah because the reason is medical, not religious.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Apply the exception
Note that the Prophet himself drank leftover wudu water and Zamzam standing, which makes these two exceptions to the general dislike. This shows that the ruling is based on his practice overriding the general prohibition.
The text says 'wa lahu' indicating the Prophet's action.
4
Extract the adab
List the adab mentioned: covering head before entering toilet, avoiding sun-heated water, not monopolizing a vessel, preferring public wudu places, not hitting the face with water, not looking at private parts, not spitting into water, using at least a mudd of water, and avoiding waste or stinginess.
Each adab is supported by a hadith or statement from a salaf.

Source Text

وأن يشرب من فضل الوضوء قائماً مستقبل القبلة، وأن يقول: اللهم اجعلني من التوابين، واجعلني من المتطهرين. وإن شاء قاعداً لأنه شرب قائماً فضل وضوئه، وماء زمزم. ويكره الشرب قائماً إلا في هذين. قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا يشربن أحدكم قائماً، فمن نسي فليستقيء». وأجمع العلماء على أن هذه الكراهة تنزيهية، لأنها لأمر طبي لا ديني. ولا يشرب ماشياً، ورخص للمسافر. وقد صح عنه الشرب قائماً في غير زمزم والوضوء، ولعله تعليماً للجواز. (وأن يقول: اللهم اجعلني من التوابين) أي الراجعين من كل ذنب. يقال: تاب العبد إلى ربه إذا رجع عن ذنبه، وتاب الله عليه إذا قبل توبته أو وفقه لها. والتائب اسم فاعل منه، والتواب مبالغة، وقيل: هو الرجل كلما أذنب بادر بالتوبة، وقيل: هو المسبح، دليله قوله تعالى: ﴿يَا جِبَالُ أَوِّبِي مَعَهُ﴾ [سبأ: ١٠] أي سبحي، إذ التواب والأواب بمعنى واحد. والتواب من صفات الله تعالى أيضاً، لأنه يرجع بالإنعام على كل مذنب بقبول توبته. واجعَلني من المتطهرين أي المنزهين عن الفواحش، وقيل: المتطهرون هم الذين لم يذنبوا. وقدم ذكر المذنبين التائبين على من لم يذنب لئلا يقنط التائب من الرحمة، ولا يعجب المتطهر بنفسه. ومن الآداب: وضع ما فيه اسم الله تعالى إلا إذا اضطر قبل دخول الخلاء، ومنها: دخوله مستور الرأس، ومنها: ألا يتوضأ بماء مشمس لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعائشة حين سخنت الماء: «لا تفعلي يا حميراء، فإنه يورث البرص». ومنها: أن لا يستخلص لنفسه إناء يتوضأ منه دون غيره. سئل محمد بن واسع: أي الوضوء أحب إليك؟ أمن ماء مخمر؟ أو متوضأ العامة؟ قال: من متوضأ العامة. قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إن أحب الأديان إلى الله تعالى السمحة الحنيفية». ومنها: صب الماء بغير تعنيف الوجه بضربه بالماء، وترك النظر إلى العورة، وإلقاء البصاق والمخاط في الماء، وأن لا ينقص ماء وضوئه عن مد، وأن لا يسرف ولا يقتّر فيه، وأن لا ...
And that he drink from the leftover of wudu standing facing the qibla, and that he say: O Allah, make me among the oft-repentant and make me among those who purify themselves. And if he wishes, sitting, because he (the Prophet) drank standing the leftover of his wudu and Zamzam water. And drinking standing is disliked except in these two. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Let none of you drink standing; whoever forgets should vomit.' And the scholars agreed that this dislike is tanzihi (not strictly forbidden), because it is for a medical reason, not religious. And he should not drink walking, and there is a concession for the traveler. And it is authentically reported that he drank standing in other than Zamzam and wudu leftover, perhaps to teach permissibility. (And that he say: O Allah, make me among the oft-repentant) meaning those who return from every sin. It is said: the servant repents to his Lord when he returns from his sin, and Allah relents toward him when He accepts his repentance or grants him success to it. 'Tā'ib' is the active participle, 'tawwāb' is an intensive form, and it is said: it is the man who hastens to repentance whenever he sins, and it is said: it is one who glorifies, its proof is His saying: 'O mountains, echo with him' [Saba:10] meaning glorify, for 'tawwāb' and 'awwāb' have the same meaning. And 'tawwāb' is also an attribute of Allah, because He returns with favor upon every sinner by accepting his repentance. And 'make me among those who purify themselves' meaning those who are pure from indecencies, and it is said: they are those who have not sinned. And the mention of the sinning repentant is placed before the non-sinning so that the repentant does not despair of mercy and the pure does not become conceited. And among the adab: placing that which contains the name of Allah before entering the toilet unless forced, among them: entering with head covered, among them: not performing wudu with water heated by the sun because the Prophet said to Aisha when she heated water: 'Do not do that, O Humayra', for it causes leprosy.' Among them: not taking for himself a vessel from which he performs wudu to the exclusion of others. Muhammad ibn Wasi' was asked: Which wudu do you love more? From covered water or the public wudu place? He said: From the public wudu place. The Prophet said: 'Indeed the most beloved religion to Allah is the tolerant Hanifiyyah.' Among them: pouring water without harshly hitting the face with water, leaving off looking at the private parts, spitting and blowing mucus into the water, and that he not reduce his wudu water from a mudd, and that he not be wasteful nor miserly in it, and that he not ...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage continues from the previous lesson, now addressing post-wudu practices and general adab (etiquette) of wudu. The first sunnah is drinking the leftover wudu water while standing and facing the qibla, accompanied by a specific dua asking to be among the repentant and purified. The author notes that the Prophet drank leftover wudu water and Zamzam water standing, but drinking standing in general is makruh tanzihi (disliked, not sinful) due to medical concerns, as indicated by the hadith 'Let none of you drink standing' and the scholarly consensus that the dislike is medical, not religious. Exceptions are made for Zamzam and leftover wudu water, as authentically reported. A concession for travelers is also mentioned. The text then explains the dua 'O Allah make me among the oft-repentant' (tawwabin) and 'those who purify themselves' (mutatahhirin), providing lexical and exegetical notes. Finally, a list of adab of wudu is given: removing items with Allah's name before entering the toilet, entering with head covered, avoiding water heated by the sun due to a hadith warning of leprosy, not monopolizing a vessel, preferring public wudu places, pouring water without hitting the face, not looking at private parts, not spitting into the water, not using less than a mudd (approx. 1.032 liters), and avoiding extravagance or miserliness. This lesson emphasizes that wudu is surrounded by both spiritual and practical etiquettes.

Key Terms
فضل الوضوء (fadl al-wudū'): The leftover water after performing wudu; it is recommended to drink it.
تواب (tawwāb): One who repeatedly repents; an attribute of Allah meaning He accepts repentance again and again.
متطهر (mutaṭahhir): One who purifies himself from sins; in context, those who avoid indecencies.
ماء مشمس (mā' mushammas): Water heated by the sun in a metal container; warned against using for wudu because it may cause leprosy.
مد (mudd): A measure of volume (approx. 1.032 liters); the minimum recommended amount of water for wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers drinking leftover wudu water a sunnah muakkadah and standing while drinking makruh tanzih except for wudu leftover and Zamzam, supported by hadith and scholarly consensus.
