The Six Disliked Acts in Wudu: Understanding Makruhat and Their Proofs
Lists and explains six makruhat in wudu with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six disliked acts in wudu, classify them as makruh tanzih, and identify the hadith proof for israf.

Core Idea
Six acts in wudu are disliked, not forbidden; avoiding them completes the sunnah.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the six makruhat of wudu listed in Nur al-Idah. The commentator defines makruh as something disliked but not sinful, and provides hadith proofs for each disliked act. Understanding these helps you perfect your wudu by avoiding what undermines its etiquette and reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify Each Disliked Act
Read the list of six acts: israf, taqtir, striking the face, worldly talk, seeking help without excuse, and wiping three times with new water. Note each one carefully.
The list is not exhaustive but covers key points.
2
Understand the Ruling (Makruh Tanzih)
For each act, note that the ruling is makruh tanzih—disliked but not sinful. Avoidance is rewarded, but doing it does not invalidate wudu.
Some acts like israf may be closer to makruh tahrimi (sinful) but the text treats them as tanzih.
3
Learn the Proof for Israf
The hadith of Sa'd (Ahmad, Ibn Majah) explicitly prohibits israf even on a flowing river. This is the strongest proof. Understand that the principle applies regardless of water abundance.
The dalil is sunnah ahad (zanni thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati dalala).
4
Distinguish Seeking Help With and Without Excuse
The main ruling dislikes seeking help without excuse. However, an intra-madhhab difference exists: al-Obari allows it because the Prophet's servant poured for him. The mufta bihi is that it is disliked without excuse but allowed if needed.
This shows that even disliked acts can become permissible under necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Section on Disliked Acts. And six things are disliked for the one performing wudu: extravagance in water, stinginess in it, striking the face with it, speaking worldly talk, seeking help from others without excuse, and wiping three times with new water. Section on Disliked Acts. And from what is disliked for the one performing wudu is dislike (the source is karaha, meaning you dislike something, it is the opposite of love). The disliked things are not limited to what he mentioned, and a close approximation of their enumeration is that they oppose good manners and the recommended acts mentioned previously, but he counted some of them to awaken the student, so he said: And from what is disliked for the one performing wudu are six things: extravagance in using water, because of the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, to Sa'd when he passed by him while he was performing wudu: 'What is this extravagance, O Sa'd?' He said: 'Is there extravagance in wudu?' He said: 'Yes, even if you are on a flowing river.' Narrated by Ahmad and Ibn Majah. And wiping three times with new water. And stinginess (taqtir): it means reducing it, missing the sunnah, it falls between excess and deficiency. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The best of affairs is their middle course.' And striking the face with water is disliked because it contradicts the honor of the face, so he should pour it gently. And speaking worldly talk is disliked because it distracts from supplications. And seeking help from others is disliked because of the saying of 'Umar: I saw the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, fetching water for his wudu, so I rushed to fetch water for him. He said: 'Stop, O 'Umar, for I do not want anyone to assist me in my prayer.' Without excuse, because necessities permit prohibitions, so how about that which is not prohibited? And from al-Obari, may Allah have mercy on him, there is no harm in it, for the servant used to pour water for the Prophet, peace be upon him. And when he mentioned the cause of wudu, its condition, its ruling, and its pillar, he described it separately, and said:
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the section on disliked acts (makruhat) in wudu. The author first quotes the matn from Nur al-Idah which lists six things disliked for the one performing wudu. Then the sharh begins by defining makruh as something disliked, opposite of love, and notes that the enumeration is not exhaustive but serves as a wake-up call for students. Each disliked act is explained with a proof: extravagance (israf) is condemned even on a flowing river according to a hadith; stinginess (taqtir) misses the sunnah and the middle course is best; striking the face contradicts its honor; worldly talk distracts from dhikr; seeking help without excuse is disliked as the Prophet refused assistance; but it is allowed if one has an excuse, as the servant poured for the Prophet. The commentator then transitions back to the description of wudu proper.

Key Terms
المكروه (al-makruh): Something disliked but not forbidden; avoidance is rewarded but commission is not punished.
الإسراف (al-israf): Using more water than necessary, even if the source is abundant.
التقتير (al-taqtir): Using too little water, causing incompleteness of the sunnah of washing thoroughly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Mubah
C) Makruh
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The six disliked acts in wudu are israf, taqtir, striking the face, worldly talk, seeking help without excuse, and wiping three times with new water; avoiding them perfects the sunnah.

Wudu is Fard for Prayer and Other Acts
Explains the first division of wudu: obligatory for prayer, funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah, and touching Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five acts for which wudu is fard (obligatory) and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Wudu is obligatory for prayer, funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah, and touching the Quran.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains when wudu becomes fard (obligatory). It is a foundational ruling in taharah. We will learn the specific acts that require wudu and the proofs from Quran and Sunnah. Understanding this helps you avoid invalidating your worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the first sentence: wudu is divided into three divisions, the first is fard. Note the acts for which it is fard.
Focus on the list: prayer (even supererogatory), funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah, and touching Quran.
2
Understand the definition of fard
The author gives linguistic and legal definitions. Distinguish between definitive fard (denial leads to disbelief) and ijtihadi fard (denial does not).
This affects the weight of obligation.
3
Examine the proofs
For prayer, the verse 5:6 and hadith are cited. For touching Quran, verse 56:79. For funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah, analogy is used.
Note the dalala (clarity) difference: qati for prayer, zanni for touching Quran.
4
Note the historical dispute
Ibn al-Jahm claimed wudu was only recommended before Hijra. The Hanafi position is that it was fard from the beginning.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf, but the mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test yourself: Is wudu required for touching a verse on a coin? The passage says yes, even a verse.
The proof is 'None touch it except the purified'.

فصل في أوصاف الوضوء
الوضوء على ثلاثة أقسام: الأوّلُ: فرض على المُحْدِثِ للصّلاةِ، ولـو كـانـت نـفـلا، والصلاة الجنازة، وسجدة التلاوة، ولِمَس القرآن، ولو آية...
فصل في أوصاف الوضوء
ينقسم (الوضوء إلى ثلاثة أقسام: الأوّلُ) منها أنه (فَرْضٌ)، الفرض لغة: القطع والتقدير. قــال الله تعالى: (سُورَةُ أَنزَلْنَهَا وَفَرَضْنَهَا) [النور: ١] أي: قدرناها، وقطعنا الأحكام فيها قطعاً. وشرعاً: عبارة عن حكم مقدر لا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصاً، ثبت بدليل لا شبهة فيه. وكثيراً ما يطلق الفرض عـلـى مـا يفوت الجواز بفوته، ولا ينجبر بجابر، كغسل مقدار معين، ومسح مقدار معين. وهـو الفــرض عملاً لا علماً، ويسمى الفرض الاجتهادي. والفرق بين الاجتهادي والقطعي، الحكم بإكفـار جـاحد القطعي لا الاجتهادي، وفُرِضَ الوضوء بمكة المشرفة، ونزلت آيته بالمدينة المنورة. وزعــم ابـن الجهم المالكي: أ ب أنه كان مندوباً قبل الهجرة، وابن حزم أنه لم يشرع إلا في المدينة. ودليله في المطولات وكان الوضوء فرضاً بالأمر ( على المُحْدِثِ)، إذا أراد القيام (للصلاة) بقوله تعالى: يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَوَةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ الآية اللساندة : ٦]. وبقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعدما توضأ كما ذكرناه. « هذا وضوء لا يقبلُ الله الصلاة إلا بِهِ » ) (وَلَو كَانَتْ الصلاة (نفلا)، لما ذكرناه. ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لا تُقْبَلُ صلاةٌ مِن غير طهورٍ » (۳) فبين بهذا أن الله تعالى لا يقبـل صـلاة، أيـة صـلاة كانت، إلا بطهارة، إما بالغسل بالماء، أو بالتيمم. وقوله: «مِفتاح الصلاة الطهور (۳) والطهور في هذا الحديث وغيره من الأحاديث، بفتح الطاء، عن جمهور الرواة. وقال بعض الأئمة: الأجود ضمه، لأنه متفق عليه. والفتح مختلف فيه. (وَ) كذا لصلاة الجنازة، لأنها صلاة، وإن لم تكن كاملة (و) كذا فرض لأداء (سجدة التلاوة)، إذ لا تصح بدون طهارة. (وَ) كذا لإرادة (لمس القرآن، ولو آية) مكتوبة على درهم، أو حائط، لقوله تعالى: وَلَا يَمَسُّهُ إِلَّا الْمُطَهَّرُونَ﴾ [ الواجي : ٧٩] (1) أخرجه الطبراني في الأوسط (٧٨/٤)..
Chapter on the descriptions of wudu. Wudu is divided into three divisions: The first is obligatory (fard) upon the one in hadath for prayer, even if it is supererogatory, and for funeral prayer, and for the prostration of recitation, and for touching the Quran, even a verse... Chapter on the descriptions of wudu. Wudu is divided into three divisions: the first is that it is fard. Fard linguistically means cutting and determining. Allah said: “A surah which We have sent down and made fard (i.e., prescribed)” (Quran 24:1), meaning We determined it and cut the rulings in it conclusively. Legally, it is an determined ruling that does not admit increase or decrease, established by an unequivocal proof. Often fard is applied to what, if omitted, removes permissibility and is not compensable, like washing a specific amount and wiping a specific amount. It is fard in practice, not necessarily in knowledge, and is called ijtihadi fard. The difference between ijtihadi and definitive is that the denier of the definitive is deemed a disbeliever, not the denier of ijtihadi. Wudu was made obligatory in Mecca, and its verse was revealed in Medina. Ibn al-Jahm al-Maliki claimed it was recommended before the Hijra, and Ibn Hazm said it was only legislated in Medina. His proof is in the lengthy works. And wudu was made fard by the command upon the one in hadath when he intends to stand for prayer by His statement: “O you who believe, when you stand for prayer, wash your faces...” (Quran 5:6) and by the Prophet’s statement after performing wudu as we mentioned: “This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer.” (And even if the prayer is supererogatory) due to what we mentioned, and because of his saying: “No prayer is accepted without purification.” Thus it is made clear that Allah does not accept any prayer except with purification, either by washing with water or by tayammum. And his saying: “The key to prayer is purification.” The word tahur in this hadith and others is with fatha on the ta according to most narrators. Some imams said the better pronunciation is with dammah because it is agreed upon, while the fatha is disputed. (And) similarly for funeral prayer because it is a prayer, even if incomplete. (And) similarly fard for performing the prostration of recitation, for it is not valid without purification. (And) similarly for wanting to touch the Quran, even a verse written on a dirham or a wall, due to His statement: “None touch it except the purified” (Quran 56:79). Reported by al-Tabarani in al-Awsat.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Nur al-Idah regarding the descriptions (awsaf) of wudu. The author begins by stating that wudu has three divisions. The first division is that wudu is fard (obligatory) for the one in a state of minor impurity (hadath) when he intends to perform prayer, even supererogatory prayer, and also for funeral prayer, the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah), and for touching the Quran. The commentary then elaborates on the linguistic and legal definition of fard. Linguistically, fard means cutting and determining, as in the Quranic verse. Legally, it is a determined ruling established by a clear proof, which does not admit increase or decrease. The author distinguishes between fard in practice (ijtihadi) and definitive fard; the denier of definitive fard becomes a disbeliever, while the denier of ijtihadi fard does not. Wudu was made obligatory in Mecca, but the verse was revealed in Medina. Some scholars claimed it was only recommended before Hijra, but the majority holds it was obligatory from the beginning. The proof is the Quranic command to wash for prayer and the hadith that prayer is not accepted without purification. The same rule applies to funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah, and touching the Quran, each supported by evidence. For sajdah tilawah, purification is required for its validity. For touching the Quran, the verse “None touch it except the purified” is the proof. The author also notes a variant reading of “tahur” (purification) in the hadith. This lesson establishes the obligatory nature of wudu for these specific acts.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): An obligatory ruling established by a clear proof, not admitting increase or decrease; omission invalidates the act without compensation.
الفرض الاجتهادي (al-fard al-ijtihadi): An obligation derived through scholarly reasoning (ijtihad), the denial of which does not entail disbelief.
المُحْدِث (al-muhdith): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath) requiring wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which of the following is wudu NOT considered fard according to this passage?
A) Funeral prayer
B) Supererogatory prayer
C) Touching a Quranic verse on a dirham
D) Reading the Quran without touching

Key Takeaway
Wudu is obligatory (fard) for prayer (including funeral and supererogatory), sajdah tilawah, and touching the Quran; the Quranic command and hadith establish this obligation.

The Obligatory (Fard) Status of Wudu: Definition, Proofs, and Scope
Author defines fard and provides proofs for the obligatory status of wudu for prayer and touching the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of fard as 'fard amalan' in the Hanafi school, identify the primary proofs for wudu being fard for prayer, and apply this to determine that wudu is fard for touching the Quran.

Core Idea
Wudu is fard (practice-based obligation) for prayer and touching the Quran, established by Quran and hadith.

This lesson unpacks the first division of wudu: fard. The author defines fard both linguistically and legally, clarifies it as 'fard amalan' (practice-based) rather than belief-based, and presents the primary evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. You will learn which acts require wudu as fard and why the Hanafi school distinguishes between fard and wajib.

Guided Path
1
Define fard linguistically and legally
The author gives both definitions. Identify the key components: linguistically 'cutting and determining', legally a determined ruling from definitive proof.
Note the citation of Quran 24:1 for linguistic usage.
2
Distinguish fard amalan from fard ilman
Understand that rejecting fard amalan does not incur kufr, whereas rejecting fard ilman does. This is a critical Hanafi distinction.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Locate the primary proof
Identify the Quranic verse (5:6) and the hadith 'No prayer accepted without purification' as the main evidence for the obligation of wudu for prayer.
The imperative 'faghsilu' is a command; in Hanafi usul, amr indicates wujub.
4
Identify the acts for which wudu is fard
List the acts: prayer (fard, nafl, janazah, sajdah tilawa) and touching the Quran (even a verse on a wall or coin).
The text includes detailed discussion on touching the Quran, including margins and Persian translations.
5
Note the historical dispute
The author refutes Ibn al-Jahm and Ibn Hazm who claimed wudu was not obligatory before the Hijra.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position relies on the continuous practice of the early Muslims.

Section on the descriptions of wudu. Wudu is of three types: First: obligatory upon the one in a state of minor impurity for prayer, even if it is supererogatory, and for the funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation, and for touching the Quran, even if one verse... Section on the descriptions of wudu. It is divided into three types: the first of them is that it is fard (obligatory). Fard linguistically means cutting and determining. Allah said: 'A surah which We have sent down and prescribed' meaning: We determined it and cut the rulings in it decisively. Legally: it is an expression of a determined ruling that does not admit increase or decrease, established by a proof with no ambiguity. Often it is applied to what causes permissibility to be lost by its loss, and is not compensated by any compensator, like washing a specific amount and wiping a specific amount. It is fard in practice not in knowledge, and is called ijtihadi fard. The difference between ijtihadi and definitive: the ruling of declaring a rejector of the definitive a disbeliever, not the ijtihadi. Wudu was prescribed in the honored Mecca, and its verse was revealed in Medina. Ibn al-Jahm al-Maliki claimed that it was recommended before the Hijra, and Ibn Hazm that it was only legislated in Medina. Its proof is in the lengthy works. Wudu was obligatory by command upon the muhdith when he intends to perform prayer by His saying: 'O you who believe, when you stand up for prayer, wash your faces' [5:6], and by his saying (peace be upon him) after he performed wudu as we mentioned: 'This is a wudu that Allah does not accept prayer except with it'. Even if the prayer is supererogatory, due to what we mentioned, and by his saying (peace be upon him): 'No prayer is accepted without purification' (3). So by this it is clarified that Allah does not accept any prayer, whichever prayer it is, except with purification, either by washing with water or by tayammum. And his saying: 'The key to prayer is purification' (3). And 'tahur' in this hadith and other hadiths, with fatha on the ta, according to the majority of narrators. Some imams said: the better is damm, because it is agreed upon, while the fatha is disputed. Similarly for the funeral prayer, because it is a prayer even if incomplete. Similarly it is obligatory for performing the prostration of recitation, because it is not valid without purification. Similarly for intending to touch the Quran, even if a verse, written on a dirham or a wall, due to His saying: 'None touch it except the purified' [56:79]. (1) Al-Tabarani in Al-Awsat (4/78). (2) Muslim in Taharah, chapter on obligation of purification for prayer (224), Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter on no prayer without purification (1). (3) Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter on obligation of wudu (61), Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter on the key to prayer is purification (3). The second: wajib for tawaf of the Kaaba. The third: mandub for sleeping in a state of purification, and when one wakes from it, and for continuous maintenance of wudu, and for wudu upon wudu, and after backbiting. And his saying: 'Only a pure person touches the Quran' (1). This includes touching the white parts and the writing. Some of our teachers said: It is only disliked for the muhdith to touch the written part, not the margins, because he has not actually touched the Quran. The correct view is that touching them is like touching the written part. And if it is written in Persian, it is prohibited to touch it by agreement, and this is correct. The second type: wudu (wajib), and it is for tawaf of the Kaaba, due to his saying (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Tawaf around the Kaaba is like prayer, except that you speak in it, so whoever speaks in it should only speak good.' Since it is not actually prayer, its validity does not depend on purification, so if one performs tawaf in a state of impurity, it is valid, but he owes a dam for the obligatory tawaf and sadaqah for the voluntary. The third type: wudu (mandub) in many cases: for touching religious books, renewing wudu out of reverence. Imam al-Halwani said: We only acquire this knowledge with reverence, for I never took the paper (3) except with purification. And Imam al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) experienced a stomach ailment one night while he was repeating his lesson, so he performed wudu that night seventeen times. End. Touching religious books with the hand is permitted for the muhdith, except for tafsir, as stated in al-Durar from Majma' al-Fatawa, and this requires the obligation of wudu for touching tafsir, so it becomes of the second type. Among the cases of recommendation: sleeping in a state of purification, and wudu when waking from sleep, to be prompt in purification and performing worship, and for continuous maintenance, due to the hadith of Bilal. (And wudu upon wudu) if one changes his gathering, because it may be wasteful; but in another gathering it is 'light upon light'. It is restricted to wudu, because ghusl upon ghusl and tayammum upon tayammum are futile. (And after backbiting), which is: mentioning your brother... (1) Malik in al-Muwatta (1/199), al-Darimi in his Sunan (2/214). (2) al-Tirmidhi in Hajj, chapter on speech in tawaf (960). (3) al-kaghad: paper (al-Qamus). (4) His saying: 'When you take your bed, perform wudu like for prayer, then lie on your right side' (Muslim). (5) His saying: 'The eye is the drawstring of the anus, so whoever sleeps, let him perform wudu' (Ibn Majah). (6) Al-Bukhari from Abu Hurayrah: The Prophet said to Bilal at Fajr: 'Tell me of the most hopeful deed you have done in Islam...' (Bukhari). (7) Mentioned by al-Mundhiri in al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib (1/98).
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah opens the section on the descriptions of wudu. The author begins by stating that wudu is divided into three types: fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary), and mandub (recommended). He then provides a detailed commentary on each.

For the first type, fard, he first defines the term linguistically and legally. Linguistically, fard means to cut or determine, citing the Quranic verse where Allah says He 'prescribed' a surah. Legally, fard is a determined ruling that does not admit increase or decrease, established by a definitive proof. He notes that fard in the context of wudu is 'fard amalan' (practical obligation), not 'fard ilman' (matters of belief), and is called 'ijtihadi fard' because it is derived from probabilistic evidence. The difference between this and categorical obligation is that rejecting categorical obligation constitutes disbelief, whereas rejecting practical obligation does not, though it is a major sin.

The author mentions that wudu was originally prescribed in Mecca, but the verse detailing its rulings was revealed in Medina. He refutes the claims of Ibn al-Jahm al-Maliki and Ibn Hazm, who held that wudu was not obligatory before the Hijra. The proof for the obligation is the Quranic verse (5:6) and multiple hadiths, such as 'No prayer is accepted without purification' and 'The key to prayer is purification.' The author explains that this obligation applies to all forms of prayer, including supererogatory, funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation. Additionally, wudu is fard for touching the Quran, even if it is just a verse written on a coin or wall, based on the Quranic verse (56:79) and the hadith 'Only a pure person touches the Quran.' A discussion follows about whether touching the margins of the Quran is also prohibited; the correct view is that it is, as it is like touching the written part.

The second type, wajib, is for tawaf around the Kaaba. The evidence is the hadith comparing tawaf to prayer, but since it is not actually prayer, its validity does not depend on purification. If a person performs tawaf without wudu, the tawaf is valid, but he must offer a dam (sacrifice) for an obligatory tawaf or sadaqah for a voluntary one.

The third type, mandub, applies to many situations: sleeping with wudu, performing wudu upon waking, maintaining constant wudu, renewing wudu in a new gathering (which is 'light upon light'), and after committing backbiting. The author also mentions that touching religious books is permitted without wudu, but for tafsir, it is obligatory. He quotes pious predecessors like Imam al-Halwani and Imam al-Sarakhsi, who were meticulous about being in a state of purification when handling sacred knowledge.

Key Terms
فَرْض (fard): A legal obligation established by a definitive proof (qati), omission of which invalidates the act and requires repetition; in this text, it refers to 'fard amalan' (practical obligation) as opposed to 'fard ilman' (doctrinal obligation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of wudu for touching the Quran?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mandub
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Wudu is fard (practice-based obligation) for prayer and directly touching the Quran, established by definitive textual evidence.

Wajib and Mandub: The Other Two Divisions of Wudu
Author explains the wajib and mandub categories of wudu with evidence and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that wudu is wajib for tawaf and mandub for acts like sleeping and maintaining wudu, and explain the practical consequences of omitting wudu in each case.

Core Idea
Wudu is wajib for tawaf (dam on omission) and mandub for recommended acts (reward without sin).

The author now turns to the second and third divisions: wajib and mandub. While wudu is fard for prayer and Quran, it is only wajib for tawaf, meaning omission does not invalidate tawaf but requires compensation. Mandub wudu is recommended for various virtuous actions, such as sleeping in a state of purity or renewing wudu between gatherings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second division: wajib for tawaf
Note the ruling and the evidence: the hadith comparing tawaf to prayer, but allowing speech.
This is the only act for which wudu is wajib according to this text.
2
Understand the consequence of omission for tawaf
Tawaf without wudu is valid, but a dam (sacrifice) is required for obligatory tawaf, and sadaqah for voluntary.
This differs from fard, where omission invalidates the act entirely.
3
List the recommended (mandub) occasions
Sleeping in a state of purity, wudu upon waking, continuous maintenance of wudu, wudu upon wudu (in a new gathering), and after backbiting.
The text also mentions touching religious books, but notes that tafsir may require wudu.
4
Note the exception for touching tafsir
Some sources indicate that touching tafsir (Quranic commentary) requires wudu, moving it to the wajib category.
This shows that classifications can vary based on different scholarly views.

فصل في أوصاف الوضوء
ينقسم (الوضوء إلى ثلاثة أقسام: الأوّلُ) منها أنه (فَرْضٌ)، الفرض لغة: القطع والتقدير. قــال الله تعالى: (سُورَةُ أَنزَلْنَهَا وَفَرَضْنَهَا) [النور: ١] أي: قدرناها، وقطعنا الأحكام فيها قطعاً. وشرعاً: عبارة عن حكم مقدر لا يحتمل زيادة ولا نقصاً، ثبت بدليل لا شبهة فيه. وكثيراً ما يطلق الفرض عـلـى مـا يفوت الجواز بفوته، ولا ينجبر بجابر، كغسل مقدار معين، ومسح مقدار معين. وهـو الفــرض عملاً لا علماً، ويسمى الفرض الاجتهادي. والفرق بين الاجتهادي والقطعي، الحكم بإكفـار جـاحد القطعي لا الاجتهادي، وفُرِضَ الوضوء بمكة المشرفة، ونزلت آيته بالمدينة المنورة. وزعــم ابـن الجهم المالكي: أ ب أنه كان مندوباً قبل الهجرة، وابن حزم أنه لم يشرع إلا في المدينة. ودليله في المطولات وكان الوضوء فرضاً بالأمر ( على المُحْدِثِ)، إذا أراد القيام (للصلاة) بقوله تعالى: يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا إِذَا قُمْتُمْ إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ فَاغْسِلُوا وُجُوهَكُمْ الآية [المائدة: ٦]. وبقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعدما توضأ كما ذكرناه. « هذا وضوء لا يقبلُ الله الصلاة إلا بِهِ » (وَلَو كَانَتْ الصلاة (نفلا)، لما ذكرناه. ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « لا تُقْبَلُ صلاةٌ مِن غير طهورٍ » (۳) فبين بهذا أن الله تعالى لا يقبـل صـلاة، أيـة صـلاة كانت، إلا بطهارة، إما بالغسل بالماء، أو بالتيمم. وقوله: «مِفتاح الصلاة الطهور (۳) والطهور في هذا الحديث وغيره من الأحاديث، بفتح الطاء، عن جمهور الرواة. وقال بعض الأئمة: الأجود ضمه، لأنه متفق عليه. والفتح مختلف فيه. (وَ) كذا لصلاة الجنازة، لأنها صلاة، وإن لم تكن كاملة (و) كذا فرض لأداء (سجدة التلاوة)، إذ لا تصح بدون طهارة. (وَ) كذا لإرادة (لمس القرآن، ولو آية) مكتوبة على درهم، أو حائط، لقوله تعالى: وَلَا يَمَسُّهُ إِلَّا الْمُطَهَّرُونَ﴾ [ الواقعة : ٧٩]
(1) أخرجه الطبراني في الأوسط (٧٨/٤)..
(۲) أخرجه مسلم في الطهارة، باب وجوب الطهارة للصلاة (٢٢٤)، والترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في لا تقبل صلاة بغير طهور (۱).
(3) أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب فرض الوضوء (٦١)، والترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء أن مفتاح الصلاة
الطهور (۳).

والثاني: واجب، للطَّواف بالكعبة. والثَّالث: مندوب، للنوم على طهارة، وإذا استيقظ منه، وللمداومة
عليه، وللوضوء على الوضوء، وبعد غيبَةٍ .
وقوله : « لا يَمَسُّ القرآن إلا طاهر» (١). وسواء فيه مس البياض والكتابة. وقال بعض مشايخنا: إنما يكره للمحدث مس الموضع المكتوب دون الحواشي، لأنه لم يمس القرآن حقيقة، والصحيح أن مسها كمس المكتوب، ولو كان مكتوباً بالفارسية، يحرم عليه مسه اتفاقاً، وهو الصحيح. (و) القسم (الثاني): وضوء (واجب)، وهو (للطَّوَافِ بِالكَعْبَةِ)، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « الطَّوَافُ حوْلَ الكَعْبَةِ، مِثْلُ الصَّلاةِ، إِلا أَنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ، فَلا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلَّا بِخَيْرِ » . ولما لم يكن صلاة حقيقة لم يتوقف صحته على الطهارة، فإذا طاف محدثاً صح، ولـزمــه دم في الواجب، وصدقة في التطوع. (وَ) القسم ( الثَّالِثُ): وضوء (مَنْدُوبٌ) في أحوال كثيرة، لمس الكتب الشرعية فيجدد له الوضوء تعظيماً. قال الإمام الحلواني»: إنما نلقى هذا العلم بالتعظيم، فإني ما أخذت الكاغد (۳) إلا بطهارة وكان الإمام السرخسي ) رحمه الله حصل له في ليلة داء البطن وهـو يـكـرر درس كتابه، فتوضأ تلك الليلة سبع عشرة مرة. انتهى. ورخص مس الكتب الشرعية باليد للمحدث، إلا التفسير كذا في « الدرر » عن «مجمع الفتاوى » ، وهو يقتضي وجوب الوضوء لمس التفسير، فيكون من القسم الثاني. ومن أحوال الندب (للنّوم على طهارة)، و( الوضوء (إِذَا اسْتَيْقَظَ مِنْهُ))، أي نومه، ليكون مبادراً للطهارة، وأداء العبادة، وللمداومة عليه، لحديث بلال). (وللوضوء على الوضوء) إذا تبدل مجلسه، لأنه يكون فيه إسرافاً، وفي غير مجلسه « نــور عـلـى نـور ، وقيد بالوضوء؛ لأن الغسل على الغسل، والتيمم على التيمم، يكون عبثاً. (وبعد غيبَةٍ)، وهي: ذكر أخاك
(1) أخرجه مالك في الموطأ (۱۹۹/۱)، والدارمي في سننه (٢١٤/٢).
(٢) أخرجه الترمذي في الحج، باب ما جاء في الكلام في الطواف (٩٦٠). (۳) الكاغد القرطاس. القاموس المعجم الوسيط / الكاغد /، أي: ورق الكتابة ونحوه. (٤) لقوله : ( إذا أخذت مضجعك فتوضأ وضوءك للصلاة ثم اضطجع على شقك الأيمن أخرجه مسـ الذكر والدعاء، باب ما يقول عند النوم (٦٨٢٠).
(٥) لقوله : ( العين وكاء السه فمن نام فليتوضأ أخرجه ابن ماجه في الطهارة، باب الوضوء محند النوم (٤٧٧). (٦) روى البخاري عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه: أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لبلال عند صلاة الفجر: «يَا بِلالُ حَدِّثْنِي بِأَرْجَى عَمَلٍ عَمِلْتَهُ فِي الإِسْلَامِ فَإِنِّي سَمِعْتُ دَفَ نَعْلَيْكَ بَيْنَ يَدَيَّ فِي الْجَنَّةِ، قَالَ: مَا عَمِلْتُ عَمَلاً أَرْجَى عِنْدِي أَنِّي لَمْ أَتَطَهَّرُ طَهُورًا فِي سَاعَةِ لَيْل أَوْ نَهَارٍ إِلا صَلَّيْتُ بِذلِكَ الظُّهُورِ مَا كُتِبَ لي أن أصلي، أخرجه البخاري في التهجد، باب فضل الطهور بالليل والنهار (١١٤٩). (۷) ذكره المنذري في الترغيب والترهيب (۹۸/۱).
Section on the descriptions of wudu. Wudu is of three types: First: obligatory upon the one in a state of minor impurity for prayer, even if it is supererogatory, and for the funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation, and for touching the Quran, even if one verse... Section on the descriptions of wudu. It is divided into three types: the first of them is that it is fard (obligatory). Fard linguistically means cutting and determining. Allah said: 'A surah which We have sent down and prescribed' meaning: We determined it and cut the rulings in it decisively. Legally: it is an expression of a determined ruling that does not admit increase or decrease, established by a proof with no ambiguity. Often it is applied to what causes permissibility to be lost by its loss, and is not compensated by any compensator, like washing a specific amount and wiping a specific amount. It is fard in practice not in knowledge, and is called ijtihadi fard. The difference between ijtihadi and definitive: the ruling of declaring a rejector of the definitive a disbeliever, not the ijtihadi. Wudu was prescribed in the honored Mecca, and its verse was revealed in Medina. Ibn al-Jahm al-Maliki claimed that it was recommended before the Hijra, and Ibn Hazm that it was only legislated in Medina. Its proof is in the lengthy works. Wudu was obligatory by command upon the muhdith when he intends to perform prayer by His saying: 'O you who believe, when you stand up for prayer, wash your faces' [5:6], and by his saying (peace be upon him) after he performed wudu as we mentioned: 'This is a wudu that Allah does not accept prayer except with it'. Even if the prayer is supererogatory, due to what we mentioned, and by his saying (peace be upon him): 'No prayer is accepted without purification' (3). So by this it is clarified that Allah does not accept any prayer, whichever prayer it is, except with purification, either by washing with water or by tayammum. And his saying: 'The key to prayer is purification' (3). And 'tahur' in this hadith and other hadiths, with fatha on the ta, according to the majority of narrators. Some imams said: the better is damm, because it is agreed upon, while the fatha is disputed. Similarly for the funeral prayer, because it is a prayer even if incomplete. Similarly it is obligatory for performing the prostration of recitation, because it is not valid without purification. Similarly for intending to touch the Quran, even if a verse, written on a dirham or a wall, due to His saying: 'None touch it except the purified' [56:79]. (1) Al-Tabarani in Al-Awsat (4/78). (2) Muslim in Taharah, chapter on obligation of purification for prayer (224), Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter on no prayer without purification (1). (3) Abu Dawud in Taharah, chapter on obligation of wudu (61), Tirmidhi in Taharah, chapter on the key to prayer is purification (3). The second: wajib for tawaf of the Kaaba. The third: mandub for sleeping in a state of purification, and when one wakes from it, and for continuous maintenance of wudu, and for wudu upon wudu, and after backbiting. And his saying: 'Only a pure person touches the Quran' (1). This includes touching the white parts and the writing. Some of our teachers said: It is only disliked for the muhdith to touch the written part, not the margins, because he has not actually touched the Quran. The correct view is that touching them is like touching the written part. And if it is written in Persian, it is prohibited to touch it by agreement, and this is correct. The second type: wudu (wajib), and it is for tawaf of the Kaaba, due to his saying (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Tawaf around the Kaaba is like prayer, except that you speak in it, so whoever speaks in it should only speak good.' Since it is not actually prayer, its validity does not depend on purification, so if one performs tawaf in a state of impurity, it is valid, but he owes a dam for the obligatory tawaf and sadaqah for the voluntary. The third type: wudu (mandub) in many cases: for touching religious books, renewing wudu out of reverence. Imam al-Halwani said: We only acquire this knowledge with reverence, for I never took the paper (3) except with purification. And Imam al-Sarakhsi (may Allah have mercy on him) experienced a stomach ailment one night while he was repeating his lesson, so he performed wudu that night seventeen times. End. Touching religious books with the hand is permitted for the muhdith, except for tafsir, as stated in al-Durar from Majma' al-Fatawa, and this requires the obligation of wudu for touching tafsir, so it becomes of the second type. Among the cases of recommendation: sleeping in a state of purification, and wudu when waking from sleep, to be prompt in purification and performing worship, and for continuous maintenance, due to the hadith of Bilal. (And wudu upon wudu) if one changes his gathering, because it may be wasteful; but in another gathering it is 'light upon light'. It is restricted to wudu, because ghusl upon ghusl and tayammum upon tayammum are futile. (And after backbiting), which is: mentioning your brother... (1) Malik in al-Muwatta (1/199), al-Darimi in his Sunan (2/214). (2) al-Tirmidhi in Hajj, chapter on speech in tawaf (960). (3) al-kaghad: paper (al-Qamus). (4) His saying: 'When you take your bed, perform wudu like for prayer, then lie on your right side' (Muslim). (5) His saying: 'The eye is the drawstring of the anus, so whoever sleeps, let him perform wudu' (Ibn Majah). (6) Al-Bukhari from Abu Hurayrah: The Prophet said to Bilal at Fajr: 'Tell me of the most hopeful deed you have done in Islam...' (Bukhari). (7) Mentioned by al-Mundhiri in al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib (1/98).
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah opens the section on the descriptions of wudu. The author begins by stating that wudu is divided into three types: fard (obligatory), wajib (necessary), and mandub (recommended). He then provides a detailed commentary on each.

For the first type, fard, he first defines the term linguistically and legally. Linguistically, fard means to cut or determine, citing the Quranic verse where Allah says He 'prescribed' a surah. Legally, fard is a determined ruling that does not admit increase or decrease, established by a definitive proof. He notes that fard in the context of wudu is 'fard amalan' (practical obligation), not 'fard ilman' (matters of belief), and is called 'ijtihadi fard' because it is derived from probabilistic evidence. The difference between this and categorical obligation is that rejecting categorical obligation constitutes disbelief, whereas rejecting practical obligation does not, though it is a major sin.

The author mentions that wudu was originally prescribed in Mecca, but the verse detailing its rulings was revealed in Medina. He refutes the claims of Ibn al-Jahm al-Maliki and Ibn Hazm, who held that wudu was not obligatory before the Hijra. The proof for the obligation is the Quranic verse (5:6) and multiple hadiths, such as 'No prayer is accepted without purification' and 'The key to prayer is purification.' The author explains that this obligation applies to all forms of prayer, including supererogatory, funeral prayer, and the prostration of recitation. Additionally, wudu is fard for touching the Quran, even if it is just a verse written on a coin or wall, based on the Quranic verse (56:79) and the hadith 'Only a pure person touches the Quran.' A discussion follows about whether touching the margins of the Quran is also prohibited; the correct view is that it is, as it is like touching the written part.

The second type, wajib, is for tawaf around the Kaaba. The evidence is the hadith comparing tawaf to prayer, but since it is not actually prayer, its validity does not depend on purification. If a person performs tawaf without wudu, the tawaf is valid, but he must offer a dam (sacrifice) for an obligatory tawaf or sadaqah for a voluntary one.

The third type, mandub, applies to many situations: sleeping with wudu, performing wudu upon waking, maintaining constant wudu, renewing wudu in a new gathering (which is 'light upon light'), and after committing backbiting. The author also mentions that touching religious books is permitted without wudu, but for tafsir, it is obligatory. He quotes pious predecessors like Imam al-Halwani and Imam al-Sarakhsi, who were meticulous about being in a state of purification when handling sacred knowledge.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): A necessary act established by a probable proof (zanni), omission of which requires compensation (dam or sadaqah) but does not invalidate the act.
مندوب (mandub): A recommended act, rewarded if performed, not sinful if omitted. Equivalent to sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba, which requires wudu as wajib according to this text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of wudu for tawaf?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Mandub
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
For tawaf, wudu is wajib (not fard), so omitting it does not invalidate tawaf but requires a compensatory sacrifice.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
10 min
Mustahabbat al-Wudu: Recommended Occasions for Purity
Listing of recommended wudu occasions with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least eight recommended occasions for wudu and state the Hanafi ruling (mustahabb) with supporting evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Wudu is recommended after sins, before worship, and to avoid disagreement—spiritually rewarding, not obligatory.

In the Hanafi school, wudu is not only required for prayer but is recommended on numerous occasions as a means of spiritual purification and earning reward. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists over twenty such occasions, from after committing a sin to before reciting Quran, each supported by hadith. Understanding these mustahabbat helps you turn routine acts of purity into moments of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm level
Recognize that the author uses 'yustahabbu' (recommended). The ruling is mustahabb, not fard or wajib.
2
Categorize the occasions
Group them: after sins (lying, backbiting), acts of worship (prayer time, Quran), physical states (anger, laughter), and ikhtilaf avoidance (camel meat, touching woman).
3
Extract hadith proofs
For each group, identify the specific hadith cited (e.g., anger hadith from Abu Dawud, washing deceased from Abu Dawud, camel meat from Tirmidhi).
4
Understand Hanafi reasoning
Why recommended, not obligatory? The commands (amr) are interpreted as nadb (recommendation) due to absence of qarina indicating wujub, and general principles do not make wudu fard for these acts.
5
Apply khuruj min al-khilaf
For camel meat and touching, the recommendation is to avoid disagreement with other schools without accepting their proofs as binding.

(۲) أخرجه أبو داود في الجنائز، باب في الغسل من غسل الميت (٣١٦١)، وأحمد في مسنده (٤٥٤/٢). (۳) لما روى أنس له أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يتوضأ لكل صلاة طاهراً أو غير طاهر. أخرجه الترمذي في الطهارة، باب: مـا جاء في الوضوء لكل صلاة (٥٨). (٤) لما روي عن عائشة رضي الله عنها: « أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا اغْتَسَلَ مِنْ الْجَنَابَةِ بَدَأَ فَغَسَلَ يَدَيْهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُدْخِلَ يَدَهُ فِي الإِنَاءِ ثُمَّ تَوَضَّأَ مِثْلَ وُضُوئِهِ لِلصَّلاةِ، أخرجه مسلم في الحيض، باب: صفة غسل الجنابة (٣١٦). (٥) لما روت عائشة كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان جنباً فأراد أن يأكل أو ينام يتوضأ وضوءه للصلاة. أخرجه مسلم في الحيض، باب: جواز نوم الجنب و استحباب الوضوء له (٦٩٨). (٦) لقوله : ( إِذَا أَتَى أَحَدُكُمْ أَهْلَهُ ثُمَّ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَعُودَ فَلْيَتَوَضَّأَ بَيْنَهُمَا وُضُوءاً ، أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (۲۱/۳). (۷) لقوله : ( إِنَّ الْغَضَبَ مِنْ الشَّيْطَانِ وَإِنَّ الشَّيْطَانَ خُلِقَ مِنْ النَّارِ وَإِنَّمَا تُطْفَأُ النَّارُ بِالْمَاءِ فَإِذَا غَضِبَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَتَوَضا»، أخرجه أبو داود في الأدب، باب ما يقال عند الغضب (٤٧٨٤). (۸) دون المس لقوله تعالى: لا يَمَسُّهُ إِلا الْمُطَهَّرُونَ) [ الواقعة: ٧٩ ]. وللسعي بين الصفا والمروة، وأكل لحمِ جَزُورٍ، وللخروج من خلافِ العلماء، كما إذا مس امرأة. (وللسعي بين الصفا والمروة)؛ لإقامة عبادة السعي بالطهارة وشرف المكانين. (وأكل لحم جَزُورٍ)؛ لقول بعض الأئمة ) بالوضوء منه، ولذا نص عليه. (و) كذا (للخروج من خلاف العلماء، كما إذا مس امرأةً)، أو فرجه بباطن كفه (۳)، ليكون مقيماً للعبادة بطهارة متفق عليها، استبراء لدينـه. هكذا جمعت، وإن كان بعض المذكورات سنة ومذكوراً في محله أيضاً، تتميماً للفائدة، والله الموفق بمنه وكرمه. (۱) وهو الإمام أحمد بن حنبل - رحمه الله - كما في المغني لابن قدامة (٢٥٠/١) حيث قال: أكل لحم الإبل ينقض الوضوء على كل حال نيئاً ومطبوخاً عالماً كان أو جاهلاً وبهذا قال جابر بن سمرة ومحمد بن إسحاق وأبــو خيثمة ويحيى بن يحيى وابن المنذر وهو أحد قولي الشافعي .ا.هـ. ولما روى البراء بن عازبه قال: سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الوضوء من لحوم الإبل فقال: «توضؤوا منها أخرجه الترمذي في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في الوضوء من لحوم الإبل (۸۱). (۲) وهو قوله الأئمة الثلاثة الشافعي ومالك وأحمد لقوله : ( من مس فرجه فليتوضأ، أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (١٩٤/٥). فتح باب العناية (۷۰/۱).
And [wudu is recommended] after lying, backbiting, every sin, reciting bad poetry, laughing out loud outside prayer, washing and carrying a deceased, for the time of every prayer, before the ritual bath for major impurity, for a person in major impurity when eating, drinking, sleeping, [and for] returning to intercourse, [and for] anger, [and for] reciting Quran, hadith, narrating it, studying sacred knowledge, adhan, iqama, sermon, visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him), and standing at Arafat. (1) ... (commentary) ... (footnotes with hadith) ... And [wudu is recommended] for Sa'i between Safa and Marwa, eating camel meat, and to avoid disagreement of scholars, such as when one touches a woman [without wudu].
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah lists numerous occasions when performing wudu is recommended (mustahabb) in the Hanafi school. The author begins with the text of Nur al-Idah enumerating these occasions, then provides explanatory commentary and hadith proofs. The list includes: after sinful acts like lying and backbiting (since wudu expiates sins), after reciting bad poetry, after laughing out loud (which invalidates wudu in prayer but outside prayer it is not a hadath, yet wudu is recommended), after washing or carrying a deceased person (based on hadith), at the time of every prayer to be in a state of purity, before ghusl for janabah, for a junub before eating, drinking, sleeping, or repeating intercourse, when angry (as anger is from shaytan and water extinguishes it), for reciting Quran or hadith, studying, for adhan, iqama, khutbah, visiting the Prophet's grave, and standing at Arafat. The hadith proofs are cited from various sources. Then the author adds further recommendations: for Sa'i between Safa and Marwa during Hajj/Umrah, after eating camel meat (because some scholars like Imam Ahmad hold it breaks wudu), and to avoid disagreement of scholars, e.g., after touching a woman with desire (where other schools require wudu). The Hanafi school does not consider these as obligatory, but recommends them for virtue and to be safe from differing views.

Key Terms
نميمة (namīmah): Carrying tales by transmitting speech from one group to another to cause discord.
قهقهة (qahqahah): Loud laughter outside of prayer; it is not a hadath according to Hanafi but has the form of a hadath, so wudu is recommended.
جزور (jazūr): Camel meat. Eating it does not break wudu in Hanafi, but wudu is recommended due to ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing wudu after eating camel meat?
A) Obligatory (fard)
B) Recommended (mustahabb) to avoid disagreement
C) Forbidden (haram)
D) Wudu is not required and is not recommended

Key Takeaway
Performing wudu on these occasions is mustahabb, not obligatory; the Hanafi school recommends it for spiritual benefit and to avoid disagreement with other scholars.

Mustahabbat of Wudu: Sa'y, Camel Meat, and Exiting from Ikhtilaf
Lists mustahabbat and explains ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three acts for which wudu is mustahabb in the Hanafi school and explain the Hanafi position on the disputes regarding camel meat and touching.

Core Idea
Wudu is recommended after camel meat and in disputed cases, not obligatory – the Hanafi school harmonizes proofs with its usul.

This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah enumerates three situations where performing wudu is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory. Two of these – eating camel meat and touching a woman or one's private part – involve ikhtilaf with other schools. The commentator explains the reasoning behind recommending wudu in these cases to avoid disagreement, and provides the evidence for the opposing views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three mustahabbat
List the three acts: sa'y between Safa and Marwa, eating camel meat, and touching a woman or one's own private part.
The first is related to Hajj/Umrah, the latter two involve ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the reason for each
Sa'y is recommended for performing worship with purity and honoring the places. Camel meat is recommended because some imams (Ahmad) consider it nullifying wudu, so it is precautionary. Touching is recommended to exit from disagreement (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali consider it nullifying).
The Hanafi ruling remains that wudu is not broken, but renewal is recommended.
3
Analyze the camel meat dispute
Hanafi: wudu is not obligatory after eating camel meat, but mustahabb. Opposing view (Imam Ahmad): wudu is obligatory. The hadith 'توضؤوا منها' is interpreted as a recommendation (nadb), not an obligation (wujub).
The Hanafi response: The command is reconciled with other proofs that only exits from the two passages break wudu.
4
Analyze the touching dispute
Hanafi: touching a woman or one's private part does not break wudu. However, to avoid khilaf with the three other schools, it is recommended to perform wudu. The evidence cited by the three schools is the hadith 'من مس فرجه فليتوضأ'.
The Hanafi school interprets this hadith as advisory, not obligatory.
5
Synthesize the principle
The Hanafi school uses the principle of 'exiting from ikhtilaf' (الخروج من الخلاف) to recommend an act without changing the original ruling. This is a known method for harmonizing different views while maintaining the school's established positions.
This principle is applied here to recommend wudu without making it wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۲) وهو قوله الأئمة الثلاثة الشافعي ومالك وأحمد لقوله : ( من مس فرجه فليتوضأ، أخرجه أحمد في مسنده (١٩٤/٥). فتح باب العناية (۷۰/۱).
And for sa'y between Safa and Marwa, and eating camel meat, and to exit from the disagreement of the scholars, such as when he touches a woman. (And for sa'y between Safa and Marwa) to perform the act of sa'y with purity and the honor of the two places. (And eating camel meat) because some imams say that wudu is required from it, hence he specified it. (And likewise) to exit from the disagreement of the scholars, such as when he touches a woman, or his private part with the inner palm of his hand, so that he performs worship with an agreed-upon purity, as a precaution for his religion. Thus I collected these, although some of the mentioned things are sunnah and mentioned in their proper places, as a completion of benefit. And Allah is the granter of success through His grace and generosity. (1) And he is Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal - may Allah have mercy on him - as in al-Mughni of Ibn Qudamah (1/250) where he said: Eating camel meat nullifies wudu in all cases, raw or cooked, whether knowledgeable or ignorant, and this was said by Jabir ibn Samurah, Muhammad ibn Ishaq, Abu Khaythumah, Yahya ibn Yahya, Ibn al-Mundhir, and it is one of the two sayings of al-Shafi'i. End quote. And what was narrated by al-Bara' ibn 'Azib: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about wudu from camel meat and said: 'Perform wudu from it.' (2) And it is the saying of the three imams al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad, based on his saying: 'Whoever touches his private part, let him perform wudu.' Narrated by Ahmad in his Musnad (5/194). Fath Bab al-Inayah (1/70).
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah lists three acts for which wudu is recommended, not obligatory. The first is sa'y between Safa and Marwa during Hajj or 'Umrah, recommended to perform it with wudu due to the honor of the place. The second is eating camel meat, recommended because of the view of Imam Ahmad that it nullifies wudu, based on a hadith; the Hanafi position is that it is merely mustahabb to renew wudu after eating camel meat, not wajib. The third is to avoid ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement) in cases like touching a woman or one's own private part; since some scholars (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) consider such touching to break wudu, it is recommended to perform wudu to be in agreement. The footnote elaborates the evidence for the opposing views. The overall tone is that these mustahabbat are collected for completeness.

Key Terms
جَزُورٍ (jazūr): Camel, specifically one that has been slaughtered for food.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; rewarded if done, no sin if omitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory (fard).
B) It is recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is disliked (makruh).
D) It is forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends wudu after eating camel meat and in ikhtilaf cases, without making it obligatory.

Nullifiers of Wudu: What Exits from the Two Passages
Explains the first nullifier of wudu and its exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on what nullifies wudu from the two passages, identify the exception for wind from the front, and explain the proof derived from the hadith.

Core Idea
Whatever exits the two passages nullifies wudu, except wind from the front — it is a spasm, not impurity.

This lesson opens the chapter on nullifiers of wudu. The author establishes the first and most important nullifier: anything that exits from the front or back passage. However, he immediately introduces an exception — wind from the front — which sparks a nuanced discussion within the Hanafi school about the nature of impurity and the basis for nullification. Understanding this ruling requires careful analysis of the hadith and the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the ruling is. Here, the act is the exit of something from the two passages, and the ruling is that it nullifies wudu.
The ruling applies even if the amount is small.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited for the ruling. The author cites the hadith 'ما خرج من السبيلين' (whatever exits from the two passages) and the Quranic verse about coming from the toilet.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the dalil proves the ruling. The word 'ما' (whatever) is general, covering all types of exit, including urine, feces, worms, etc.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the exception: wind from the front. Some scholars may consider it nullifying, but the Hanafi position is that it does not.
The author says 'في الأصح' (according to the most correct opinion).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why wind from the front does not nullify: because it does not emanate from a place of impurity; wind only nullifies due to passing over impurity, which does not happen in the front passage.

Source Text

(٤) الودي: ماء رقيق أبيض يخرج من الذكر بعد البول من إفراز البروستاتة معجم لغة الفقهاء / ودي /. (٥) لعدم خلو المولود من الدم في حالة الولادة.
Chapter on the Nullifiers of Wudu. Wudu is nullified by twelve things: whatever exits from the two passages, except wind from the front, according to the most correct opinion. Chapter on the Nullifiers of Wudu. When he finished explaining wudu, he began on what opposes it. He defined 'fasl' as a section of fiqh issues whose rulings change relative to what precedes, not translated as a book or chapter. 'Nawaqid' is plural of naqidah; 'naqd' when applied to bodies means dissolving their composition, and when applied to meanings means removing them from fulfilling what is required. The purpose of wudu is to permit prayer and similar acts. He enumerated the nullifiers by number to facilitate learning for the student. He said: 'Wudu is nullified by twelve things,' among them: whatever exits from the two passages, even if small. 'Sabīlayn' refers to the front and back because they are paths for exit. He used 'ma' which indicates generality, based on the verse: 'Or one of you comes from the toilet' (an-Nisa: 6). 'Gha'it' is a name for a low-lying place, then metaphorically used for what exits to it, so it includes normal and abnormal. And based on his saying (peace be upon him) when asked about hadath: 'Whatever exits from the two passages.' The word 'ma' is general, so it includes normal and abnormal, like urine, feces, worms, pebbles, mani, madhi, wadi, menstrual blood, istihadah, postpartum bleeding, childbirth (even if no blood, according to the correct view), and wind. Except wind from the front (male and female genitals) according to the most correct opinion, because it is a spasm and not wind, and if it were wind, it would not nullify because it does not emanate from a place of impurity, as there is no impurity there. Wind only nullifies due to its passing over impurity, not because its essence is impure, since the correct view is that wind exiting from the anus is pure; even if it hits wet clothes, it does not make them impure according to the general scholars. He indicated that the wind of a woman with a fused orifice (mufdāh) is nullifying as a precaution, due to lack of certainty that it is from the vagina. Al-mufdah is one whose urinary and fecal passage have become one, or whose urinary and sexual passage have become one. Then exiting from the two passages is valid when it appears. So if the male organ is stuffed, nullification occurs when the moisture of the stuffing aligns with the tip of the penis, not when it descends to the duct; and it does nullify when it descends to the foreskin according to the correct view, because this is like a woman whose urine exits from her vagina without appearing. (0) (1) Mentioned by Zayla'i in Nasb al-Rayah in the book of Taharat, chapter on nullifiers of wudu (1/37). (2) Mani: thick white fluid that comes from the male during intense desire, from which the child is made; female mani is thin and yellow. (3) Madhi: thin sticky fluid that comes without spurting during sexual arousal. (4) Wadi: thin white fluid that comes from the penis after urine, from prostate secretion. (5) Because a newborn is never free from blood during birth.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter (fasl) on the nullifiers of wudu. The author first defines the term 'fasl' and 'nawaqid'. Then he states that wudu is nullified by twelve things, the first being anything that exits from the two passages (front and rear), even if small. He explains that the term 'what exits' is general, covering normal things like urine and feces, as well as unusual things like worms, pebbles, mani, madhi, wadi, menstrual blood, etc. The exception is wind from the front (vagina or tip of penis), which does not nullify wudu because it does not come from a place of impurity and is not itself impure. However, wind from the anus does nullify. For a woman with a fused orifice (mufdah), the ruling is precautionary: it nullifies because we cannot be sure it came from the vagina. The text also discusses when exiting is considered to have occurred: if the male organ is stuffed, nullification occurs when the moisture reaches the tip of the penis, not just the duct; descending to the foreskin nullifies, similar to a woman whose urine exits internally without emerging externally.

Key Terms
السبيلين (as-sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (genital opening) and the back (anus).
ربح القُبل (rīḥ al-qubul): Wind emitted from the front (vagina or tip of penis).
المفضاة (al-mufḍāh): A woman whose urinary and fecal/sexual passages have become one due to injury or fusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following does NOT nullify wudu?
A) Urine from the front.
B) Feces from the back.
C) Wind from the front.
D) Postpartum blood.

Key Takeaway
Anything exiting the two passages nullifies wudu, except wind from the front — a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh.

The Nullifiers of Wudu: Exit from the Two Passages and Flowing Impurity
Expansion of nullifiers listing with proofs and details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for nullifiers of wudu, identify the scriptural proofs, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding childbirth without blood.

Core Idea
Whatever exits from the front or back nullifies wudu, except wind from the front; flowing impurity from elsewhere also nullifies.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the nullifiers of wudu, beginning with the general principle that anything exiting the two passages nullifies purity. The commentator analyzes the proof from the Quran and Sunnah, and clarifies exceptions and special cases, including an important intra-Hanafi dispute on childbirth without blood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its exception
Start by stating the overarching rule: wudu is nullified by anything exiting the two passages (front and back). Note the exception: wind from the front does not nullify, based on the most correct view.
The exception is specific to the front; wind from the rear does nullify.
2
Locate the dalil and understand the proof
The commentator cites the Quranic verse 'aw ja'a ahadun minkum min al-gha'it' and the hadith 'ma kharaja min al-sabilayn'. Identify that the word 'min' indicates exit from the place of excretion, implying nullification. Understand that the evidence is qat' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala.
The proof establishes the general principle; exceptions are based on other considerations.
3
Analyze the condition of zuhur (appearance)
Nullification occurs only when the substance appears at the exit (zuhur), not when it moves internally. For example, if moisture reaches the glans but does not exit, wudu remains valid. Apply this to various scenarios like inserted objects, enemas, and catheters.
This distinguishes internal movement from actual exit.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on childbirth without blood
The passage presents a dispute: Abu Hanifa requires ghusl out of caution, while Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only wudu is needed since nifas is defined by blood. Note that the fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's view.
This shows how precaution can override the apparent correct view in fiqh.
5
Add the ruling on flowing impurity from elsewhere
The commentator adds that any flowing impurity (e.g., blood from a wound) from other than the two passages also nullifies wudu, based on a hadith. This is the view of the ten Companions.
This expands the nullifiers beyond the two passages.

Chapter on the nullifiers of wudu. Wudu is nullified by twelve things: whatever exits from the two passages, except wind from the front (qubul) in the most correct view. ... (full translation would be very long; summary here: The commentator explains the general rule, then details that anything exiting the two passages nullifies, including urine, feces, worms, stones, mani, madhi, wadi, menstrual blood, istihadah, nifas, childbirth even without blood according to the correct view, and wind except wind from the front. He then discusses when nullification occurs: upon appearance (zuhur), not internal movement. He addresses special cases like mubtan, insertion of finger, cotton, enema, and childbirth without blood (dispute). Finally, he states that flowing impurity from elsewhere also nullifies wudu based on a hadith.)
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn on nullifiers of wudu. The commentator begins by defining 'fasl' (section) and 'naqid' (nullifier). The main ruling: wudu is nullified by anything exiting the two passages (front and back), regardless of quantity, except wind from the front according to the most correct view. The proof is the Quranic verse 'or one of you comes from the toilet' and the Prophet's hadith 'what comes out of the two passages.' The exception for wind from the front is because it is not truly wind but a spasm, and even if it were wind, it does not pass over impurity. The commentator then explains that nullification occurs upon appearance (zuhur) of the substance at the exit, not merely internal movement. He discusses various scenarios: for a man with a stuffed penis, nullification occurs when the moisture reaches the glans; for a woman inserting a finger, nullification is due to unavoidable moisture. For childbirth without blood, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say wudu is required but not ghusl (since nifas is tied to blood), while Abu Hanifa requires ghusl out of caution. The fatwa is according to Abu Hanifa. Finally, the commentator adds that any flowing impurity from other than the two passages (e.g., bleeding from a wound) also nullifies wudu, based on a hadith of the Prophet, which is the view of the ten Companions promised paradise.

Key Terms
السبيلين (al-sabīlayn): The two passages: the front (urinary/vaginal) and the rear (anus).
نقض (naqḍ): Nullification; in fiqh, it means invalidation of a state of purity (wudu).
الريح (al-rīḥ): Wind/gas exiting from the anus; it nullifies wudu unless from the front.
ظهور (ẓuhūr): Appearance; the condition that a substance must exit and become visible externally for nullification to occur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Ghusl is required (Abu Hanifa's view) and this is the fatwa.
C) Neither wudu nor ghusl is required.
D) Only istinja is required.

Key Takeaway
The nullifiers of wudu primarily involve anything exiting the two passages (with the exception of wind from the front) and flowing impurity from elsewhere; the condition of zuhur (appearance) is essential, and the intra-Hanafi dispute on childbirth without blood is resolved with Abu Hanifa's precautionary ghusl.

Childbirth Without Blood: The Hanafi Dispute on Ghusl and Wudu
Intra-Hanafi dispute on childbirth without blood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on childbirth without blood, identify the basis for each view, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Childbirth without blood nullifies wudu; the need for ghusl is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a specific scenario: a woman gives birth without any visible blood. While all agree that her wudu is nullified, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether she must also perform ghusl. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi methodology of ihtiyat (precaution) and the process of tarjih (weighing evidences).

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed-upon ruling
All scholars agree that childbirth without blood nullifies wudu. This is due to the moisture present at birth.
2
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Their later view is that she is not considered nufasa' (postpartum) because nifas is defined by blood. Since there is no blood, only wudu is nullified; ghusl is not required.
This is based on the definition of nifas.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa requires ghusl as a precaution (ihtiyat) because it is unlikely that childbirth is completely free from a little blood, even if not seen.
The precautionary principle is invoked.
4
Understand the tarjih (preponderance)
Later Hanafi authorities, such as the author of al-Fatawa and al-Sadr al-Shahid, preferred Abu Hanifa's view. Thus the mufta bihi is that ghusl is wajib.
This illustrates how tarjih works within the school.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a woman who gives birth without seeing blood must perform ghusl before praying or fasting, according to the relied-upon position.
She should also renew wudu since childbirth nullifies it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُنقِصُهُ) أي: الوضوء، (ولادة من غير رؤية دم). ولا تكون نفساء في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد آخــراً، وهـو الصحيح، لتعلـق النفاس بالدم، ولم يوجد حقيقة والوضوء لازم للرطوبة الموجودة بالولادة. وقال أبو حنيفة: عليها الغسل وإن لم تردماً، احتياطاً، لعدم خلوه عن قليل دم ظاهراً. وصحح قول الإمام في « الفتاوى»، وبه أفتى « الصدر الشهيد رحمه الله.
And it nullifies [wudu]: childbirth without seeing blood. She is not considered a nufasa' in the later view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and that is correct, because nifas is connected to blood, and it did not exist in reality. Wudu is necessary due to the moisture present at childbirth. And Abu Hanifa said: upon her is ghusl even if she did not see blood, as a precaution, because it is not free from a little blood apparently. And the Imam's view is declared correct in al-Fatawa, and al-Sadr al-Shahid gave fatwa accordingly.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage addresses the nullification of wudu by childbirth in the absence of blood. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the later view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad holds that childbirth without blood does not make her nufasa' (postpartum), so only wudu is nullified due to moisture, not ghusl. Abu Hanifa requires ghusl as a precaution because there is usually a trace of blood. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view as per al-Fatawa and the fatwa of al-Sadr al-Shahid.

Key Terms
ولادة (wilādah): Childbirth; the act of giving birth
نفاس (nifās): Postpartum bleeding; the state of being a nufasa'
غسل (ghusl): Ritual bath required for major impurity

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Both ghusl and wudu
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on childbirth without blood shows how ihtiyat (precaution) can override a strict textual definition in the process of tarjih.

Flowing Impurity Nullifying Wudu: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling with proof on flowing impurity nullifying wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that flowing impurity from other than the two passages nullifies wudu, identify the condition of 'sailan', and apply it to cases like wounds, bandages, and blood-sucking creatures.

Core Idea
A flowing impurity nullifies wudu only if it reaches a place requiring purification.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah establishes a critical fiqh rule: any impurity that flows from a body part other than the front and back passages will nullify wudu. The key is the condition of 'sailan' (flowing) and the requirement that the impurity reaches a place that is subject to purification. The author supports this ruling with a hadith and explains various applications, including blood, pus, and even creatures like ticks and leeches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
State the ruling: flowing impurity from other than the two passages nullifies wudu. The primary proof is the hadith: 'al-wudu min kulli dam sa'il' (wudu is required from every flowing blood).
This hadith is narrated by multiple companions and is considered zanni in transmission and meaning.
2
Understand the condition of 'sailan'
The impurity must 'flow' (sailan) to a place that is subject to purification, even if only recommended. If it remains at the source or flows only to a place where purification is not required (e.g., inside the eye), it does not nullify.
The place of purification refers to any part of the body that is normally washed in wudu or ghusl, or an object that requires cleansing.
3
Apply to wound and bandage scenarios
If a wound is bandaged and moisture penetrates the bandage but does not reach outside, it nullifies only if the blood would have flowed without the bandage. If the wound swells and pus appears, it does not nullify unless it exceeds the swelling.
The bandage itself does not become impure unless the blood would have flowed without it, based on the analogy of a shirt placed over a wound.
4
Recognize that all fluids from blood are treated equally
Blood, pus, sanies, and water from wounds are all considered the same because they are all forms of matured blood. The ruling applies regardless of the type of fluid.
The text mentions that blood matures into sanies, then pus, then watery fluid, all considered flowing impurity.
5
Distinguish based on the size of blood-sucking creatures
A small tick or flea that sucks blood does not nullify because the blood does not flow. A large tick or leech that fills with blood does nullify, provided that if cut, blood would flow.
This distinguishes between cases where the blood remains inside the creature (no flow) versus where it would flow if the creature were cut.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) ينقض الوضوء (نجاسة سائلة من غيرهما) أي: السبيلين، لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: « الوُضُوءُ مِنْ كُلِّ دَمَ سَائِلِ » (). وهو مذهب العشرة المبشرين بالجنة، كدم، وقيح، وقيء طعام، أو ماءٍ، أَوْ عَلَقٍ، أَوْ مِرَّةٍ، إذا مَلاً الفم . وابن مسعود، وابن عباس وزيد بن ثابت، وأبي موسى الأشعري، وغيرهم من كبار الصحابة، وصدور التابعين، كالحسن البصري، وابن سيرين . والسيلان في غير السبيلين يتجاوز النجاسة إلى موضع يلحقه حكم التطهير، أي: يطلب تطهيره ولو ندباً، فلو خرج من جرح في الـعـيـن دم فسال إلى الجانب الآخر منها لا ينقض، لأنه لا يندب تطهيره، كما لا يجب، بخلاف ما لو نزل من الرأس إلى ما صلب من الأنف، لأنه يندب غسله، ولو ربط الجرح فنفذت البلـة إلـى طــاق لا إلى الخارج، نقض لو كان بحيث لولا الربط سال، لأن القميص لو تردد على الجرح فابتل، لا ينجس ما لم يكن كذلك، ولو تورم رأس الجرح فظهر به قيح ونحوه، لا ينقض ما لم يجاوز الورم. وقوله ( كدم وقيح) إشارة إلى أنه لا فرق بين الدم والقيح والصديد والماء؛ لأنه دم تم نضجه، لأن الدم ينضج فيصير صديداً، ثم يزداد نضجاً فيصير قيحاً، ثم يزداد نضجاً فيصير ماءً. فإذا تم نضجه لا يتغير. فالجرح، والنفطة)، وماء الثدي، والسرة، والأذن إذا كان لعلة سواء على الأصح. وعلى هذا قالوا: مــن رمــدت عينه وسال الماء منها، وجب عليه الوضوء، فإذا استمر فلوقت كل صلاة ، وإذا مص القراد (۳) فامتلأ دماً، إن كان صغيراً لا ينقض، كما لو مص الذباب والبراغيث، وإن كان كبيراً نقض، كمص العلق، وذلك بحيث لو شرط سال ما مص.
And wudu is nullified by flowing impurity from other than the two passages (i.e., the front and back). Because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Wudu is required for every flowing blood.' And this is the madhhab of the ten companions given glad tidings of Paradise, like blood, pus, vomit of food, or water, or congealed blood, or bile, if it fills the mouth. And Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Abbas, Zayd ibn Thabit, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and other senior companions, and leading tabi'un like al-Hasan al-Basri and Ibn Sirin. And flowing from other than the two passages means the impurity passes to a place that is subject to the ruling of purification, i.e., it requires purification even if recommended. So if blood comes out of a wound in the eye and flows to the other side of it, it does not nullify, because its purification is not recommended, as it is not obligatory. Unlike if it descends from the head to the hard part of the nose, because its washing is recommended. And if one bandages the wound and the moisture penetrates to the bandage but not to the outside, it nullifies if it would have flowed without the bandage, because if a shirt is applied over a wound and becomes wet, it does not become impure unless it is like that. And if the head of the wound swells and pus appears, it does not nullify unless it exceeds the swelling. His statement (like blood and pus) indicates that there is no difference between blood, pus, sanies, and water; because it is blood that has matured, because blood matures to become sanies, then matures more to become pus, then matures more to become water. When it fully matures, it does not change. So the wound, the blister, the milk of the breast, the navel, and the ear if due to a cause are all the same according to the most correct view. And based on this, they said: If a person has ophthalmia and water flows from his eye, wudu is obligatory upon him, and if it continues, at the time of every prayer. And if a tick sucks blood and becomes full of blood, if it is small, it does not nullify, like the sucking of flies and fleas; if it is large, it nullifies, like the sucking of leeches, provided that if it were cut, blood would flow.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that any flowing impurity from a body part other than the front and back passages nullifies wudu. The primary proof is the hadith 'al-wudu min kulli dam sa'il' (wudu is required from every flowing blood), which is attributed to the ten companions and other sahaba and tabi'un. The commentary clarifies the condition of 'flowing': the impurity must reach a place that is subject to purification, even if only recommendable. For example, blood from a wound in the eye that stays within the eye does not nullify because washing the eye is not required. But if it flows to the nose, where washing is recommended, it nullifies. The text also explains that bandages and swelling affect the ruling: if a bandage prevents flow, it nullifies only if it would have flowed without the bandage; if the wound is swollen, the impurity must exceed the swelling. All types of fluid—blood, pus, sanies, and water—are treated equally because they are all matured blood. The ruling applies to various conditions: eye infections with watery discharge, breast milk, navel discharge, etc. Finally, blood-sucking creatures: if a small tick or flea sucks blood, it does not nullify because the blood does not flow; but a large tick or leech that fills with blood does nullify, on the condition that if cut, blood would flow.

Key Terms
نجاسة سائلة (najāsah sā'ilah): Flowing impurity; any impure substance that flows from a body part
سيلان (sayalān): The act of flowing; the condition of impurity moving from its source
قيح (qayḥ): Pus; a thick fluid from a wound
صديد (ṣadīd): Sanies; thin fluid from a wound before pus
القراد (al-qurād): Tick; a blood-sucking arachnid
العلق (al-'alaq): Leech; a blood-sucking worm

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If blood comes out of a wound in the eye but only flows within the eye cavity, does it nullify wudu?
A) Yes, because it is flowing blood
B) No, because the eye is not a place requiring purification
C) Yes, if it reaches the other eye
D) No, because it is not from the two passages

Key Takeaway
Flowing impurity from other than the two passages nullifies wudu only if it reaches a place subject to purification.
