Ten Things That Do Not Nullify Wudu: The Hanafi Position and the Dispute on Touching Private Parts
Listing and explaining ten items that do not break wudu, with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the ten things that do not nullify wudu according to the Hanafi school, explain the principle of flow (sailan), and argue the Hanafi position on touching private parts using hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Touching private parts does not break wudu in the Hanafi school because it is like any other body part—proved by the Prophet's hadith.

The Hanafi school explicitly lists actions that do not nullify wudu, some of which are disputed by other schools. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah enumerates ten such items, with particular emphasis on touching private parts—a classic inter-madhhab disagreement. By studying this lesson, you will understand the Hanafi methodology of weighing hadith evidence and the crucial concept of flow (sailan) in nullification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-nullifiers and the flow principle
List the four items explicitly discussed: blood that does not flow, falling flesh without blood, worm from wound/ear/nose, and touching private parts. The key principle for blood, flesh, and worm is whether the substance flows (yasil) or not.
The text says 'dam lam yasil' (blood that does not flow) and 'min ghayr silan dam' (without blood flow).
2
Understand the Hanafi position on touching private parts
The Hanafi school holds that touching the penis, anus, or vagina does not break wudu, whether one's own or another's, with any part of the hand. This is based on the hadith: 'Is it not just a piece of you?'
The text cites the practice of many Companions and Tabi'un.
3
Identify the opposing school's proof
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Busra bint Safwan: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.' This hadith is found in Abu Dawud and others.
The text mentions that a group of scholars declared this hadith weak.
4
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal and tarjih
The Hanafis declare the Busra hadith weak (da'if) and prefer the stronger hadith of the Bedouin. They also cite the practice of the majority of Companions. Al-Tirmidhi declared the Bedouin hadith as the best in this chapter.
The text states 'قد ضعفه جماعة' (a group declared it weak).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
For Hanafis, wudu is not required after touching private parts; for Shafi'is, it is. This affects daily acts of worship like prayer.

(2) فصل عشرة أشياء لا تنقض الوضوء وهو وإن علم حكم أكثره من نواقض الوضوء، لكن ذكره نصاً وإن علم ضمناً، وحصـــره بـالـعد تقريباً على المتعلم فقال: (عشرة أشياء لا تنقض الوضوء ) منها : ( ظهور دم لم يسل عن محله)، لأنه لا يكون خارجاً، بل ظاهراً، ولا ينجس طاهراً، جامداً كان أو مائعاً، على الصحيح. (و) منها: (وسُقُوطُ لحم من غير سيلان دم، لطهارته، وانفصال الطاهر لا يوجب الوضوء، (كــالـعـرقِ المدني (2) الذي يقال له: رِشته بالفارسية لا يفسد الوضوء كما في « البزازية» وغيرها. (وَ) منها: (خُرُوجُ دُودةٍ مِنْ جُرْحٍ، وأُذُنِ، وأنف)، لعدم نجاستها، والرطوبة الـتـي بـها ليـس لـهـا قـوة السيلان، بخلاف خروجها من الدبر كما تقدم. (و) منها: (مس ذكر)، ودبر وفــرج سواء كان ذكره، أو ذكــر غيره، بباطن كفه، أو غيره وهو مذهب عمر بن الخطاب وعلي بن أبي طالب، وابن مسعود، وابن عباس، وزيد بن ثابت وغيرهم من كبار الصحابة، وصدور التابعين مثل الحسن البصري، وسعيد بن المسيب، والثوري. وقال الطحاوي رحمه الله : لم نعلم أحداً من الصحابة أفتى بالوضوء منـه غـيـر ابن عمر، وقد خالفه أكثرهم « لأن رسول الله الله جاءه رجل كأنه بدوي فقال: يا رسول الله، ما تقولُ في رجل مَسَّ ذَكَرَهُ في الصَّلاةِ؟ فقال: هلْ هُوَ إلا بضعةٌ مِنْكَ أو مُضْغَةً مِنْكَ؟ ، قال الترمذي: وهذا الحديث أحسن شيء في هذا الباب وأصح. وقد رواه غيره من الأكابر. وعن أبي أمامة الباهلي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام، سُئل عن مس الذكر فقال: « إِنَّمَا هُوَ جُزْءٌ مِنْكَ » . وأما حديـث بـســرة بنت صفوان، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَنْ مَسَّ ذَكَرَهُ فَلْيَتَوَضَا» (ه). فقد ضعفه جماعة. Chapter: Ten things that do not break ablution. Ten things do not break ablution: appearance of blood that does not flow from its place, falling of flesh without blood flow, like the Madani vein (which is called 'rishta'), exit of a worm from a wound, ear, or nose, and touching the penis. (2) Chapter: Ten things that do not break ablution. And although the ruling of most of them is known from the nullifiers of ablution, he mentioned it explicitly even if known implicitly, and enumerated them approximately for the student. He said: (Ten things do not break ablution.) Among them: (Appearance of blood that does not flow from its place) because it is not exiting but appearring, and it does not make a pure thing impure, whether solid or liquid, according to the correct view. (And) among them: (Falling of flesh without blood flow) because it is pure, and the separation of pure does not necessitate ablution, like the Madani vein (which in Persian is called 'rishta') does not invalidate ablution as in al-Bazzaziyya and others. (And) among them: (Exit of a worm from a wound, ear, and nose) because it is not impure, and the moisture on it does not have the quality of flowing, unlike its exit from the anus as previously mentioned. (And) among them: (Touching the penis) and anus and vagina, whether one's own or another's, with the inner palm or otherwise. This is the madhhab of Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali ibn Abi Talib, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, Zayd ibn Thabit, and other great Companions, and leading Tabi'un like al-Hasan al-Basri, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, and al-Thawri. Al-Tahawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We do not know any Companion who gave a fatwa requiring wudu from it except Ibn Umar, and the majority opposed him. Because a man who seemed like a Bedouin came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and said: O Messenger of Allah, what do you say about a man who touches his penis during prayer? He said: Is it not just a piece of you or a lump of you? Tirmidhi said: This hadith is the best and most authentic thing in this chapter. Others among the great scholars also narrated it. And from Abu Umamah al-Bahili that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about touching the penis and said: It is only a part of you. As for the hadith of Busra bint Safwan that the Messenger of Allah said: Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu, a group of scholars declared it weak.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and ruling statement on ten things that do not nullify wudu. The author lists them: 1) blood that appears but does not flow, because it is not exiting and does not transfer impurity; 2) falling of flesh without bleeding (e.g., the Madani vein/rishta); 3) exit of a worm from a wound, ear, or nose, because it is not impure and its moisture does not flow; nullification only if it exits from the anus; 4) touching the penis, anus, or vagina, whether one's own or another's, with any part of the hand. The author then provides evidence from the Prophet's hadith that the penis is just a part of the body, so touching it does not necessitate wudu. A strong hadith is cited, while the opposing hadith (Busra) requiring wudu is declared weak. The author notes the consensus of the Companions, with only Ibn Umar dissenting. This establishes the Hanafi position that touching the private parts does not break wudu.

Key Terms
مس الذكر (mass al-dhakar): Touching the penis with the hand, which according to the Hanafi school does not nullify wudu.
دم لم يسل (dam lam yasil): Blood that appears on the surface but does not flow from its place; it is not considered a nullifier.
عرق مدني (‘irq madani): A Madani vein: a small fleshy protrusion that emerges from the skin like a worm, common in Medina.

Three Non-Nullifiers of Wudu: Blood, Flesh, Worm
Listing and explaining first three non-nullifiers of wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three specific things that do not break wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain why each one is not a nullifier.

Core Idea
Blood that does not flow, flesh detached without blood, and worm from a wound do not break wudu.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on Nur al-Idah's list of ten things that do not invalidate wudu. We focus on the first three: blood that appears but does not flow, a piece of flesh that falls off without accompanying blood flow, and a worm that exits from a wound, ear, or nose. Understanding these exceptions clarifies the Hanafi criterion for nullification of wudu by exiting substances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
Recognize that the passage enumerates things that do not break wudu. The general principle is that wudu remains valid unless a specific nullifier occurs.
The author explicitly lists ten items for ease of learning.
2
Analyze the first case: non-flowing blood
Understand that blood that appears on the skin but does not flow (lam yasil) from its place is not a nullifier. The key condition is the absence of flow (sayalan).
If blood flows, it breaks wudu because it is considered exiting the body.
3
Analyze the second case: falling flesh
A piece of flesh that detaches without blood flowing with it is pure (tahir). Since the detached item is pure and not impure, its separation does not necessitate wudu.
Example given: 'al-'irq al-madani' (Madani vein/skin tag) is pure and does not invalidate wudu.
4
Analyze the third case: worm from wound
A worm exiting from a wound, ear, or nose does not break wudu because the worm itself is not impure (najis), and the moisture on it does not have the power of flow.
Exception: if the worm exits from the anus, it breaks wudu because of the impurity of its source.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(و) منها: (وسُقُوطُ لحم من غير سيلان دم، لطهارته، وانفصال الطاهر لا يوجب الوضوء، (كــالـعـرقِ المدني (٢) الذي يقال له: رِشته بالفارسية لا يفسد الوضوء كما في « البزازية» وغيرها. (وَ) منها: (خُرُوجُ دُودةٍ مِنْ جُرْحٍ، وأُذُنِ، وأنف)، لعدم نجاستها، والرطوبة الـتـي بـها ليـس لـهـا قـوة السيلان، بخلاف خروجها من الدبر كما تقدم.
Section: Ten things that do not break wudu. Ten things do not break wudu: Appearance of blood that did not flow from its place, and falling of flesh without blood flow, like the Madani vein which is called 'rishta' in Persian, and exit of a worm from a wound, ear, and nose, and touching the penis. And although he knows the ruling of most of them from the nullifiers of wudu, but he mentions it textually although known implicitly, and its enumeration by counting is for approximation for the learner. So he said: (Ten things do not break wudu). Among them: (Appearance of blood that did not flow from its place), because it is not exiting, rather apparent, and it does not make a pure thing impure, whether solid or liquid, according to the correct view. (And) among them: (Falling of flesh without blood flow), due to its purity, and detachment of a pure thing does not necessitate wudu, like the Madani vein (2) which is called 'rishta' in Persian, it does not invalidate wudu as in al-Bazzaziyyah and others. (And) among them: (Exit of a worm from a wound, ear, and nose), due to it not being impure, and the moisture on it does not have the power of flowing, unlike its exit from the anus as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is an expansion probe (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah. The author lists the first three of ten things that do not break wudu according to the Hanafi school. The first is blood that appears but does not flow from its place. The key point is that if blood appears on the surface (e.g., from a scratch) but does not flow, it does not invalidate wudu. This is because it is not considered 'exiting' the body, and it does not render something impure. The second is the falling of a piece of flesh without blood flowing with it. Since the flesh itself is pure (tahir), its detachment does not necessitate wudu. An example given is the 'Madani vein' (a skin tag or small piece of flesh common in Medina). The third is the exit of a worm from a wound, ear, or nose. Worms are not impure (najis), and the moisture on them is not sufficient to flow, so wudu remains intact. However, if a worm exits from the anus, that is different because it comes from a source of impurity and may be accompanied by moisture that breaks wudu. The passage also notes the wisdom of enumerating these items: although students may already know the ruling from understanding the nullifiers, the explicit list is for ease of learning.

Key Terms
لم يسل (lam yasil): did not flow: means the blood appears on the skin but does not move or spread from its spot
العرق المدني (al-'irq al-madani): a small piece of flesh like a vein that appears on the skin in Medina, called 'rishta' in Persian

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only if the blood is in liquid form.
D) Only if the blood originates from the private parts.

Key Takeaway
Blood must flow to break wudu; flesh falling without blood and worms from wounds do not break wudu.

Touching the Penis Does Not Break Wudu: Hanafi Proof and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Hanafi ruling and evidence for touching the penis not breaking wudu, with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that touching the penis does not break wudu, identify the key hadith evidence, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument from the hadith of Busrah.

Core Idea
Touching the penis is like touching any other body part; it does not break wudu.

In this lesson, we examine a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: whether touching the genital organs nullifies wudu. The Hanafi school holds that it does not, citing a hadith where the Prophet compared the penis to a mere piece of the body. The Shafi'i school relies on a hadith commanding wudu after touch. We will explore the proofs and how the Hanafi school resolves the conflict.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by clearly stating that in the Hanafi school, touching the penis (or anus or vagina) does not break wudu. Washing the hand is recommended but not required.
2
Identify the supporting evidence
The primary dalil is the hadith where the Prophet said, 'Is it but a piece of you?' – a rhetorical question indicating no purification is needed. Also note the consensus of many Companions as reported by al-Tahawi.
The hadith is narrated by al-Tirmidhi and others.
3
Consider the opposing evidence
The opposing school (Shafi'i) relies on the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan: 'Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu.'
This hadith is considered weak by many scholars.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by declaring the Busrah hadith weak, and even if authentic, it is interpreted as recommendation (mustahabb) to wash the hand, as stated in al-Mabsut.
The recommendation is analogous to the hadith about washing before and after food.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: In the Hanafi school, wudu remains valid after touching; in the Shafi'i school, wudu is invalidated and must be renewed for prayer.
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) منها: (مس ذكر)، ودبر وفــرج سواء كان ذكره، أو ذكــر غيره، بباطن كفه، أو غيره وهو مذهب عمر بن الخطاب وعلي بن أبي طالب، وابن مسعود، وابن عباس، وزيد بن ثابت وغيرهم من كبار الصحابة، وصدور التابعين مثل الحسن البصري، وسعيد بن المسيب، والثوري. وقال الطحاوي رحمه الله : لم نعلم أحداً من الصحابة أفتى بالوضوء منـه غـيـر ابن عمر، وقد خالفه أكثرهم « لأن رسول الله الله جاءه رجل كأنه بدوي فقال: يا رسول الله، ما تقولُ في رجل مَسَّ ذَكَرَهُ في الصَّلاةِ؟ فقال: هلْ هُوَ إلا بضعةٌ مِنْكَ أو مُضْغَةً مِنْكَ؟ ، قال الترمذي: وهذا الحديث أحسن شيء في هذا الباب وأصح. وقد رواه غيره من الأكابر. وعن أبي أمامة الباهلي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام، سُئل عن مس الذكر فقال: « إِنَّمَا هُوَ جُزْءٌ مِنْكَ » . وأما حديـث بـســرة بنت صفوان، أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَنْ مَسَّ ذَكَرَهُ فَلْيَتَوَضَا» (0). فقد ضعفه جماعة. ولكن يستحب لمن مس ذكره أن يغسل يده. صرح به صاحب ( المبسوط وهـو أحـد مـا حـمـل عـلـيـه حديث بسرة فقال: أو المراد غسل اليد استحباباً، كما في قوله: « الوضوءُ قَبْلَ الطَّعَامِ يَنْفِي الفَقْرَ، وَبَعْدَهُ ينْفِي المَمَ )
(And) among them: (Touching the penis), anus, and vagina, whether it is his own or another's, with the inner palm or other, and this is the madhhab of Umar ibn al-Khattab, Ali ibn Abi Talib, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, Zayd ibn Thabit and other senior Companions, and the leading Tabi'un like al-Hasan al-Basri, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, and al-Thawri. And al-Tahawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We do not know any Companion who gave a fatwa of wudu from it besides Ibn Umar, and the majority opposed him. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was approached by a man who seemed like a bedouin and said: O Messenger of Allah, what do you say about a man who touched his penis during prayer? He said: Is it but a piece of you or a morsel of you? At-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is the best and most authentic in this chapter. Others among the greats have also narrated it. And from Abu Umamah al-Bahili that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about touching the penis and said: It is only a part of you. As for the hadith of Busrah bint Safwan that the Prophet said: Whoever touches his penis, let him perform wudu, a group of scholars declared it weak. But it is recommended for whoever touches his penis to wash his hand. The author of al-Mabsut stated this, and this is one of the interpretations on which the hadith of Busrah is carried, meaning that the intended meaning is washing the hand as a recommendation, just as in his saying: Wudu before food repels poverty, and after it repels insanity.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of touching the penis breaking wudu. The author first states that touching the penis (or anus or vagina) does not break wudu, whether one touches his own or another's, and whether with the palm or other part. He then provides the evidence and lists the Companions and early scholars who held this view, including major figures like Umar, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn Abbas, and Zayd ibn Thabit. He quotes al-Tahawi who noted that no Companion except Ibn Umar gave a fatwa of wudu from touching. The primary Hanafi proof is the hadith where the Prophet said the penis is just a piece (bughda) or morsel (mudgha) of the body, implying it is like any other limb. The hadith of Busrah bint Safwan commanding wudu is declared weak (da'if) by many scholars. However, the Hanafi school still recommends washing the hand after touching, as stated in al-Mabsut, to reconcile the Busrah hadith as a recommendation. This is similar to the concept of wudu before and after food being recommended for cleanliness, not ritual purity.

Key Terms
مس الذكر (mass adh-dhakar): touching the male genital organ
بضعة (bud'a): a piece of flesh, used in the hadith to refer to the penis as a normal body part

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on touching the penis during prayer?
A) Wudu is broken immediately.
B) Wudu remains valid, but it is makruh.
C) Wudu remains valid, and it is recommended to wash the hand.
D) The prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Touching the penis does not break wudu in the Hanafi school; the opposing hadith is weak or interpreted as a recommendation to wash the hand.

Touching a Woman Does Not Break Wudu
Hanafi ruling and proof from sunnah and Quran for touching not breaking wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching a woman and wudu, explain the sunnah and Quranic proofs, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Mere touch does not break wudu; only sexual intercourse nullifies purity in the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that touching a woman, even a non-mahram, does not break wudu unless there is sexual discharge. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's practice and a nuanced interpretation of the Quran. You will learn the key proofs and understand why the Hanafi school differs from others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
State the Hanafi rule: touching a woman (including non-mahram) does not break wudu. Note the exception: sexual intercourse does.
The Hanafi school defines 'touching' as mere skin contact, not intercourse.
2
Analyze the Sunnah Proof
Examine the hadith from Aisha: the Prophet used to kiss his wives and then pray without wudu. Why does this prove the ruling? Because it's a direct action showing that such contact does not nullify purity.
The hadith is recorded in the four Sunan and is considered authentic.
3
Interpret the Quranic Verse
Look at the verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' (or you have touched women). The Hanafi school, following Ibn Abbas, interprets 'lamasa' as sexual intercourse, not mere touch. Why? Because Allah uses euphemism for intimate acts. Support from divorce verse (al-Baqarah 237) where 'tamassuhunna' clearly means intercourse.
This interpretation is key to the Hanafi position.
4
Understand the Ikhtilaf
Recognize that Shafi'i school holds that touching a woman with desire breaks wudu. Their proof is a literal reading of the Quran and a different hadith. The Hanafi response: the hadith is weak or pertains to recommended wudu.
The practical difference (thamarah): Hanafi says no wudu, Shafi'i says wudu required.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position mufta bihi? Because the sunnah proof is clear and the Quranic interpretation is consistent and supported by Ibn Abbas, a prominent companion.
The Hanafi school prioritizes the actual prophetic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) منها: (مَسَّ امْرَأَةٍ غير محرم، لما في السنن الأربعة عن عائشة : وكان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «كَانَ يُقبلُ بَعْضَ أَزْوَاجِهِ ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي، ولا يَتَوَضاء ، وأما الآية، فقد قال ابن عباس : المراد باللمس الجماع ، لأن الله تعالى حبي كنى بالحسن عن القبيح، كما كنى باللمس عن الجماع في قوله تعالى: وَإِن طَلَقْتُمُوهُنَّ مِن قَبْلِ أَن تَمَسُّوهُنَّ) (البقرة: ۲۳۷) والمراد الجماع.
(And) among them: (Touching a woman other than a mahram), because in the four Sunan from Aisha: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to kiss some of his wives then pray without performing wudu. As for the verse, Ibn Abbas said: The intended meaning of touching (al-lams) is sexual intercourse, because Allah the Exalted used euphemism for the base act with a pure expression, just as He used touching (al-lams) euphemistically for intercourse in His saying: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them' (al-Baqarah 237), where the intended meaning is intercourse.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling that touching a woman, even a non-mahram (except sexual intercourse), does not break wudu. The proof is from the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who would kiss his wives and then pray without renewing wudu, as recorded in the four Sunan. Regarding the Quranic verse (4:43) 'or you have touched women' (aw lamastum al-nisa'), the Hanafi school, following Ibn Abbas, interprets 'lamasa' as sexual intercourse, not mere touch. This is supported by the verse in Surah al-Baqarah where 'tamassuhunna' (touch them) clearly means intercourse in the context of divorce. Thus, mere skin contact without sexual discharge does not break wudu.

Key Terms
اللمس (al-lams): In this context, interpreted as sexual intercourse by Hanafi school, not mere touch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what evidence from the Quran is used to support that touching a woman does not break wudu?
A) The verse 'aw lamastum al-nisa' is interpreted as sexual intercourse.
B) The verse 'wa in kuntum junuban fa-tahharu'.
C) The verse 'fa-lam tajidu ma'an fa-tayammamu'.
D) The verse 'wa la taqrabu al-zina'.

Key Takeaway
Mere touch does not break wudu; only sexual intercourse nullifies purity in the Hanafi school.

Five Cases That Do Not Break Wudu (Hanafi)
Rulings on five non-nullifiers of wudu with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five exceptions where wudu remains valid and derive the ruling for each based on the evidence provided.

Core Idea
Not all sleep or vomit nullifies wudu — the Hanafi school distinguishes light sleep and non-impure substances.

The Hanafi school provides detailed exceptions to the nullifiers of wudu. This passage clarifies five situations where wudu remains intact: vomit less than a mouthful, phlegm (even abundant), leaning sleep, deep seated sleep, and sleep during prayer in the sunnah posture. Understanding these protects against unnecessary repetition of wudu.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first case: vomit less than a mouthful
Read the ruling on vomit (qay') that does not fill the mouth. Note the reason: it comes from the upper stomach and is not impure.
Mouthful is defined as what fills the mouth; less than that does not nullify.
2
Identify the second case: phlegm (balgham)
Phlegm is viscous and not permeated by impurity, so it does not break wudu even if abundant.
Phlegm is distinguished from stomach vomit.
3
Examine the third case: leaning sleep (tama'il)
A sleeping person whose seat might move but is not fully lying down. The hadith of the Companions shows nodding off does not break wudu.
Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi: Companions slept waiting for Isha and prayed without wudu.
4
Analyze the fourth case: deep seated sleep (nawm mutamakkin)
Sleep while seated firmly on the ground, even if leaning. The posterior is stable, so wind is unlikely to escape.
Intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no break; al-Quduri and al-Tahawi say it breaks. The mufta bihi is the former.
5
Understand the fifth case: sleep in prayer in sunnah posture
Sleep while bowing or prostrating in the recommended posture (arms away, belly separated) does not break wudu inside or outside prayer.
The hadith: wudu is only obligatory when lying down because joints relax.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) منها: (قي: لا يَمْلأُ القَمَ)، لما تقدم، ولكونه ليس نجساً، لأنه من أعلى المعدة. (وَ) منها : (قَيءُ بَلْغَم، وَلَوْ كَثِيراً) لأنه لزج لا تتداخله النجاسة (و) منها: (تَمَائِلُ نَائِمٍ احْتُمِلَ زَوَالُ مَقْعَدَتِهِ)، لما في سنن أبي داود: «كَانَ أصحابُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنتَظِرُونَ العشاء حتى تخفق رؤوسهم ثمَّ يصلون ولا يتوضؤونَ». (وَ) منها: (نَــوم مُتَمَكِّن) من الأرض، (وَلَوْ) كان (مُستنداً إلى شيءٍ)، كحائط وسارية ووسادة، بحيث (لو أُزيل) المستند إليه (سَقط) الشخص، فلا ينتقض وضوءه عَلَى الظَّاهِر ) من مذهب أبي حنيفة (فيهما) أي: في المسألتين، هذه والتي قبلها، أما دليل الأولى فقد تقدم، والثانية: فلأن مقعدته مستقرة على الأرض، فيأمن خروج شيء منه فلا ينتقض وضوءه. رواه أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة، وهو الصحيح وبـه أخـذ عـامـة المشايخ، وذكر « القدوري » أنه ينتقض ، وهو مروي عن «الطحاوي». (وَ) منها: (نومُ مُصَلَّ، ولو) نـام (رَاكِعاً أو ساجداً) إذا كان ( عَلَى جِهَةِ)، أي: صفة ( السُّنّة)، في ظاهر المذهب بأن أبدى ضبعيه، وجــافـي بطنه عن فخذيه؛ لقوله : ( لا يَجِبُ الوُضُوءَ على مَنْ نَامَ جَالِسَاً أو قَائِمَاً أَو سَاجِدًا، حَتَّى يَضَعَ جَنبَهُ، فإذا اضطجع استرخت مفاصله )، وإذا نام كذلك خارج الصلاة، فلا ينتقض وضوءه في الصحيح. وإن لم يكن على هيئة السجود، والركوع المسنون، انتقض وضوءه
(And) among them: (Vomit that does not fill the mouth), due to what preceded, and because it is not impure since it is from the upper stomach. (And) among them: (Vomit of phlegm, even if abundant), because it is viscous, impurity does not permeate it. (And) among them: (Leaning of a sleeping person that makes it possible that his sitting place could move), because in Sunan Abi Dawud: The Companions of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to wait for the Isha prayer until their heads nodded, then they prayed and did not perform wudu. (And) among them: (Deep sleep while seated firmly on the ground, even if leaning on something) like a wall, pillar, or cushion, such that if the support is removed, the person would fall. Then his wudu is not broken according to the apparent (zahir) view of Abu Hanifah in both matters. As for the proof of the first, it has preceded; and for the second: because his posterior is firmly on the ground, so he is secure from something exiting from him, so his wudu is not broken. Abu Yusuf narrated this from Abu Hanifah, and it is the correct view, and most mashayikh adopted it. Al-Quduri mentioned that it breaks, and it is narrated from al-Tahawi. (And) among them: (Sleep of a praying person, even if he sleeps while bowing or prostrating) if it is in the manner (sunnah posture) according to the apparent madhhab, by displaying his armpits and separating his belly from his thighs, because of his saying: 'Wudu is not obligatory on one who sleeps sitting, standing, or prostrating until he lies on his side. When he lies down, his joints relax.' And if he sleeps in this manner outside prayer, his wudu is not broken according to the correct view. But if he is not in the sunnah posture of prostration and bowing, his wudu breaks.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage covers the remaining items from the list of ten things that do not break wudu. First, vomit that is less than a mouthful does not break wudu because it is from the upper stomach and is not considered impure (najis). Second, phlegm (balgham), even if abundant, does not break wudu because it is viscous and does not allow impurity to permeate it. Third, a sleeping person who is leaning (tama'il) such that his seat could move but he is not fully lying down — the Companions used to nap while waiting for Isha and then pray without wudu. Fourth, deep sleep (nawm mutamakkin) where one is seated firmly on the ground, even if leaning on something that if removed would cause him to fall, does not break wudu according to the apparent (zahir) view of Abu Hanifah, narrated by Abu Yusuf. This is the correct view and adopted by most scholars, although al-Quduri and al-Tahawi held that it does break. Fifth, sleep during prayer while in the position of ruku' or sujud, if done in the sunnah posture (arms away from sides, belly separated from thighs), does not break wudu. The hadith indicates that wudu is required only when lying down because the joints relax. This applies both inside and outside prayer. If the sleeper is not in the sunnah posture, his wudu breaks because his sitting is not stable.

Key Terms
قيء (qay'): vomit; here it is distinguished by quantity (less than mouthful) and source (upper stomach)
نوم متمكن (nawm mutamakkin): deep sleep while seated firmly on the ground, even if leaning but stable
بلغم (balgham): phlegm; viscous secretion from the chest
تمائل (tama'il): leaning or swaying of a sleeping person such that his seat might shift

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following breaks wudu?
A) Vomit of phlegm, even if abundant.
B) Sleep while prostrating in the sunnah posture.
C) Vomit from the stomach that fills the mouth.
D) Deep sleep while sitting firmly on the ground.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wudu remains valid for less-than-mouthful vomit, phlegm, leaning sleep, deep seated sleep, and sleep in prayer in sunnah posture—only lying down sleep or mouthful stomach vomit nullify.

Eight Actions That Do Not Break Wudu (Hanafi)
Lists eight nullifiers that do not break wudu with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight actions that do not break wudu according to the Hanafi school and explain the evidence for at least two of them.

Core Idea
Fixed sleep and touching a woman without desire do not break wudu – uncertainty of wind or intent matters.

This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah clarifies common misconceptions about wudu nullifiers. The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings based on hadith and qiyas, distinguishing between actions that definitively break wudu and those that do not. Understanding these exceptions prevents unnecessary repetition of wudu and deepens your grasp of Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify each action
List the eight actions mentioned in the passage: touching a woman, vomiting less than mouthful, phlegm, swaying sleep, fixed sleep, sleep in Sunnah posture, and the recommendation to wash hands after touching the penis (as a separate sunnah).
The passage also mentions a recommendation but it is not a nullifier.
2
Locate the proof for each
For each action, find the dalil cited: hadith for touching, reasoning for vomit/phlegm, hadith of Companions for swaying sleep, narration from Abu Yusuf for fixed sleep, and hadith about sleep postures.
Some proofs are explicit hadith, others are qiyas or istihsan.
3
Note intra-Hanafi differences
Focus on fixed sleep: Abu Hanifa (via Abu Yusuf) says it does not break wudu; al-Quduri and al-Tahawi say it does. The correct view adopted by most mashayikh is non-breakage.
This difference arises from whether the seat being fixed guarantees no wind release.
4
Extract the mufta bihi ruling
For each action, determine the operative ruling for fatwa: all eight actions do NOT break wudu. The recommendation to wash hands after touching the penis is separate.
The mufta bihi is clear from the text: 'on the apparent view' and 'the correct view'.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Use the principles to evaluate whether a given situation breaks wudu: e.g., does touching a mahram break? (No). Does vomiting a mouthful? (Yes, because fills mouth). Does sleeping on a chair while leaning? (Fixed sleep if seat stable).
The key is the presence of wind release or impurity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومس امرأة، وقيء لا يملا الفم، وقي بلغم، ولو كثيراً، وتمايل نائم احْتُمِلَ زوالُ مَقْعَدَتِهِ، ودوم متمكن، ولَوْ مُسْتَئِداً إلى شيء، لو أُزِيلَ سَقَطَ على الظّاهِر فيهما. ونومُ مُصَلِّ، ولوْ رَاكِعاً، أو ساجداً، على جهة السنة. والله الموفق.
ولكن يستحب لمن مس ذكره أن يغسل يده. صرح به صاحب ( المبسوط وهو أحد ما حمل عليه حديث بسرة فقال: أو المراد غسل اليد استحباباً، كما في قوله: « الوضوءُ قَبْلَ الطَّعَامِ يَنْفِي الفَقْرَ، وَبَعْدَهُ ينْفِي المَمَ ) (و) منها: (مَسَّ امْرَأَةٍ غير محرم، لما في السنن الأربعة عن عائشة : وكان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «كَانَ يُقبلُ بَعْضَ أَزْوَاجِهِ ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي، ولا يَتَوَضاء ، وأما الآية، فقد قال ابن عباس : المراد باللمس الجماع ، لأن الله تعالى حبي كنى بالحسن عن القبيح، كما كنى باللمس عن الجماع في قوله تعالى: وَإِن طَلَقْتُمُوهُنَّ مِن قَبْلِ أَن تَمَسُّوهُنَّ) (البقرة: ۲۳۷) والمراد الجماع. (و) منها: (قي لا يَمْلأُ القَمَ)، لما تقدم، ولكونه ليس نجساً، لأنه من أعلى المعدة. (وَ) منها : (قَيءُ بَلْغَم، وَلَوْ كَثِيراً) لأنه لزج لا تتداخله النجاسة (و) منها: (تَمَائِلُ نَائِمٍ احْتُمِلَ زَوَالُ مَقْعَدَتِهِ)، لما في سنن أبي داود: «كَانَ أصحابُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنتَظِرُونَ العشاء حتى تخفق رؤوسهم ثمَّ يصلون ولا يتوضؤونَ». (وَ) منها: (نَــوم مُتَمَكِّن) من الأرض، (وَلَوْ) كان (مُستنداً إلى شيءٍ)، كحائط وسارية ووسادة، بحيث (لو أُزيل) المستند إليه (سَقط) الشخص، فلا ينتقض وضوءه عَلَى الظَّاهِر ) من مذهب أبي حنيفة (فيهما) أي: في المسألتين، هذه والتي قبلها، أما دليل الأولى فقد تقدم، والثانية: فلأن مقعدته مستقرة على الأرض، فيأمن خروج شيء منه فلا ينتقض وضوءه. رواه أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة، وهو الصحيح وبـه أخـذ عـامـة المشايخ، وذكر « القدوري » أنه ينتقض ، وهو مروي عن «الطحاوي». (وَ) منها: (نومُ مُصَلَّ، ولو) نـام (رَاكِعاً أو ساجداً) إذا كان ( عَلَى جِهَةِ)، أي: صفة ( السُّنّة)، في ظاهر المذهب بأن أبدى ضبعيه، وجــافـي بطنه عن فخذيه؛ لقوله : ( لا يَجِبُ الوُضُوءَ على مَنْ نَامَ جَالِسَاً أو قَائِمَاً أَو سَاجِدًا، حَتَّى يَضَعَ جَنبَهُ، فإذا اضطجع استرخت مفاصله ) ()، وإذا نام كذلك خارج الصلاة، فلا ينتقض وضوءه في الصحيح. وإن لم يكن على هيئة السجود، والركوع المسنون، انتقض وضوءه ( والله الموفق) بمحض فضله وكرمه.
And touching a woman, and vomiting that does not fill the mouth, and vomiting phlegm even if much, and the swaying of a sleeper whose seat may move, and fixed sleep even if leaning on something such that if removed he would fall, on the apparent [view] in both. And the sleep of a praying person, even if bowing or prostrating, in the manner of the Sunnah. And Allah is the granter of success. But it is recommended for one who touches his penis to wash his hand. The author of al-Mabsut explicitly stated it, and it is one interpretation of the hadith of Busrah: he said the intent is washing the hand as a recommendation, as in the saying: 'Wudu before food removes poverty, and after it removes [?]'. And among them: touching a woman not a mahram, due to what is in the four Sunan from Aisha: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) used to kiss some of his wives then pray without performing wudu.' As for the verse, Ibn Abbas said: the meaning of 'touch' is intercourse, because Allah Almighty, with His wisdom, expressed the indecent by the decent, just as He used 'touch' euphemistically for intercourse in His saying: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them' (al-Baqarah: 237), and the meaning is intercourse. And among them: vomiting that does not fill the mouth, due to what preceded, and because it is not impure, as it is from the upper stomach. And among them: vomiting phlegm even if much, because it is viscous, impurity does not penetrate it. And among them: the swaying of a sleeper whose seat may move, due to what is in Sunan Abu Dawud: 'The companions of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) used to wait for Isha until their heads nodded, then they would pray without performing wudu.' And among them: fixed sleep on the ground, even if leaning on something like a wall, pillar, or cushion, such that if the support were removed, the person would fall; then his wudu is not broken on the apparent [view] from the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. In both issues—this and the one before—as for the proof of the first, it has preceded; and the second, because his seat is fixed on the ground, so he is safe from anything exiting him, so his wudu is not broken. Abu Yusuf narrated it from Abu Hanifa, and it is the correct view, and most mashayikh adopted it. Al-Quduri mentioned that it is broken, and that is narrated from al-Tahawi. And among them: the sleep of a praying person, even if sleeping while bowing or prostrating, if it is in the manner (i.e., description) of the Sunnah, according to the apparent madhhab: by extending his upper arms and keeping his belly away from his thighs; due to his saying: 'Wudu is not obligatory for one who sleeps sitting, standing, or prostrating, until he lies down on his side, for when he lies down, his joints relax.' If he sleeps like that outside the prayer, his wudu is not broken according to the correct view. If he is not in the posture of the prostrating or bowing according to Sunnah, his wudu is broken. And Allah is the granter of success, by His pure grace and generosity.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section listing cases that do NOT break wudu according to the Hanafi school. The author of Sharh explains each case from the matn. First, touching a woman without lust is not a nullifier; the proof is from the practice of the Prophet. The verse about 'touching women' is interpreted as intercourse. Second, vomit that does not fill the mouth does not break wudu because it is not impure. Third, phlegm even in large quantity does not break wudu due to its viscosity. Fourth, swaying sleep where the seat might move does not break wudu, as per the hadith of the Companions nodding. Fifth, fixed sleep on the ground or leaning on something that if removed would cause a fall—the correct Hanafi position is that it does not break wudu, narrated by Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa, though al-Quduri and al-Tahawi hold it breaks. Sixth, the sleep of a praying person in the Sunnah posture of ruku' or sujud does not break wudu; otherwise, it breaks. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each item and the evidence.

Key Terms
تَمَاكُن (tamakkun): Fixed sleep on the ground or a surface where the seat is stable
تَمَايُل (tamayul): Swaying or tilting of a sleeper where the seat might shift

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following breaks wudu?
A) Touching a non-mahram woman without desire
B) Vomiting a mouthful of phlegm
C) Sleeping while sitting firmly on the ground without leaning
D) Sleeping lying on one's side

Key Takeaway
Wudu remains valid after touching a woman without desire, fixed sleep, vomiting less than a mouthful, swaying sleep, and sleep in Sunnah posture.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Introduction to Ghusl and Its First Cause: Emission of Maniy
Opening the chapter on obligatory ghusl, this passage defines ghusl and janabah, then lists the first of seven causes: emission of maniy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ghusl linguistically and technically, identify the first cause of obligatory ghusl (maniy), and explain why the cause is sometimes treated as a condition in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory upon emission of maniy with desire; this emission causes janabah, which blocks permissible acts until purification.

This passage opens the chapter on obligatory ghusl by clarifying the linguistic and technical definitions of ghusl and janabah, then lists the first of seven causes: emission of maniy. Although the author calls these 'causes', the commentary explains they are actually conditions of obligation—a subtle but important distinction in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between the cause of janabah and the cause of ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and scope
The passage defines the term 'ghusl' and enumerates its causes. Note that the author first clarifies terminology before listing the seven causes.
Ghusl is a comprehensive washing of the body with pure water.
2
Distinguish cause versus condition
The commentary explains that the so-called 'causes' (like emission of maniy) are actually conditions for obligation, not causes. In Hanafi usul, a cause (sabab) directly necessitates the ruling, while a condition (shart) is a prerequisite for the ruling to apply.
The author uses metaphorical language to simplify for learners.
3
Define maniy and its legal implication
Maniy is defined as a thick white fluid emitted with desire. Its emission triggers janabah, a state of major impurity that requires ghusl before prayer and other acts.
Janabah is both a state and a legal impediment (mani).
4
Understand the pillar (rukn) of ghusl
The passage states the pillar is to wash the entire body as far as possible without hardship. The minimal obligation is to ensure water reaches every part once.
Multiple washings are sunnah, not fard.
5
Summarize the ruling and its practical effect
Ghusl is obligatory (fard ayn) for janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding. Its effect is to make permissible what was prohibited (e.g., prayer, touching the Quran).
The seven causes are listed elsewhere; this lesson focuses on the first.

Source Text

باب ما يوجب الاغتسال
يُفْتَرَضُ الغُسْلُ بواحد من سبعةِ أَشياء: خروجُ المَنِي ..
باب ما يوجب الاغتسال
ما يوجب: يعني يلزم الاغتسال، لما كان سبب وجوب الغسل مختلفاً فيـه تبـع ظاهر عبارة الهداية) بجعله إنزال المني ونحوه سبباً، لقوله: المعاني الموجبة للغسل: إنزال المني إلخ، لأنـه أظهر وأسهل للمتعلم، وإن كانت هذه المعاني شروطاً للوجوب، لا أسباباً، فإضافة الوجوب إلى الشروط مجاز كقولهم: صدقة الفطر؛ لأن السبب يتعلق به الوجود والوجوب، والشرط يضاف إليـه الوجود، فشارك الشرط السبب في الوجود، وإن اعترض على ( الهداية» بأن هذه المعاني موجبة للجنابة لا للغسل، على المذهب الصحيح عن علمائنا فإنها تنقضه، فكيف توجبه؟ فقد رد بأن المراد وجوب الغسل بهذه المعاني على طريق البدل، وإنما يتوجه ما اعترض به إذا كانت هذه المعاني موجبة لوجود الغسل، لا لوجوبه، ورد أيضاً بأنها تنقض ما كان، وتوجب مــا سيكون، فلا منافاة، ولذا كان الأولى أن يقال: سبب الغسل وجوب ما لا يحل مع الجنابة أو إرادته، وإن لم يجب. واعلم أن الكلام على الغسل في تفسيره لغة، وشريعة، وسببه، وشرطه، وركنه، وسننه، و آدابـه وصفته، وحكمه. أما تفسيره لغة: فهو بالضم اسم من الاغتسال، وهو تمـام غسل الجسد، واسم للماء الذي يغتسل به أيضاً. والضم هو الذي يستعمله الفقهاء أو أكثرهم، لأنه يجوز فتح الغين، كضمها، والفتح أفصح وأشهر عند أهل اللغة واصطلاحاً: غسل البدن بالماء الطهور من جنابة، أو حيض أو نفاس. والجنابة في اللغة: حالة تحصل عند خروج المني على وجه الشهوة، فيصيـر مـن قامت به جنباً. يقال: أجنب الرجل إذا قضى شهوته من المرأة. وأما سببه فقد علمته بأنه إرادة ما لا يحل مع الجنابة أو وجوبه. وأما شرائطه فتنقسم إلى قسمين شروط وجوب، وشروط صحة، كما علمتها في الوضوء. وأما ركنه فعُموم ما أمكن من الجسد من غير حرج بالماء الطهور. وأما سننه: فسنذكرها كالوضوء قبله، وأما آدابه فكما في الوضوء ويــزاد مـا ستعلمه قريباً، وأمـا صفتـه فـهـو فرض في الجنابة والحيض والنفاس، وسنة للجمعة ونحوها، ومندوب لمن بلغ بالسن ونحـوه كـمـا ستعلمه، وأما حكمه فحل ما كان ممتنعاً قبله، والثواب في الآخرة بفعلـه تقـربـاً. ثـم إنـه حـصـر موجبات الغسل مع وصفه بقوله: (يُفْتَرَضُ الغُسْلُ بواحد ) يحصل للإنسان ( من سبعة أشياء). منها: (خروج المني)، وهو ماء أبيض ثخين ينكسر به الذكر عند خروجه، يشبه رائحة الطلـع
Chapter on what makes ghusl obligatory. Ghusl is obligatory by one of seven things: emission of maniy... Chapter on what makes ghusl obligatory. 'Makes obligatory' means it necessitates ghusl. Since the cause of obligation of ghusl is disputed, the author of al-Hidayah followed the apparent wording by making maniy and similar things the cause, saying: 'The meanings that necessitate ghusl: emission of maniy, etc.' because it is clearer and easier for the learner, even if these meanings are conditions for obligation, not causes. So attributing obligation to conditions is metaphorical, like saying 'zakat al-fitr'; because the cause is related to existence and obligation, while the condition is related to existence only, so the condition shares with the cause in existence. If one objects to al-Hidayah that these meanings necessitate janabah, not ghusl, according to the correct madhhab of our scholars, since they nullify the state of purity, how can they necessitate it? The reply is that what is meant is the obligation of ghusl through these meanings by way of substitution; the objection only applies if these meanings necessitate the existence of ghusl, not its obligation. It is also replied that they nullify what was, and obligate what will be, so there is no contradiction. Therefore, it would be better to say: the cause of ghusl is the obligation of what is not permissible with janabah, or the intention thereof, even if not obligatory. Know that the discussion on ghusl concerns its linguistic and shar'i definitions, its cause, conditions, pillar, sunnas, etiquettes, description, and ruling. As for its linguistic definition: it is, with damm, a noun from ightisal, meaning the complete washing of the body, and also the water used for washing. The damm is what the fuqaha use, mostly, because it is permissible to open the ghayn like its damma, but the fatha is more eloquent and famous among linguists. And in terminology: washing the body with tahur water from janabah, or menstruation, or postpartum bleeding. Janabah linguistically: a state that occurs upon emission of maniy with desire, so the one in that state becomes junub. It is said: a man becomes junub when he fulfills his desire from a woman. As for its cause, you have learned that it is the intention of what is not permissible with janabah or its obligation. As for its conditions, they are divided into two categories: conditions of obligation and conditions of validity, as you learned in wudu. As for its pillar, it is the general washing of the body as far as possible without difficulty with tahur water. As for its sunnas, we will mention them like wudu before it. As for its etiquettes, they are as in wudu, with additional aspects you will soon learn. As for its description, it is obligatory for janabah, menstruation, and postpartum bleeding; sunnah for Friday and the like; and recommended for one who reaches puberty by age or similar, as you will learn. As for its ruling, it is the permissibility of what was previously forbidden, and reward in the hereafter for doing it as an act of worship. Then he enumerated the causes of ghusl with their description, saying: 'Ghusl is obligatory by one of seven things' that occur to a person: among them, 'emission of maniy', which is a thick white fluid that causes the penis to break [subside] upon its exit, resembling the smell of pollen.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-ruling section opening the chapter on obligatory ghusl. The author clarifies terminology: the causes of ghusl are sometimes called causes but are actually conditions of obligation. He explains the linguistic and technical definitions of ghusl and janabah. The seven causes are listed, but only the first is detailed: emission of maniy, defined as a thick white fluid exiting with desire. The commentary then discusses each aspect of ghusl: cause, conditions, pillar, sunnas, etiquettes, description, and ruling. The author follows the order of the matn, explaining the first cause and providing necessary definitions.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing the entire body with tahur water for ritual purification
الجنابة (al-janabah): A state of ritual impurity that results from emission of maniy or intimacy
المني (al-maniy): A thick white fluid emitted with desire

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Washing the entire body three times
B) Washing the entire body once
C) Washing the entire body with intention
D) Washing the entire body except the hair

Key Takeaway
Emission of maniy with desire causes janabah and obligates ghusl, which requires washing the entire body once with pure water.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Obligation of Ghusl Due to Emission of Maniy: The Condition of Shahwa
Explains ruling and conditions for ghusl due to maniy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when ghusl becomes obligatory due to maniy, explain the essential condition of shahwa, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its timing.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory only when maniy exits with desire; without shahwa, no ghusl.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, opens the chapter on what necessitates ghusl. It focuses on the first of the seven causes: the emission of maniy (semen). The text clarifies that the key factor is sexual desire (shahwa) at the moment of emission. It then presents an important intra-Hanafi debate between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other regarding whether shahwa must persist until the maniy exits the body or only at the initial separation from the spine. The passage also includes the prophetic evidence from the hadith of Umm Sulaym and Hawla bint Hakim, and provides practical examples and fatwa guidelines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is the emission of maniy (semen). The ruling is that ghusl becomes fard (obligatory) due to this emission, but only under specific conditions.
The text considers maniy as a cause (sabab) for ghusl, though technically it is a condition (shart) for janaba.
2
Locate the essential condition
The condition for ghusl to be obligatory is that the maniy exits with shahwa (sexual desire). Without desire, ghusl is not required. The text explicitly states this and gives examples like being struck on the spine or carrying something heavy.
Shahwa is the key differentiating factor. Other schools may also require dafaq (gushing), but Hanafi relies on shahwa.
3
Trace the dalil (evidence)
The evidence is from two hadiths: Umm Sulaym asked about ghusl for a woman after a wet dream, and the Prophet said 'Yes, if she sees water.' Similarly, Hawla bint Hakim asked, and the Prophet said 'No ghusl until she emits, just as a man does not have ghusl until he emits.' These ahadith establish that ghusl is tied to the actual emission of fluid ('seeing water' or 'emitting').
The dalil is ahad (non-mutawatir), but its meaning is definitive (qati' al-dalala) in requiring ghusl upon emission with desire.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute about the timing of shahwa. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require shahwa only at the moment the maniy separates from the spine. Abu Yusuf requires shahwa to persist until the maniy actually exits the body. This difference leads to practical consequences in scenarios like holding the penis until desire subsides.
This is a legitimate differing within the madhhab, not a contradiction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text states that the fatwa is on the view of Abu Yusuf for a guest who is shy or fears suspicion, and on the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) for everyone else. This shows a context-dependent tarjih.
The fatwa is differentiated based on necessity (darura) and ease (taysir).

Source Text

ونحوها، ومندوب لمن بلغ بالسن ونحوه كما ستعلمه، وأما حكمه فحل ما كان ممتنعاً قبله، والثواب في الآخرة بفعله تقرباً. ثم إنه حصر موجبات الغسل مع وصفه بقوله: (يُفْتَرَضُ الغُسْلُ بواحد) يحصل للإنسان ( من سبعة أشياء). منها: (خروج المني)، وهو ماء أبيض ثخين ينكسر به الذكر عند خروجه، يشبه رائحة الطلع، (۱) (الطلع: أول ما يثمر من النخل ثم يخرج منه التمر المبسوط للسرخس (١٧٥/١٢) ) إلى ظاهر الجسد، إذا انفصل عن مقره بشهوة، من غير جماع.. ومني المرأة رقيق أصفر إلى ظاهر الجسد، لأنه ما لم يظهر لا حكم له (إذا انفصل عن مقره)، يعني: الصلب (بشهوة)، وكان خروجه ( من غير جماع)، كأن حصل باحتلام، ولو كان أول ما حصل، كبلوغ صبي في الأصح، أو عبث أو فكر، أو نظر، وشرط الشهوة في خروجه، فأغنى عن ذكر الدفق، لأنه إذا وجدت الشهوة كان بدفق، وإذا لم توجد الشهوة عند خروجه، لا يوجب الغسل عندنا، كما إذا ضرب من على صلبه، أو حمل شيئاً ثقيلاً، فنزل منه مني بلا شهوة. ويشترط وجود الشهوة عند انفصاله من الصلب، ولا يشترط دوامها إلى انفصاله إلى ظاهر الفرج عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، خلافاً لأبي يوسف. والمرأة فيه كالرجل في ظاهر الرواية وبه يؤخذ، وقيل: يلزمها الغسل بالاحتلام من غير رؤية ماء إذا وجدت اللذة، لأن ماءها ينزل من صدرها إلى رحمها، بخلاف الرجل، وحيث يشترط ظهور المني منه حقيقة، وجه ظاهر الرواية « أن أم سليم، جاءت إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فقالت: يا رسول الله، إن الله لا يستحي من الحق، هل على المرأة من غسل إذا هي احتلمت؟ فقال: نعم إذا رأت الماء». وكذا «عن حولة بنت حكيم أنها سألت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن المرأة ترى في منامها ما يرى الرجل فقال: ليس عليها غسل حتى تنزل، كما أن الرجل ليس عليه غسل حتى ينزل». وثمرة الخلاف فيما تقدم، تظهر فيما لو أمسك ذكره، أو ربطه، حتى سكنت شهوته، ثم أرسله، فنزل المني، لزمه الغسل عندهما لا عند أبي يوسف، وفيما إذا أمنى بشهوة واغتسل من ساعته، وصلى ثم خرج بقية المني، عليه الغسل عندهما لا عند أبي يوسف، ولا يعيد الصلاة بالإجماع، لأنه اغتسل للأول، ولا يجب الغسل للثاني إلا بعد خروجه، ولو خرج بعدما بال وارتخى ذكره، أو نام، أو مشى خطوات كثيرة، لا يجب عليه الغسل اتفاقاً؛ لأن ذلك يقطع مادة المني الزائل عن مكانه بشهوة، فيكون الثاني زائلاً بغير شهوة، ولو خرج منه بعد البول، وذكره منتشر، وجب الغسل، والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف في الضيف إذا استحيا من أهل البيت، أو خاف أن يقع في قلبهم ريبة، بأن طاف حول بيتهم، وعلى قولهما في غير الضيف. وإذا لم يتدارك مسك ذكره حتى نزل المني، صار جنباً بالاتفاق، فإذا خشي الريبة، يتستر بإيهام أنه يصلي، بغير قراءة، ونية، وتحريمة، فيرفع يديه، ويقوم، ويركع شبه المصلي.
Chapter on What Necessitates Ghusl. 'What necessitates' means: it makes ghusl obligatory. Since the cause of obligation of ghusl is disputed, [the author] followed the apparent expression of al-Hidayah by making the emission of maniy and the like a cause, because it is more apparent and easier for the learner, even if these meanings are conditions for obligation, not causes. Attributing obligation to conditions is metaphorical, like saying 'zakat al-fitr', because the cause is attached to existence and obligation, while the condition is added to existence, so the condition shares with the cause in existence. If one objects to al-Hidayah that these meanings necessitate janaba (ritual impurity) not ghusl, according to the correct madhhab from our scholars, for they nullify it, so how can they necessitate it? It is replied that what is meant is the obligation of ghusl by these meanings in a substitutive way; the objection would only apply if these meanings necessitated the existence of ghusl, not its obligation. It is also replied that they nullify what was [before] and obligate what will be, so there is no contradiction. Hence it is better to say: the cause of ghusl is the obligation of something not permitted in a state of janaba, or its intention, even if not obligatory. Know that the discussion of ghusl covers its linguistic and legal definition, its cause, condition, pillar, sunnan, etiquettes, description, and ruling. As for its linguistic definition: it is, with a damma, a noun meaning complete washing of the body, and also a name for the water used for washing. The damma is what the jurists or most of them use, because it is permissible to open the ghayn, like damma, but the fatha is more eloquent and famous among linguists. Technically: washing the body with pure water from janaba, menstruation, or postnatal bleeding. Janaba linguistically: a state occurring when maniy emerges with desire, so the person becomes junub. It is said: 'ajnab al-rajul' if he fulfills his desire from a woman. As for its cause, you have learned it: the intention of what is not permissible in a state of janaba or its obligation. Its conditions are divided into two types: conditions of obligation and conditions of validity, as you learned in wudu. Its pillar is: complete coverage of what is possible of the body without difficulty with pure water. Its sunnan: we will mention them, like wudu before it. Its etiquettes: as in wudu, with addition of what you will learn shortly. Its description: it is obligatory in janaba, menstruation, and postnatal bleeding; sunna for Friday and the like; and recommended for one who reaches puberty by age and the like, as you will learn. Its ruling: the permissibility of what was forbidden before it, and reward in the Hereafter by doing it as an act of worship. Then he restricted the necessitators of ghusl with his description saying: 'Ghusl is prescribed as obligatory by one of seven things.' Among them: 'The emission of maniy', which is a thick white water that causes the penis to break [i.e., become erect] at its exit, similar in smell to the pollen of the date palm (al-tala: first what fruits from the palm then exit the scattered dates, according to al-Sarakhsi) to the exterior of the body, when it separates from its place with desire, without intercourse. And a woman's maniy is thin and yellow to the exterior of the body, because as long as it does not appear, it has no ruling. (When it separates from its place) i.e., the spine (with desire), and its exit (without intercourse), such as by a wet dream, even if it is the first time, like a boy reaching puberty in the soundest opinion, or by playing, thinking, or looking. The condition of desire in its exit dispenses with mentioning dafaq (gushing), because when desire exists, it occurs with a gush. If desire does not exist at its exit, it does not necessitate ghusl in our school, such as if one is struck on his spine or carries something heavy and maniy comes out without desire. The presence of desire at its separation from the spine is required, but its persistence until it separates to the exterior of the private part is not required according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. A woman is like a man in the apparent narration, and it is adopted. It is said: ghusl is required from her by wet dream without seeing water if she finds pleasure, because her water descends from her chest to her uterus, unlike a man, as the apparent narration requires the actual appearance of maniy from her. The evidence for the apparent narration is: that Umm Sulaym came to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and said: 'O Messenger of Allah, Allah is not shy of the truth. Is there ghusl upon a woman if she has a wet dream?' He said: 'Yes, if she sees water.' Similarly, it is reported from Hawla bint Hakim that she asked the Prophet, peace be upon him, about a woman who sees in her dream what a man sees, and he said: 'There is no ghusl upon her until she emits, just as there is no ghusl upon a man until he emits.' The fruit of the disagreement previously mentioned appears in the case where he held his penis or tied it until his desire subsided, then released it, and maniy came out: ghusl is required from him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), not according to Abu Yusuf. And in the case where he ejaculated with desire, performed ghusl immediately, prayed, then the remainder of maniy came out: ghusl is required from him according to the two, not according to Abu Yusuf, and he does not repeat the prayer by consensus, because he performed ghusl for the first, and ghusl is not required for the second until after it comes out. If it comes out after he urinated and his penis became flaccid, or he slept, or walked many steps, ghusl is not required from him unanimously, because that cuts the flow of maniy that left its place with desire, so the second is exiting without desire. If it comes out after urination while his penis is erect, ghusl is required. The fatwa is on the opinion of Abu Yusuf in the case of a guest who is shy of the household or fears that suspicion may fall in their hearts, [such that he] circumambulates their house, and on their opinion (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) in other than the guest. If he does not grasp his penis in time until maniy comes out, he becomes junub by agreement. If he fears suspicion, he may conceal himself by pretending to pray without recitation, intention, or takbir tahrima, raising his hands, standing, and bowing like a praying person.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, opens the chapter on what necessitates ghusl. The author first discusses terminology: whether the enumerated items are causes or conditions for the obligation of ghusl, following al-Hidayah in calling them causes for simplicity. He then provides comprehensive definitions of ghusl linguistically and legally, its cause, conditions, pillar, sunnan, etiquettes, description, and ruling. The main topic is the first of the seven things necessitating ghusl: the emission of maniy (semen). The text defines maniy, its characteristics, and the essential condition of shahwa (sexual desire). Importantly, ghusl is only obligatory if maniy exits with desire, even if not from intercourse (e.g., wet dream, thinking, looking). If maniy exits without desire (e.g., due to a blow or heavy lifting), ghusl is not required in the Hanafi school. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require shahwa only at the moment the maniy separates from the spine, but not necessarily until it exits the body; Abu Yusuf requires shahwa to persist until exit. The text then addresses the ruling for women, citing two hadiths: Umm Sulaym's question about ghusl after a wet dream, and Hawla bint Hakim's similar question. The Prophet replies that women must have ghusl if they see water (i.e., emission). The practical consequence (thamara) of the dispute is illustrated: if a man holds his penis to prevent ejaculation and then releases it, ghusl is required according to the two imams but not Abu Yusuf. Similarly, if after ghusl and prayer, residual maniy exits, a second ghusl is required according to the two. The fatwa is situational: for a guest who is embarrassed or fears suspicion, the fatwa follows Abu Yusuf (no ghusl required if he did not have full desire at exit), while in other cases, the fatwa follows the two imams. The passage ends with advice for one who becomes junub and fears suspicion: pretend to pray without actual prayer to avoid detection.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniy): A thick white fluid (semen) that exits with desire from a man, and a thin yellow fluid from a woman; its emission with desire necessitates ghusl.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing the entire body with pure water to remove ritual impurity (janaba, menstruation, postnatal bleeding).
الشهوة (al-shahwa): Sexual desire; a condition for the emission of maniy to necessitate ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following scenarios requires ghusl?
A) A man carries a heavy box and feels moisture on his thigh, which he discovers is maniy.
B) A woman has a wet dream and finds a yellowish fluid on her underwear.
C) A man urinates and notices a drop of white fluid after finishing, without any desire.
D) A person is splashed with water that they think might be impure.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of ghusl from maniy is contingent upon the presence of shahwa at the time of emission; the exact timing of shahwa is disputed within the school with practical fatwa differentiation.

Conditions for Ghusl from Semen and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Desire
Explains conditions for ghusl and intra-Hanafi dispute on desire duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for ghusl due to semen emission, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the duration of desire, and apply the ruling to specific scenarios.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory when semen exits with desire, but the duration of desire required is disputed among Hanafi imams.

This lesson examines the conditions that make ghusl obligatory due to semen emission. The Hanafi school requires that semen exits with sexual desire and reaches the surface of the body. However, a key disagreement arises between the founders: does desire need to persist until the semen exits the private part, or is desire at the moment of separation from the backbone sufficient? Understanding this subtle point has real consequences for when ghusl is required.

Guided Path
1
State the three main conditions for ghusl from semen
Identify from the text: semen must reach the surface of the body, separate from the backbone with desire, and occur without intercourse.
These conditions narrow the general ruling that ghusl is fard after seminal emission.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require desire at the moment of separation from the backbone only. Abu Yusuf requires desire to persist until the semen exits the private part.
This is an ikhtilaf within the same madhhab.
3
Examine the evidence and reasoning for each position
Both sides rely on the same hadith but interpret 'desire' differently. The text states that desire implies gushing (dafq), which suffices for the majority. Abu Yusuf sees the term 'shahwa' as a continuous condition.
No explicit hadith is cited for the duration; the dispute is over linguistic implication.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequences)
Work through the scenarios given: holding the penis until desire subsides then releasing (ghusl for majority, not for Abu Yusuf); residual semen after first ghusl (new ghusl for majority, not for Abu Yusuf).
The dispute matters because it affects when a person must repeat ghusl or perform wudu and prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The text gives a context-sensitive fatwa: for a guest who may face social suspicion, Abu Yusuf's view is taken (to avoid hardship); for others, the majority view applies.
This is a classic Hanafi tarjih based on the principle of removing hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

( مِنْ غَيْرِ جماعِ)، كأن حصل باحتلام، ولو كان أول ما حصل، كبلوغ صبي في الأصح، أو عبث أو فكر، أو نظر، وشرط الشهوة في خروجه، فأغنى عن ذكر الدفـــق، لأنه إذا وجدت الشهوة كان بدفق، وإذا لم توجد الشهوة ومحمد، خلافاً لأبي يوسف. والمرأة فيه كالرجل في ظاهر الرواية وبه يؤخذ ، وقيل : يلزمها الغسل بالاحتلام من غير رؤية ماء إذا وجدت اللذة، لأن ماءها ينزل من صدرها إلى رحمها، بخلاف الرجل، وحيث يشترط ظهور المني منه حقيقة، وجه ظاهر الرواية « أنَّ أم سليم ، جاءت إلى النبي ، فقالت: يا رسول الله، إنَّ اللهَ لا يستحي مِنَ الحقِّ، هَلْ عَلَى المَرْأَةِ مِنْ غُسلِ إِذَا هِي احْتَلَمَتْ؟ فَقَالَ: نَعَمْ إِذَا رَأتِ المَاءَ». وكذا «عَنْ حَوْلَةَ بنت حكيم أَنَّهَا سَأَلَتِ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنِ المَرْأَةِ تَرى فِي مَنَامِهَا مَا يَرَى الرَّجُلُ فَقَالَ: لَيْسَ عَلَيْهَا غُسل حتَّى تُنزِلَ، كَمَا أَنَّ الرَّجلَ ليسَ عليه غسل حتَّى يُنْزِلَ ) (). وثمرة الخلاف فيما تقدم، تظهر فيمـا لـو أمسك ذكره، أو ربطه، حتى سكنت شهوته، ثم أرسله، فنزل المني، لزمه الغسل عندهما لا عند أبـي يوسف، وفيما إذا أمنى بشهوة واغتسل من ساعته، وصلى ثم خرج بقية المني، عليه الغسل عندهما لا لد أبي يوسف، ولا يعيد الصلاة بالإجماع، لأنه اغتسل للأول، ولا يجب الغسل للثاني إلا بعد خروجه، ولو خرج بعدما بال وارتخى ذكره، أو نــام، أو مشى خطوات كثيرة، لا يجب عليه الغسل اتفاقاً؛ لأن ذلك يقطع مادة المني الزائل عن مكانه بشهوة، فيكون الثاني زائلاً بغير شهوة، ولـو خــرج منه بعد البول، وذكره منتشر ، وجب الغسل، والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف في الضيف إذا استحيا من أهل البيت، أو خاف أن يقع في قلبهم ريبة، بأن طاف حول بيتهم، وعلى قولهما في غير الضيف. وإذا لم يتدارك مسك ذكره حتى نزل المني، صار جنباً بالاتفاق، فإذا خشي الريبة، يتستر بإيهام أنه يصلي، بغير قراءة، ونية، وتحريمة، فيرفع يديه، ويقوم، ويركع شبه المصلي.
To the surface of the body, when it separates from its place with desire, without intercourse. And the woman's semen is thin and yellow. (To the surface of the body) because as long as it does not appear, there is no ruling. (When it separates from its place) meaning the backbone (with desire), and its exit (without intercourse), as if it occurs by wet dream, even if it is the first time it occurs, like the puberty of a boy according to the most correct opinion, or by playing, thinking, or looking. And the condition of desire in its exit dispenses with mentioning gushing, because when desire is present, it is with gushing, and when desire is not present at its exit, it does not necessitate ghusl according to us, as if he is struck on his backbone or carries something heavy, and semen descends from him without desire. And the existence of desire at its separation from the backbone is required, but its continuance until its separation to the surface of the private part is not required according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And the woman is like the man in the apparent narration, and it is adopted. And it is said: ghusl is obligatory upon her by wet dream without seeing water if she finds pleasure, because her water descends from her chest to her womb, unlike the man. And where the appearance of semen from her is required in reality, the face of the apparent narration is that Umm Sulaym came to the Prophet and said: O Messenger of Allah, indeed Allah is not shy of the truth, is there ghusl upon a woman when she has a wet dream? He said: Yes, when she sees water. And likewise from Hawlah bint Hakim that she asked the Prophet about a woman who sees in her dream what a man sees, and he said: There is no ghusl upon her until she discharges, just as a man has no ghusl until he discharges. And the fruit of the difference in what precedes appears in the case where he holds his penis or ties it until his desire subsides, then releases it and semen descends: ghusl is obligatory upon him according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), not according to Abu Yusuf. And in the case where he ejaculates with desire and performs ghusl immediately and prays, then the rest of the semen exits: upon him is ghusl according to the two, not according to Abu Yusuf, and he does not repeat the prayer by consensus, because he performed ghusl for the first, and ghusl for the second is not obligatory except after its exit. And if it exits after he urinated and his penis became flaccid, or slept, or walked many steps, ghusl is not obligatory upon him by agreement, because that cuts the source of the semen that left its place with desire, so the second is exiting without desire. And if it exits after urination while his penis is erect, ghusl is obligatory. And the fatwa is on the saying of Abu Yusuf in the case of a guest who is shy of the household or fears that suspicion might fall in their hearts, by circumambulating their house, and on their saying (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) in other than the guest. And if he does not hasten to hold his penis until the semen descends, he becomes junub by agreement. So if he fears suspicion, he pretends to pray without recitation, intention, or takbir tahrimah, raising his hands, standing, and bowing like a praying person.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage details the conditions under which the emission of semen necessitates ghusl (ritual bath). It begins by stating the ruling: semen must reach the surface of the body, separate from its source (the backbone) with sexual desire, and occur without actual intercourse (e.g., wet dream, masturbation, etc.). The text emphasizes that desire at the moment of separation from the backbone is required, but continuity of desire until it exits the private part is not required according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf holds a stricter view requiring desire to persist until exit. The same ruling applies to women in the authoritative narration (zahir al-riwayah), supported by hadith: a woman must see water (semen) for ghusl. A minority opinion suggests women need ghusl with wet dream if they experience pleasure, since their semen originates from the chest to the womb. The difference of opinion (intra-Hanafi dispute) has practical consequences: if a man suppresses his desire by holding his penis and then releases it, resulting in emission, ghusl is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad but not Abu Yusuf. Similarly, if after initial ghusl and prayer, residual semen exits, a new ghusl is required only according to the majority; but prayer is not repeated by consensus. The fatwa (operative ruling) is given according to Abu Yusuf for a guest who fears social suspicion, but otherwise according to the majority for non-guests. Finally, if one becomes junub and fears suspicion, he may feign prayer to avoid embarrassment, without actual recitation or intention.

Key Terms
مني (maniy): Semen; the fluid that necessitates ghusl when it exits with desire from its source.
شهوة (shahwa): Sexual desire; a necessary condition for the emission of maniy to necessitate ghusl.
دفق (dafq): Gushing; the forceful emission of semen. The text states that if desire is present, it implies dafq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when is the condition of desire required for the emission of semen to necessitate ghusl?
A) At the moment of separation from the backbone
B) Until the semen exits the private part
C) Both at separation and throughout exit
D) Only if the person is awake

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ghusl from semen hinges on the presence of desire at the time of separation from the backbone, but the duration of that desire is subject to a well-known intra-madhhab difference with practical effects.

Conditions for Ghusl Due to Insertion
Defines tawari al-hashafah and related rulings including khuntha and istimna'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that obligate ghusl upon insertion and apply the ruling to cases involving hermaphrodites and cloth barriers.

Core Idea
Ghusl becomes obligatory upon disappearance of the glans into a passage, whether or not ejaculation occurs.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on when ghusl becomes obligatory due to sexual penetration. The key condition is the complete covering of the glans (hashafah) in the front or rear passage of a living human. We will examine the textual proof from hadith, clarify the metaphorical meaning of 'meeting of the two circumcised parts,' and address special cases such as the cloth barrier and the ambiguous hermaphrodite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its obligation
The act is sexual insertion; the ruling is that ghusl is obligatory (fard 'ayn) upon the disappearance of the glans into either the front or rear passage of a living human.
The obligation applies to both parties if they are legally responsible; adolescents are commanded for character building.
2
Locate the textual proof
The hadith: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl is obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' This is the primary dalil.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalalah).
3
Understand the Hanafi interpretation
The Hanafi school interprets 'meeting of the two circumcised parts' as metaphorical: due to anatomy, the circumcision sites do not literally meet; rather, the disappearance of the glans indicates alignment.
The text provides an anatomical explanation to refute literal reading.
4
Apply to special cases
Cases: insertion with a cloth barrier (ghusl if heat and pleasure felt), insertion into a young girl (ghusl obligatory on male), and insertion involving an ambiguous hermaphrodite (no ghusl without ejaculation due to uncertainty).
The precautionary view suggests ghusl in all cloth barrier cases.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is require ejaculation for ghusl (understanding the hadith to imply emission). Hanafis do not; the practical difference is that Hanafis obligate ghusl upon mere insertion.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on differing interpretations of the same hadith.
