(وَ) منها: (تَوَارِي (٣) حَشَفَةٍ)، وهي رأس ذكر آدمي حي، خرج بــه ذكــر البهائم، وذكر الميت، والمقطوع والمصنوع من جلد، أو غيره على صفة الذكر، والإصبع، وذكر الصبي الذي لا يشتهي بخلاف المراهق في بالغة، فإنه يوجب عليها الغسل، (و) تواري (قدرها)، أي: الحشفة (منْ مَقْطُوعِهَا)، إذا كان التواري ( في أحد سبيلي آدمي حي)، فيجب الغسل عليهما لو مكلفين، ويؤمر به المراهق تخلقاً، ولم نقيد بكونه مشته، لأنه لو أولج في صغيرة لا تشتهي، ولم يفضها لزمه الغسل، وإن لم ينزل في الصحيح، لأنها صارت ممن يُجامع، ولم نعبر بالتقاء الختانين، لأن الحاصل في الفرج، محاذاتهما لا التقاؤهما، لأن ختان الرجل موضع القطع، وهو فيما دون حزة الحشفة، وختان المرأة موضع قطع جلدة منها، كعرف الديك فوق الفرج، وذلك لأن مدخل الذكر هو مخرج المني والولد والحيض، وفوق مدخل الذكر مخرج البول كإحليل الرجل، وبينهما جلدة رقيقة يقطع منها في الختان فختان المرأة تحت مخرج البول، وتحت مخرج البول مدخل الذكر، فإذا غابت الحشفة في الفرج، فقد حاذى ختانه ختانها، ولكن يقال لموضع ختان المرأة: خفاض، فذكر الختانين بطريق التغليب ولو لف ذكره بخرقه، وأولج ولم ينزل، فالأصح أنه إن وجد حــرارة الفرج واللذة، وجب الغسل، وإلا فلا، والأحوط وجوب الغسل في الوجهين، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إِذَا الْتَقَى الْخِتَانَانِ وَغَابَتِ الْحَشَفَةُ، وَجَبَ الْغُسْلُ انْزَلَ أو لَمْ يُنْزِلَ . تنبيه: لو أولج، الواضح في فرج خنثى مشكل، أو أولج الخنثى المشكل ذكره في فـــرج، أو دبــر من مثله، أو غيره، لا يجب الغسل على أحد إلا بالإنزال لجواز أن يكون الخنثي الفاعل امرأة، وذكره كالإصبع، وأن يكون رجلاً ففرجـه زائـد، وهـو كـالجرح، فلا يجـب بـالإيلاج فيه الغسل بمجرده، كذا في ( البحر ) عن «السراج» . قلت: ويشكل عليه معاملة الخنثى بالأضر في أحواله، وعليه يلزمه الغسل، فليتأمل.
A branch: For one with excessive desire, who is unmarried, masturbation to calm desire, and he saves himself head to head, and he is not rewarded. Thus from Abu Hanifa. And among them: covering of the glans, which is the head of a living human's penis, excluding animal penis, dead person's, amputated, artificial, finger, and the penis of a boy who does not desire, unlike an adolescent with an adult woman, for it obligates ghusl upon her. And covering of its equivalent, i.e., the glans from an amputated one, when the covering is in one of the two passages of a living human. So ghusl is obligatory upon both if they are legally responsible, and the adolescent is commanded with it as a means of character building. And we did not restrict it to being desirous, because if he inserts into a young girl who does not desire and does not deflower her, ghusl is obligatory upon him, even if he does not ejaculate, according to the correct opinion, because she has become one who is engaged in intercourse. And we did not use the expression 'meeting of the two circumcised parts' because what occurs in the vagina is their alignment, not their meeting. Because the man's circumcision site is the cut area, which is below the corona of the glans, and the woman's circumcision site is the cut area of a piece of skin like a rooster's comb above the vagina. That is because the entry of the penis is the exit of semen, child, and menstruation, and above the entry of the penis is the exit of urine like the man's urethra, and between them is a thin skin that is cut in circumcision. So the woman's circumcision site is below the exit of urine, and below the exit of urine is the entry of the penis. So when the glans disappears into the vagina, his circumcision site aligns with hers, but the place of the woman's circumcision is called khifad. So mentioning the two circumcised parts is by way of predominance. And if he wraps his penis with a cloth and inserts and does not ejaculate, the most correct is that if he finds the vagina's heat and pleasure, ghusl is obligatory; otherwise not. And the precautionary view is obligation in both cases, because of his saying: 'When the two circumcised parts meet and the glans disappears, ghusl is obligatory, whether he ejaculates or not.' Caution: If a clear man inserts into the vagina of an ambiguous hermaphrodite, or an ambiguous hermaphrodite inserts his penis into a vagina or anus of someone like him or another, ghusl is not obligatory upon anyone except with ejaculation, because it is possible that the acting hermaphrodite is a woman and his penis is like a finger, or that he is a man and his vagina is extra and like a wound, so ghusl is not obligatory by mere insertion. Thus in al-Bahr from al-Siraj. I say: It is problematic because the hermaphrodite is treated in the stricter of his situations, and accordingly ghusl would be obligatory upon him, so let it be considered.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage covers two related topics: first, a ruling on masturbation (istimna') for an unmarried person with excessive desire—according to Abu Hanifa, it is permitted to calm desire, but he is not rewarded; second, the conditions for ghusl due to insertion (tawari al-hashafah). The text defines the glans (hashafah) as the head of a living human's penis, excluding animals, dead, amputated, artificial, finger, and the penis of a young boy who does not desire. Insertion into the front or rear passage of a living human necessitates ghusl upon both parties if they are legally responsible; adolescents are commanded for character building. The condition of desire is not required; even insertion into a young girl who does not desire obligates ghusl on the male. The text explains that the hadith 'when the two circumcised parts meet' is metaphorical—actual alignment of circumcision sites does not occur because of anatomical positions; rather, it refers to the glans disappearing. If insertion is done with a cloth barrier, ghusl is obligatory if heat and pleasure are experienced; precaution suggests ghusl in all cases. Finally, a cautionary note on hermaphrodites (khuntha): if a clear man inserts into an ambiguous hermaphrodite's vagina, or vice versa, ghusl is not obligatory without ejaculation, because the hermaphrodite's status is unclear—the penis might be like a finger (if female) or the vagina like a wound (if male). However, the commentator notes a conflict with the principle of treating the hermaphrodite in the stricter of his/her situations, which would require ghusl.

Key Terms
حشفة (hashafah): The glans or head of the penis; its disappearance (tawari) into the passage necessitates ghusl.
ختان (khitan): Circumcision; the text explains that the term 'meeting of the two circumcised parts' is figurative, referring to alignment of the circumcision sites.
خنثى (khuntha): Hermaphrodite; a person with both male and female reproductive organs. The ruling on ghusl is suspended due to uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum condition for ghusl to become obligatory from sexual intercourse?
A) Ejaculation
B) Covering of the glans in the front or rear passage
C) Both ejaculation and glans covering
D) Desire and ejaculation

Key Takeaway
The disappearance of the glans in the passage, not ejaculation, is the sole condition for ghusl obligation from insertion in the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Ghusl Due to Insertion of the Glans
Defines the condition for ghusl upon insertion of the glans

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for obligatory ghusl upon insertion and apply it to cases including the ambiguous hermaphrodite.

Core Idea
Concealment of the glans into a living human's passage triggers obligatory ghusl, regardless of ejaculation.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the precise trigger for obligatory ghusl (ghusl) in the Hanafi school. While many assume ejaculation is necessary, the school holds that mere concealment of the glans (hashafah) into a living human's front or back passage suffices. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, exceptions, and the contested element with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what legal status (hukm) it carries. Here, the act is insertion (ilaj) causing concealment of the glans, and the ruling is that ghusl becomes wajib (obligatory).
Note that the ruling applies regardless of ejaculation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the textual evidence cited by the author. The hadith: 'When the two circumcisions meet and the glans is concealed, ghusl becomes obligatory.' This is a sunnah ahad (solitary narration) but accepted in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is reported by Abu Hanifa in his Musnad and others.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil proves the ruling. The imperative phrase 'ghusl becomes obligatory' indicates obligation. The phrase 'glans is concealed' identifies the effective cause (illa) for the ruling.
The Hanafi school considers concealment itself, not ejaculation, as the trigger.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify where other schools differ. The Shafi'i school requires the meeting of the two circumcision points, not merely concealment. The Hanafi school explains that actual meeting is impossible; what occurs is alignment, so concealment is the operative condition.
This difference leads to practical variations in rulings.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. The Hanafi position (concealment suffices) is authoritative from Zahir al-Riwayah and affirmed by later scholars like al-Marghinani.
The special case of the khuntha mushkil (ambiguous hermaphrodite) illustrates the limits of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وَ) منها: (تَوَارِي حَشَفَةٍ)، وهي رأس ذكر آدمي حي، خرج بــه ذكــر البهائم، وذكر الميت، والمقطوع والمصنوع من جلد، أو غيره على صفة الذكر، والإصبع، وذكر الصبي الذي لا يشتهي بخلاف المراهق في بالغة، فإنه يوجب عليها الغسل، (و) تواري (قدرها)، أي: الحشفة (منْ مَقْطُوعِهَا)، إذا كان التواري ( في أحد سبيلي آدمي حي)، فيجب الغسل عليهما لو مكلفين، ويؤمر به المراهق تخلقاً، ولم نقيد بكونه مشته، لأنه لو أولج في صغيرة لا تشتهي، ولم يفضها لزمه الغسل، وإن لم ينزل في الصحيح، لأنها صارت ممن يُجامع، ولم نعبر بالتقاء الختانين، لأن الحاصل في الفرج، محاذاتهما لا التقاؤهما، لأن ختان الرجل موضع القطع، وهو فيما دون حزة الحشفة، وختان المرأة موضع قطع جلدة منها، كعرف الديك فوق الفرج، وذلك لأن مدخل الذكر هو مخرج المني والولد والحيض، وفوق مدخل الذكر مخرج البول كإحليل الرجل، وبينهما جلدة رقيقة يقطع منها في الختان فختان المرأة تحت مخرج البول، وتحت مخرج البول مدخل الذكر، فإذا غابت الحشفة في الفرج، فقد حاذى ختانه ختانها، ولكن يقال لموضع ختان المرأة: خفاض، فذكر الختانين بطريق التغليب ولو لف ذكره بخرقه، وأولج ولم ينزل، فالأصح أنه إن وجد حــرارة الفرج واللذة، وجب الغسل، وإلا فلا، والأحوط وجوب الغسل في الوجهين، لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « إِذَا الْتَقَى الْخِتَانَانِ وَغَابَتِ الْحَشَفَةُ، وَجَبَ الْغُسْلُ انْزَلَ أو لَمْ يُنْزِلَ . تنبيه: لو أولج، الواضح في فرج خنثى مشكل، أو أولج الخنثى المشكل ذكره في فـــرج، أو دبــر من مثله، أو غيره، لا يجب الغسل على أحد إلا بالإنزال لجواز أن يكون الخنثي الفاعل امرأة، وذكره كالإصبع، وأن يكون رجلاً ففرجـه زائـد، وهـو كـالجرح، فلا يجـب بـالإيلاج فيه الغسل بمجرده، كذا في ( البحر ) عن «السراج» . قلت: ويشكل عليه معاملة الخنثى بالأضر في أحواله، وعليه يلزمه الغسل، فليتأمل. (٢) أي: تغييب. ط. (٣) أي: أدخل ذكره في فرج الأنثى معجم لغة الفقهاء / إيلاج / بتصرف. (٤) أخرجه أبو حنيفة في مسنده (١٦١/١)، والطبراني في الأوسط (۳۸۰/٤) ، وابن ماجه في الطهارة، باب ما جاء في وجوب الغسل إذا التقى الختانان (٦١١) بنحوه.
And concealment of the glans, and its equivalent from the amputated part, into one of the two passages of a living human. (And) among them: concealment of the glans, which is the head of the penis of a living human, excluding the penis of animals, the dead, the amputated, the artificial of skin or other resembling a penis, the finger, and the penis of a boy who does not arouse desire, contrary to a boy nearing puberty in a mature woman, for it necessitates ghusl upon her. (And) concealment of its equivalent, i.e., the glans from the amputated one, when the concealment is in one of the two passages of a living human, then ghusl is obligatory upon both if they are obligated, and the boy nearing puberty is commanded to do it as a discipline. We did not restrict it to the one who desires, because if he inserts into a young girl who does not desire and does not deflower her, ghusl is incumbent upon him, even if he did not ejaculate according to the correct view, because she has become one who is copulated with. We did not express it as meeting of the two circumcisions, because what occurs in the vagina is their alignment, not their meeting, for the man's circumcision is the place of cutting below the corona of the glans, and the woman's circumcision is the place of cutting a piece of skin like a rooster's comb above the vagina. That is because the male organ's entry is the exit of semen, child, and menses; above the male organ's entry is the exit of urine like the male urethra, and between them is a thin skin from which is cut in circumcision; so the woman's circumcision is below the urine exit, and below the urine exit is the male organ's entry. When the glans disappears in the vagina, his circumcision aligns with hers, but the place of the woman's circumcision is called khifad, so mentioning the two circumcisions is by way of predominance. If he wrapped his penis with a cloth and inserted and did not ejaculate, the most correct is that if he finds the heat of the vagina and pleasure, ghusl is obligatory, otherwise not, and precaution is that ghusl is obligatory in both cases, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'When the two circumcisions meet and the glans is concealed, ghusl becomes obligatory, whether he ejaculated or not.' Note: If an unambiguous man inserts into the vagina of an ambiguous hermaphrodite, or the ambiguous hermaphrodite inserts his penis into the vagina or anus of one like him or another, ghusl is not obligatory on anyone except with ejaculation, because it is possible that the active hermaphrodite is a woman and his penis is like a finger, or that he is a man and her vagina is extra like a wound, so ghusl is not obligatory by mere insertion into it, as in al-Bahr from al-Siraj. I say: This is problematic with treating the hermaphrodite in the worst of his states, and upon him ghusl is necessary, so reflect. (2) i.e., concealment. (3) i.e., he inserted his penis into the female's vagina. (4) Reported by Abu Hanifa in his Musnad, al-Tabarani in al-Awsat, and Ibn Majah in Tahara, chapter on the obligation of ghusl when the two circumcisions meet.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the ruling on ghusl due to insertion. The author states that ghusl becomes obligatory when the glans (hashafah) or its equivalent in an amputated man disappears into one of the two passages (front or back) of a living human. He clarifies exceptions: the penis of an animal, a dead person, a prosthetic, a finger, and a boy who does not arouse desire are excluded. For a boy nearing puberty who inserts into a mature woman, ghusl is obligatory on her. The condition is based on concealment of the glans, not the meeting of circumcisions, because circumcision points in men and women do not actually meet; they only align. If the glans is covered with a cloth and inserted without ejaculation, the ruling depends on perceiving heat and pleasure, but precautionary ghusl is recommended. The author cites the hadith: 'When the two circumcisions meet and the glans is concealed, ghusl is obligatory.' A special case involves an ambiguous hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil): insertion by or into such a person does not necessitate ghusl without ejaculation due to uncertainty of gender. The author notes a potential inconsistency with the principle of treating the hermaphrodite in the worst state, so caution is advised.

Key Terms
حَشَفَة (hashafah): The glans or head of the male organ; the locus for obligation of ghusl.
إِيلاج (ilaj): Insertion of the male organ into a female's vagina or anus.
خُنْثَى مُشْكِل (khuntha mushkil): A hermaphrodite whose gender is ambiguous; special rulings apply to avoid ghusl without ejaculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because concealment occurred.
B) No, because the passage is not of a living human.
C) Yes, if he ejaculates.
D) No, unless he feels pleasure.

Key Takeaway
Concealment of the glans into a living human's passage is the sole condition for obligatory ghusl, regardless of ejaculation.

Masturbation for a Bachelor: Hanafi Ruling
States the ruling on masturbation to calm desire for a bachelor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on masturbation for a bachelor with excessive desire and identify the condition that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Masturbation is permissible for a bachelor only to avoid greater sin, but it carries no reward.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on masturbation (istimna') for a bachelor ('azab) who fears falling into zina or liwat. According to a narration from Abu Hanifa, masturbation is permitted as a lesser harm to avoid a greater sin. However, it is not rewarded; it is merely a concession to preserve chastity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person and Situation
The ruling specifically applies to a bachelor ('azab) with excessive desire (farṭ shahwa). The condition is the fear of committing a major sin like fornication or sodomy.
If the person is married or has a lawful outlet, the ruling may differ.
2
State the Ruling
According to Abu Hanifa, masturbation is permissible (mubah) in this specific context. It is a dispensation to avoid greater evil.
It is not recommended (mandub) nor obligatory.
3
Identify the Condition for Permissibility
The permissibility is conditional on the fear of falling into a major sin. The text says 'fear of falling into sodomy or fornication'.
Without such fear, masturbation would be haram.
4
Note the Consequence
The person 'escapes head to head' (yanjū ra'san bi ra's), meaning he barely avoids sin, and he is not rewarded (lā yakūnu ma'jūran).
This underscores that it is not an act of worship but a necessary concession.
5
Recognize the Legal Principle
The commentator explicitly applies the principle of 'choosing the lesser of two harms' (irtikāb akhaff al-ḍararayn).
This principle is used in cases of necessity (ḍarūra).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرع لمن به فرط شهوة، وهو عَزَب الاستمناء لتسكين الشهوة ) ، وينجو رأساً برأس، ولا يكون مأجوراً. كذا عن أبي حنيفة. (١) أي: خشية الوقوع في لواط أو زنا فيكون هذا من ارتكاب أخف الضررين ط.
Branch: For one who has excessive desire, and he is a bachelor, masturbation to calm the desire, and he escapes head to head (i.e., just barely avoids sin), and he is not rewarded. Thus from Abu Hanifa. (1) i.e., fear of falling into sodomy or fornication, so this is from committing the lesser of two harms.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This is a subsidiary ruling (far') concerning a person with overwhelming sexual desire who is unmarried. According to Abu Hanifa, masturbation is permitted as a means to avoid greater sin (zina or liwat), but it carries no reward; it is simply a necessary evil to escape sin. The commentator clarifies that it falls under the principle of choosing the lesser of two harms.

Key Terms
استمناء (istimna'): Masturbation; self-stimulation to release sexual tension.
عَزَب ('azab): A bachelor; unmarried person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on masturbation for a bachelor with excessive desire?
A) It is forbidden
B) It is permissible but not rewarded
C) It is recommended
D) It is obligatory

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, masturbation for a bachelor fearing sin is permissible as a lesser harm, but it carries no reward.

Ejaculation from Intercourse with a Dead Body or Animal: Condition for Ghusl
Clarifies a condition for ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for ghusl to become obligatory after intercourse with a dead body or an animal, and explain the rationale based on deficient desire.

Core Idea
Ejaculation, not mere insertion, triggers ghusl after intercourse with a corpse or animal due to deficient desire.

In this passage, the author clarifies a specific ruling from the chapter of ghusl. Unlike intercourse with a living human, where concealment of the glans alone necessitates ghusl regardless of ejaculation, the case of intercourse with a dead body or an animal is treated differently. The obligation arises only upon emission of semen, because the act itself is not considered fully stimulating of sexual desire. This distinction reflects the Hanafi attention to the effective cause (illa) underlying the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed and what legal obligation results. Here, the act is sexual intercourse (wat') with a dead human body or an animal. The ruling is that ghusl becomes wajib (obligatory) only if ejaculation (inzal) occurs.
Ghusl itself is fard in Hanafi law; this passage specifies when its obligation arises in this particular scenario.
2
Distinguish the general rule for living humans
Recall the general rule: for intercourse with a living human, mere insertion of the glans (iltiqa al-khatanayn) necessitates ghusl, regardless of ejaculation. This is based on the hadith 'If the circumcised parts meet, ghusl is wajib.'
This general rule applies when both partners are alive and human.
3
Apply the exceptional condition for dead bodies and animals
In contrast, for a dead body or an animal, the condition of inzal is added. The text states: 'شرط إنزال المني' – the condition is emission of semen. Without it, ghusl is not required.
This exception is not universal; some other schools may differ, but here we follow the Hanafi position.
4
Understand the rationale (illa)
The reason given is 'لقصور الشهوة' (due to deficiency of desire). Intercourse with a corpse or animal is not considered a fully stimulating act that generates the same level of sexual desire as with a living human. Therefore, only actual emission indicates that janabah (major impurity) has occurred.
This rationale is a form of talil (legal reasoning) based on the nature of the act.
5
Confirm the scope of the ruling
The passage includes both 'ميتة' (dead body of a human) and 'بهيمة' (animal). The same condition applies to both. Note that bestiality is haram, but the discussion here is about the consequent taharah (purification).
The ruling is limited to these two objects; for a living human, the general rule applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنزالُ المَنِي بِوَطْءِ مَيْتَةٍ أو بهيمة. (و) منها: (انْزَالُ المَنِي بِوَطءِ مَيْتَةِ، أو بَهِيمَةٍ، شرط إنزال المني، لأن مجرد وطئهما لا يوجب الغسل، لقصور الشهوة.
And ejaculation of semen from intercourse with a dead body or an animal. (And) among them: ejaculation of semen from intercourse with a dead body or an animal, the condition is the emission of semen, because mere intercourse with them does not necessitate ghusl due to deficiency of desire.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
The author lists another cause for ghusl: ejaculation resulting from sexual intercourse with a dead human body or an animal. He emphasizes that the mere act of insertion with a corpse or animal does not obligate ghusl because these acts do not stimulate full sexual desire; only the emission of semen triggers the obligation. This differentiates it from intercourse with a living human, where concealment of the glans alone suffices.

Key Terms
إنزال (inzal): Emission of semen, specifically in the context of sexual intercourse.
وطء (wat'): Sexual intercourse; insertion of the male organ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for ghusl to be obligatory after intercourse with a dead body or an animal?
A) Mere insertion
B) Ejaculation of semen
C) Both insertion and heat
D) It is never obligatory

Key Takeaway
Ejaculation is the essential condition for ghusl after intercourse with a dead body or animal, due to the deficiency of sexual desire in such acts.

Ghusl for Finding Thin Fluid After Sleep: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghusl for post-sleep moisture

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on finding thin fluid after sleep without wet dream, identify the conditions that affect the ruling, and evaluate the disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Finding thin fluid after sleep without wet dream requires ghusl unless the penis was erect before sleep.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person wakes up and finds a thin fluid but does not recall a wet dream, does ghusl become obligatory? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule yes, citing a hadith and precaution, while Abu Yusuf analogizes from wakefulness to claim it is only madhi. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh textual evidence against analogy in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Imams' positions
State the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say ghusl is wajib; Abu Yusuf says it is madhi and no ghusl.
Abu Yusuf's view is also supported by later Hanafis like Khalaf ibn Ayyub and Abu al-Layth.
2
Locate the dalil for the majority view
Find the hadith narrated by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi from Aisha where the Prophet commands ghusl for a man who finds moisture without remembering a wet dream.
The command 'yaghtasilu' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's counter-argument
Understand his qiyas: if such fluid appears when awake, it is madhi; sleep does not change its nature, so it is still madhi and does not require ghusl.
He considers the thinness of the fluid as evidence of madhi.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The response: sleep is a time when semen can thin due to air or diet, so the fluid may be semen; precaution in worship demands ghusl, and the hadith directly overrules analogy.
The principle of ihtiyat (precaution) is invoked.
5
Note the condition and special case
If the penis was erect before sleep, the fluid is attributed to madhi, so no ghusl. Also, if a couple finds moisture between them without distinguishing features, both must perform ghusl as a precaution.
This shows the ruling has exceptions and edge cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجود ماء رقيق بعد النوم، إذا لم يكن ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم. (و) منها: (وُجُودُ مَاءٍ رَقِيقِ بَعْدَ ) الانتباه من (النوم) ولم يتذكر احتلاماً، عندهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف هو يقول: إنه مذي، وأنه لا يوجب الغسـل حــال اليقظة، فبالأولى عدمه في المنام، وبه أخذ خلف بن أيوب وأبو الليث، لكونه أقيس، ولهما ما روى أبو داود والترمذي عن عائشة قالت: سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عنِ الرَّجلِ يَجدُ البَلل ولا يذكرُ احْتِلاماً قال: يَغْتَسِلُ . ولأن النوم مظنة الاحتلام، لأنه راحة فيهيج الشهوة، فيحال عليه، ثم يحتمل أنـه كـان منيـاً، فـرق بواسطة الهواء أو الغذاء، والاحتياط لازم في باب العبادات. وهذا ( إذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ ذَكَرُهُ مُنْتَشِراً قَبْلَ النَّوْمِ)؛ لأن الانتشار قبل النوم سبب لخروج المذي، فيحال عليه، ولو وجد الزوجان، بينهما ماء دون تذكر ومميز بأن لم يظهر غلظه، ولا رقته، ولا بياضه ولا صفرته، ولا طوله، ولا عرضه، يجب عليهما الغسل، في الصحيح احتياطاً. (١) المذي: ماء رقيق يضرب إلى البياض، يخرج من الرجل عند الملاعبة مع أهله، وأما ما يخرج من المرأة فيسمى القذي. فتح باب العناية (۷۸/۱). (٢) أخرجه أبو داود في الطهارة، باب: في الرجل يجد البلـة في منامه (٢٣٦)، والترمذي في الطهارة، باب: فيـمـن يستيقظ فيري بللاً ولم يذكر احتلاماً (۱۱۳).
And finding thin water after sleep, if his penis was not erect before sleep. (And) among them: finding thin water after waking from sleep and he does not remember a wet dream, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf who says it is madhi and does not necessitate ghusl when awake, so even more so in sleep, and Khalaf ibn Ayyub and Abu al-Layth adopted this because it is more analogical. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is what Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi narrated from Aisha: the Messenger of Allah was asked about a man who finds moisture and does not remember a wet dream; he said: he should perform ghusl. And because sleep is a place for wet dreams, for it is rest that arouses desire, so it is attributed to it. Then it is possible that it was semen that thinned due to air or food, and precaution is necessary in the chapter of worship. This is when his penis was not erect before sleep, because erection before sleep is a cause for madhi to exit, so it is attributed to it. If a couple finds between them water without remembering and distinguishable by not appearing thick or thin, white or yellow, long or wide, ghusl is obligatory on both in the correct view as a precaution.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage addresses the case of a person who wakes up and finds a thin fluid (ma' raqiq) but does not recall a wet dream. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), this requires ghusl because it might be semen that thinned. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding it is madhi (prostatic fluid) which does not require ghusl. The two base their position on a hadith from Aisha where the Prophet commanded ghusl in such a case. They also argue that sleep is a likely occasion for wet dreams, so the moisture is attributed to semen unless there is reason to think otherwise. However, if the penis was erect before sleep, the fluid is more likely madhi, so ghusl is not required. A precautionary ruling: if a couple finds moisture between them without distinguishing features, both must perform ghusl.

Key Terms
الماء الرقيق (al-ma' al-raqiq): Thin fluid; here it refers to fluid that could be semen or madhi.
مذي (madhi): Prostatic fluid that exits during arousal; does not require ghusl.
احتلام (ihtilam): Wet dream; nocturnal emission of semen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ghusl is obligatory only if the fluid is thick
B) Ghusl is obligatory unless the penis was erect before sleep
C) Ghusl is never required
D) Only wudu is required

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, finding thin fluid after sleep without wet dream and without prior erection necessitates ghusl; precaution and direct hadith outweigh analogy.

Ghusl for Moisture After Intoxication or Unconsciousness
States a cause that obligates ghusl as a precaution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when moisture suspected to be semen is found after intoxication or unconsciousness and explain the precautionary basis.

Core Idea
Moisture after intoxication/fainting triggers obligatory ghusl, even without memory, as a precaution.

In matters of purity, the Hanafi school sometimes requires actions as a precaution (ihtiyatan) to ensure worship is valid. This lesson covers one such case: if a person finds moisture they suspect is semen after regaining consciousness from intoxication or fainting, ghusl becomes wajib. This ensures that any undetected janabah is cleared, even if the person has no recollection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is finding moisture (balal) suspected to be semen (zann annahu maniyyan) after recovery (ifaqah) from intoxication (sukr) or unconsciousness (ighma'). The ruling is that ghusl is obligatory.
The ruling is based on precaution, not certainty.
2
Locate the condition
The condition is that the moisture must be thought (zann) to be semen. Mere existence of moisture is not enough; there must be a reasonable suspicion.
If the moisture is clearly something else (e.g., madhy, sweat), ghusl is not obligatory.
3
Understand the legal basis
The basis is ihtiyat (precaution) in worship. Since during intoxication or fainting a person may have had a wet dream without memory, the law requires ghusl to ensure purity.
This is a distinctive Hanafi application of the precautionary principle.
4
Apply the ruling
If the scenario matches (moisture found, suspicion of semen, after intoxication/fainting), perform ghusl. If not, no ghusl is required beyond normal hygiene.
The ruling remains irrespective of whether the person remembers a dream.

Source Text

(وَ) منها: (وُجُودُ بَلَلٍ، ظَنَّهُ مَنِيَا، بَعْدَ إِفَاقَتِهِ مِنْ سُكْرٍ، وَ) بعد إفاقته من (إغماء)، احتياطاً.
(And) among them: finding moisture that he thinks is semen, after his recovery from intoxication, and after his recovery from unconsciousness, as a precaution.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
The author includes another cause: if a person finds moisture after regaining consciousness from intoxication or fainting, and they suspect it is semen, ghusl is obligatory as a precaution (ihtiyatan). This is because during these states, they may have had a wet dream or emission without memory. The precautionary principle in acts of worship demands ghusl.

Key Terms
بلل (balal): Moisture; here it refers to any wetness that could be semen.
سكر (sukr): Intoxication; a state of drunkenness.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness; fainting.

When Ghusl Becomes Wajib: Menstruation and Postpartum Bleeding
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of obligation.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib upon cessation of menstruation/postpartum bleeding, but the cause is the blood itself, not the purity.

This passage from Nur al-Idah discusses when ghusl becomes obligatory for a woman after menstruation or postpartum bleeding. While all Hanafis agree that ghusl must be performed before resuming acts like prayer, there is a subtle intra-madhhab disagreement on the exact moment of obligation: is it when the blood exits or when it stops? Understanding this distinction sharpens your grasp of how causes (asbab) and conditions (shurut) operate in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is ghusl after menstruation (hayd) or postpartum bleeding (nifas). The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory).
This is the starting point: ghusl is required.
2
Locate the two intra-Hanafi opinions
The passage presents two views among Hanafis. The scholars of Bukhara hold that ghusl becomes wajib only at the cessation of bleeding. The Iraqi scholars (including al-Karkhi) hold that the blood itself is the cause of impurity, but one delays ghusl until cessation because performing it earlier would be futile due to continuous flow.
Both agree that ghusl is performed after cessation, but differ on the cause.
3
Analyze the talil (legal reasoning)
The author critiques the Bukhara view: cessation is a state of purity, and it is impossible for purity to obligate another purity. Rather, the impure excretion (blood) must be the obligator. The Iraqi view is thus more sound: the blood is the cause, but cessation is a condition for the effectiveness of ghusl.
The argument is based on the principle that an impurity itself triggers purification, not its absence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that ghusl becomes wajib upon cessation of bleeding. The blood is the cause (sabab), and cessation is the condition (shart) for the obligation to take effect. This is the adopted position in later Hanafi fatwa.
In practice, a woman must perform ghusl when bleeding stops, not when it starts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) منها: أنه يفترض الغسل (بِحَيْض، ونفاس)، أي بخروج دم حيض، أو نفاس إلى فرجها الخارج. وقيل: لا يصح أن يُؤولا بخروج الدم، لأنه لا يجب بخروجه الغسل، وإنما يجب عند انقطاعه وهو اختيار مشايخ « بخارى». وفيه نظر، إذ الانقطاع طهارة، ويستحيل أن توجب الطهارة طهارة، وإنما يوجبها الخارج النجس، وهو اختيار « الكرخي»، وعامة العراقيين. وإنما لا يغتسل قبل الانقطاع لعدم الفائدة باستمرار الدم لا لأنه لا يرفع الحدث المتقدم. وحاصله: أن الحيض، أو النفاس موجب بشرط الانقطاع، والتحقيق أنه سبب للاتصاف بالحدث، وانقطاعه شرط لتبقى طهارة الاغتسال وسبب وجوبه إرادة أو وجوب ما لا يحل معه، كما تقدم.
(And) among them: that ghusl is obligatory due to menstruation and postpartum bleeding, i.e., due to the exit of menstrual blood or birth blood to her external vulva. And it was said: it is not correct to interpret it as the exit of blood, because ghusl is not obligatory upon exit, but rather at its cessation, and this is the choice of the scholars of Bukhara. There is consideration in this, for cessation is purity, and it is impossible that purity obligates purity; rather, the impure excretion obligates it, and this is the choice of al-Karkhi and most Iraqis. The reason one does not perform ghusl before cessation is the lack of benefit due to continuous blood, not that it does not remove the previous impurity. The summary: that menstruation or postpartum bleeding is a cause with the condition of cessation; the investigation is that it is a reason for being described as junub, and cessation is a condition for the purity of ghusl to remain, and its obligation is due to the intention or obligation of what is not permissible with it, as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage discusses whether ghusl is required upon the start or the end of menstruation/postpartum bleeding. The author states two opinions. The first, from scholars of Bukhara, holds that ghusl becomes obligatory only when the bleeding stops. The second, from al-Karkhi and most Iraqis, says the obligation is due to the blood itself, but one delays ghusl until cessation because performing it earlier would be futile due to continuous bleeding. The author favors the latter: the blood is the cause of ritual impurity, and ghusl removes that impurity, but it is effective only after bleeding has ceased. Therefore, ghusl is required when the blood ends, but the underlying cause is the blood itself.

Key Terms
حيض (hayd): Menstrual bleeding; one of the causes of ghusl.
نفاس (nifas): Postpartum bleeding; similar ruling to menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, when does a woman become obligated to perform ghusl after menstruation?
A) Immediately when the blood starts
B) When the blood completely stops
C) After a fixed number of days
D) Only if she intends to pray

Key Takeaway
Ghusl from menstruation and postpartum bleeding is wajib upon complete cessation, as the blood is the cause and cessation is the condition for effective purification.

Ghusl Obligatory for Pre-Islamic Causes
States ruling on ghusl for pre-Islamic causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that pre-Islamic causes of ghusl still obligate ghusl after conversion, and explain the persistence of janaba.

Core Idea
Ghusl remains obligatory even if the cause occurred before Islam; conversion does not remove janaba.

A new Muslim may wonder if they need to perform ghusl for events that happened before embracing Islam. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the state of major ritual impurity (janaba) persists after conversion, and ghusl is still required before any act of worship that demands purity. The ruling is based on the continuity of the impurity, not on the person's previous religious status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is ghusl (ritual bath). The text states that it is 'farada' (obligatory) for all its mentioned causes. In Hanafi fiqh, ghusl for janaba is fard (obligatory).
The text uses the verb 'يفترض' indicating a fard ruling.
2
Note the condition: pre-Islam occurrence
The ruling applies even if the cause (e.g., intercourse, nocturnal emission) occurred before the person embraced Islam. This is the specific point of the passage.
The phrase 'ولو حصلت الأشياء المذكورة قبل الإسلام' emphasizes the scope.
3
Understand the reasoning: persistence of janaba
The cause of ghusl creates a state of janaba that remains until ghusl is performed. Conversion to Islam does not automatically remove this impurity. The text says 'لبقاء صفة الجنابة' (due to the persistence of the quality of janaba).
The impurity is a physical state, not a spiritual one.
4
Note the operative opinion
The text qualifies the ruling as 'في الأصح' (the most correct opinion). This indicates that while there might be other views, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that ghusl is required.
Some early scholars may have considered the act waived, but the madhhab rejects that.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفترض الاغتسال في جميع موجباته، ولو حَصَلَتِ الأشياءُ المَذْكُورَةُ قَبْلَ الإسلام، في الأصح)؛ لبقاء صفة الجنابة ونحوها بعد الإسلام، ولا يمكن أداء المشروط بزوال الجنابة.
(And) ghusl is obligatory in all its causes, even if the mentioned things occurred before Islam, according to the most correct opinion, because the quality of janaba and similar remains after Islam, and the conditioned act cannot be performed by the removal of janaba.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion of ghusl by stating that if any of the previously mentioned causes (insertion, ejaculation from intercourse with dead/animal, fluid after sleep, etc.) occurred before a person embraced Islam, they are still obliged to perform ghusl after becoming Muslim. This is because the state of ritual impurity (janaba) persists after conversion and must be removed to perform acts of worship that require purity. Performing ghusl does not remove the impurity of disbelief; rather, it removes janaba.

Key Terms
جنابة (janaba): Major ritual impurity that requires ghusl to remove.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No ghusl is needed because conversion erases all
B) Ghusl is still obligatory
C) Only wudu is needed
D) It depends on the cause

Key Takeaway
Pre-Islamic janaba obligates ghusl after conversion because the state of impurity persists and must be removed for worship.

Ghusl Obligation from Intercourse with Dead Woman or Animal
States ruling and condition for ghusl from intercourse with a corpse or animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ghusl is obligatory only if semen is emitted during intercourse with a corpse or animal, and explain the reason (qusur al-shahwah).

Core Idea
For intercourse with a corpse or animal, ghusl requires emission of semen due to weak desire.

In the rules of ghusl, we learned that sexual intercourse with a living partner obligates ghusl regardless of emission. But what if the partner is a dead woman or an animal? This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies that the Hanafi school conditions ghusl on actual emission in these cases, because the act itself does not generate full sexual excitement. Understanding this nuance helps you apply the rules of ritual purity precisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is intercourse (wat') with a dead woman (mayyitah) or an animal (bahimah). State that the general ruling is that ghusl becomes obligatory, but only under a specific condition.
This is not a blanket obligation like with a living partner.
2
Locate the condition (shart)
The text explicitly says 'shart inzal al-mani' – the condition is the emission of semen. Without emission, no ghusl is required.
The word 'shart' indicates a necessary condition for the ruling to apply.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The reason given is 'qusur al-shahwah' – weak sexual desire. Because intercourse with a corpse or animal does not typically produce full arousal, the mere act does not trigger the same obligation as with a living being. Emission is therefore treated as the decisive factor.
This shows the Hanafi method of looking at the cause ('illa) behind a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) منها: (انْزَالُ المَنِي بِوَطءِ مَيْتَةِ، أو بَهِيمَةٍ، شرط إنزال المني، لأن مجرد وطئهما لا يوجب الغسل، لقصور الشهوة.
And among them: emission of semen by intercourse with a dead woman or an animal, with the condition of emission of semen because mere intercourse with them does not necessitate ghusl due to weak desire.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement within the commentary on the causes of ghusl. The author explains that for ghusl to become obligatory from intercourse with a dead woman or an animal, actual emission of semen is a condition. This is because the act itself, without emission, does not generate the full sexual excitement (shahwa) that would otherwise trigger the obligation. The ruling is straightforward and agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ميتة (mayyitah): A dead human female body, specifically a woman's corpse.
بهيمة (bahīmah): Any animal, including both edible and inedible types.
قصور الشهوة (qusūr al-shahwah): Weakness or deficiency of sexual desire, which means the act does not typically lead to full arousal and emission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the specific condition for ghusl to become obligatory from intercourse with a dead woman or an animal?
A) The act of intercourse itself
B) Actual emission of semen
C) The presence of sexual desire
D) The woman or animal being alive

Key Takeaway
For intercourse with a corpse or animal, ghusl is only obligatory if semen is emitted, because the act alone does not produce full sexual excitement.
